Prophethood
beginner
4 min
Prophets are not divine
Al-Bajuri excludes divine attributes from prophets, refuting Christian deification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributes of divinity cannot be applied to prophets, and how this refutes Christian deification of Jesus.

Core Idea
Prophets are not gods; divinity belongs only to Allah.

Al-Bajuri begins by clarifying that the restriction 'what is from the accidents' in the creedal text excludes divine attributes from prophets. This is because accidents are properties of created beings, not the Creator. This serves as a direct refutation of Christian claims about Jesus, and establishes a foundational principle: no prophet can be described with divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Al-Bajuri defines the restriction and immediately applies it to exclude divinity.
2
Understand the exclusion of divine attributes
The passage states that divine attributes are excluded because accidents are specific to contingent beings (الحوادث). This logical reason is key.
Accidents are attributes of created things, not the Creator.
3
Reflect on the refutation of Christians
Al-Bajuri explicitly mentions those who made Jesus a god. Think about how this principle invalidates Christian doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ خرج بهذا القيد: صِفَاتُ الألوهية، فلا تجوز عليهم، خلافاً لمن أضلَّهم الله تعالى في جعلهم سيدنا عيسى إلها، وإنما خَرَجَتْ صفاتُ الألوهية بهذا القيد؛ لأن الأعراض خاصة بصفات الحوادث.
:(قوله: الْبَشَرِيَّةِ) أي: المتعلّقة بالبشر، وهم بنو آدم سموا بذلك؛ لبُدُو بشرتهم، وهي ظاهرُ الجلد. وخرج بهذا القيد الأعراض المتعلقة بالملائكة، فلا تجوز عليهم، خلافاً لجَهَلَة العرب في زعمهم: أن الرسول يكون متّصفاً بصفات الملائكة، فلا يأكل ولا يشربُ، وتوصلوا بذلك إلى نفي رسالته كما حكاه الله تعالى عنهم في قوله: وَقَالُواْ مَالِ هَذَا الرَّسُولِ يَأْكُلُ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشِي فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ الآية (٢).

تقريرات العلامة محمد الأتبابي.
(قوله: وَخَرَجَ بِهَذَا الْقَيْدِ الْأَعْرَاضُ الْمُتَعَلِقَةُ بِالْمَلَائِكَةِ، فَلَا تَجُوزُ عَلَيْهِمْ) فوجوبُ عدم الأكل الثابت للملائكة لا يجوز في الأنبياء.
His saying: 'what is from the accidents' – by this restriction are excluded the attributes of divinity, so they are not permissible for them, contrary to those whom Allah has led astray in making our master Jesus a god. The attributes of divinity are excluded by this restriction only because accidents are specific to the attributes of contingent beings.
His saying: 'of humanity' means related to humans, who are the children of Adam, so named because of the apparentness of their skin, which is the outer layer. By this restriction, the accidents related to angels are excluded, so they are not permissible for them, contrary to the ignorant Arabs in their claim that the messenger must be described with the attributes of angels, so he does not eat nor drink, and they used that to deny his message, as Allah the Exalted related about them in His saying: 'And they said, What is this messenger who eats food and walks in the markets?' verse (2).
Annotations of al-Allama Muhammad al-Attababi: His saying: 'And by this restriction the accidents related to angels are excluded, so they are not permissible for them' – so the obligation of not eating established for angels is not permissible for prophets.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the attributes that are and are not permissible for prophets. Al-Bajuri explains the restriction 'what is from the accidents' (مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ) which appears in the original text. This restriction excludes the attributes of divinity (صفات الألوهية) because accidents are specifically attributes of contingent created beings, not the Creator. Thus, no prophet can be described with divine attributes, contrary to Christians who deify Jesus. Then, the further restriction 'of humanity' (الْبَشَرِيَّةِ) excludes accidents related to angels. Prophets are human, so they can have human accidents, but not angelic ones. This refutes the ignorant Arabs who demanded that a prophet must be like an angel—neither eating nor drinking—and used this to reject Muhammad's prophethood. Al-Quran 25:7 is cited as evidence. The marginal note by al-Attababi reinforces that the obligation of not eating is established for angels, but it is not permissible to require it of prophets, because prophets are human and must have human attributes.

Key Terms
الألوهية
الأعراض
الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jesus is divine and should be worshipped as God.
Correction: Prophets are not divine; divine attributes are exclusive to Allah. Accidents are properties of created beings, not the Creator.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Bajuri, why are divine attributes excluded from prophets?
A) Because prophets are human.
B) Because accidents are specific to the attributes of contingent beings.
C) Because the Quran says so.
D) Because prophets are sinless.

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes cannot apply to prophets because accidents belong only to created beings, not the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even for a moment, felt that a righteous person—perhaps a scholar, a spiritual guide, or a prophet—deserves a level of reverence that belongs only to Allah? How does this passage's logical reasoning expose the danger of such subtle exaltation? What concrete steps will you take to ensure your heart attributes divinity exclusively to Allah?
?
The Christian claim about Jesus is a clear error, but what about attributing hidden knowledge or absolute power to any human? Do you catch yourself relying on someone—other than Allah—as if they have ultimate control or knowledge? How does understanding that accidents belong only to created beings reshape your reliance?
?
If accidents are specific to contingent beings, and you are a contingent being, what does that mean for your own limitations? How does this truth affect your daily life, your fears, and your hopes? Will you consciously remind yourself that only Allah is self-sufficient, and that your existence depends entirely on Him?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
Prophets are human, not angels
Al-Bajuri excludes angelic attributes from prophets, refuting Arab pagans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must have human attributes and cannot be like angels, refuting the Arab pagans' demand that a prophet must be angelic.

Core Idea
Prophets are fully human; angelic attributes do not apply to them.

After excluding divinity, Al-Bajuri further restricts the accidents to those specifically related to humanity, thereby excluding angelic attributes. This addresses the misguided Arab pagans who argued that a true messenger must not eat or drink—like angels—and used this to reject Prophet Muhammad. Al-Bajuri affirms that prophets are human and must have human traits, citing Quran 25:7 as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Focus on the definition of 'humanity' and the exclusion of angelic accidents.
2
Understand exclusion of angelic traits
The passage says that accidents related to angels are not permissible for prophets. The reason is implied: prophets are human, not angelic.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Quran 25:7 is quoted as a refutation of the Arab pagans who denied prophethood because Muhammad ate and walked in markets. Notice how this verse affirms his humanity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ خرج بهذا القيد: صِفَاتُ الألوهية، فلا تجوز عليهم، خلافاً لمن أضلَّهم الله تعالى في جعلهم سيدنا عيسى إلها، وإنما خَرَجَتْ صفاتُ الألوهية بهذا القيد؛ لأن الأعراض خاصة بصفات الحوادث.
:(قوله: الْبَشَرِيَّةِ) أي: المتعلّقة بالبشر، وهم بنو آدم سموا بذلك؛ لبُدُو بشرتهم، وهي ظاهرُ الجلد. وخرج بهذا القيد الأعراض المتعلقة بالملائكة، فلا تجوز عليهم، خلافاً لجَهَلَة العرب في زعمهم: أن الرسول يكون متّصفاً بصفات الملائكة، فلا يأكل ولا يشربُ، وتوصلوا بذلك إلى نفي رسالته كما حكاه الله تعالى عنهم في قوله: وَقَالُواْ مَالِ هَذَا الرَّسُولِ يَأْكُلُ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشِي فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ الآية (٢).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets must be free from human needs like eating and drinking, and if they eat, they cannot be true prophets.
Correction: Prophets are human and therefore have human attributes. Eating and drinking do not diminish prophethood; rather, they affirm the prophet's humanity.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Bajuri, why are angelic accidents excluded from prophets?
A) Because prophets are sinless.
B) Because the restriction 'of humanity' specifies accidents related to humans, not angels.
C) Because angels are superior to prophets.
D) Because the Quran commands it.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are human, not angels; they have human attributes like eating and drinking, and this is necessary for their role.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself wishing that the Prophet ﷺ had been more 'angelic'—that he had never felt hunger, tiredness, or ordinary human struggles? How does that desire reflect a misunderstanding of his role and your own duty to follow him as a complete human being?
?
The ignorant Arabs rejected the Prophet because he ate and walked in markets. How does your own heart react when you see a scholar or religious leader engaging in everyday human activities? Are you tempted to dismiss them as less spiritual? What does that reveal about your concept of prophetic perfection?
?
If the Prophet ﷺ had been an angel, would his example still be accessible to you in your daily life? How does knowing that he shared your human needs—like eating and walking—change the way you relate to his Sunnah? Will you now seek to follow him in those mundane acts with more intention and love?

Prophethood
beginner

The Condition for Permissible Human Accidents in Prophets
Al-Bajuri defines the qualifying condition and lists examples of impermissible accidents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition that distinguishes permissible from impermissible human accidents in prophets, and be able to list examples of what is impermissible.

Core Idea
Any accident that diminishes a prophet's dignity or undermines his mission is impermissible.

Prophets are human beings subject to certain human experiences, but not all human accidents are permissible for them. Al-Bajuri begins by explaining the key condition: an accident must not lead to any diminishment of their lofty rank or contradict the wisdom of their mission. This lesson examines that condition and the examples of what is excluded.

Guided Path
1
Read the condition definition
Read the opening phrase 'the ones that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks' and understand its meaning. Note that this condition is the key filter.
The condition is explicitly stated in the first sentence.
2
Identify the categories of impermissible accidents
Find the list of what is excluded: actions that compromise dignity, anything repelling, and anything undermining the mission. Note the specific examples given.
Examples include eating on the road, lowly profession, lack of intellect, etc.
3
Understand why these are impermissible
Reflect on how each example could diminish the prophet's rank or harm acceptance of their message. This connects the condition to practical instances.
The condition is applied to concrete situations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ) أي: منازلهم المرتفعة. وخرج بهذا القيد: الأعراضُ البشريَّةُ التي تؤدّي إلى نَقْصٍ في مراتبهم، كالأمور المُخِلَّةِ بالمروءة، وعدمِ السلامة عن كلّ ما يُنفِرُ ، وكلّ ما يُخِلَّ بحكمةِ بعثتهم، وهي أداء الشرائع، وقبول الأمم لهم. ودخل في ذلك الأكل على الطريق، والحِرْفَةُ الدنيئة، وعدم كمال العقل والذكاء والفطنة وقوَّة الرأي، ودناءة الآباء، وعُهْرُ الأمهات والغِلْظَةُ والفَطَاظَة، والعيوبُ المنفِّرَةُ كَالْبَرَصِ وَالْجُذَامِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ.

:(قوله: كَالْمَرَضِ) ومنه الإغماء، فهو جائز عليهم، بخلاف الجنون والشكر والخَبَل ونحو ذلك كما علم مما مر.
:(قوله: وَنَحْوِهِ) أي: كالأكل والشرب والنوم، لكن بأعينهم لا بقلوبهم؛ لما ورد انَحْنُ - مَعَاشِرَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ - تَنَامُ أَعْيُنُنَا وَلَا تَنَامُ قُلُوبُنَا» ()، وكخروج المني الناشئ من امتلاء الأوعية مثلاً، لا من الاحتلام الناشئ من الشيطان؛ لأنه لا تَسَلَّطَ للشيطان عليهم، وكالجوع كما وَقَعَ له ، ففي "الشَّفَا" وغيره: أنه كان يَبِيتُ يتلوَّى من الجوع، ولا ينافي ذلك قوله : أَبِيتُ عِنْدَ رَبِّي يُطْعِمُنِي وَيَسْقِينِي؛ لأنه كان يَحْضُلُ له ذلك تارةً، ولا يحصل له تارةً أخرى لأجل التأسي به ، والعِنْدَيَّةُ في الحديث المذكور ،مجازية، والمعنى: أنه كان يبيتُ وقلبه متعلّق بربه، وملاحظ لجلاله وعظمته، أو أنه كان يبيتُ في كنف الله وحفظه، ومعنى قوله: (يطعمني ويسقيني): يعطيني قُوَّةَ الطاعم والشارب، أو يطعمني ويسقيني من طعام الجنة وشرابها.
His saying: 'that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks' means their high stations. By this restriction are excluded the human accidents that lead to deficiency in their ranks, such as matters that compromise dignity, lack of safety from anything that repels, and everything that undermines the wisdom of their mission, which is the delivery of laws and the acceptance of nations for them. Included in that are eating on the road, a lowly profession, lack of perfection of intellect, intelligence, sagacity, strength of opinion, lowliness of fathers, unchastity of mothers, harshness, roughness, and repelling defects like leprosy, elephantiasis, and the like.
His saying: 'like sickness' – includes fainting, so it is permissible for them, unlike insanity, intoxication, imbecility, and the like, as is known from what has passed.
His saying: 'and the like' means like eating, drinking, and sleep, but with their eyes, not their hearts, because it is reported: 'We, the company of prophets, our eyes sleep but our hearts do not sleep.' And like the emission of semen arising from the filling of vessels, for example, not from a nocturnal emission arising from Satan, because Satan has no power over them. And like hunger as occurred to him. In al-Shifa and others: he used to spend the night writhing from hunger. And that does not contradict his saying: 'I spend the night at my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink,' because that would happen to him at times and not happen at other times for the sake of causing the community to follow him. And the 'at-ness' in the mentioned hadith is metaphorical. The meaning is that he used to spend the night with his heart attached to his Lord, observing His majesty and greatness, or that he used to spend the night in the care of Allah and His protection. And the meaning of his saying 'He feeds me and gives me drink' is: He gives me the strength of the eater and drinker, or He feeds me and gives me drink from the food and drink of Paradise.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of human accidents permissible for prophets. It begins by defining the condition 'that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks' (الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ). This means that any human accident that would diminish the prophet's high station or contradict the wisdom of their mission is impermissible. Examples of impermissible defects include: eating on the road (an unseemly act), a lowly profession, lack of intellect or intelligence, lowly parents, immoral mothers, harshness, and repelling diseases like leprosy and elephantiasis. These are excluded because they would undermine the acceptance of their message.
Then the passage explains permissible accidents. Sickness, including fainting, is permissible, as these do not inherently diminish rank. However, insanity, intoxication, and imbecility are not permissible. The condition 'and the like' (وَنَحْوِهِ) includes eating, drinking, and sleep, but with the qualification that prophets' hearts remain awake while their eyes sleep, based on a hadith. Also, the emission of semen is permissible if natural, but not from a nocturnal dream induced by Satan, as Satan has no power over prophets. Hunger is permissible, and the Prophet experienced it. The passage reconciles the hadith 'I spend the night at my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink' with his physical hunger, offering two interpretations: either it happened at times but not others for the sake of the community, or the 'at-ness' is metaphorical, meaning spiritual sustenance or protection.

Key Terms
مروءة
نقص
مراتب
الأعراض البشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all human needs are impermissible for prophets because of their high status.
Correction: The passage shows that only accidents that lead to deficiency in their ranks are prohibited; many human experiences are permissible.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is considered impermissible for a prophet?
A) Fainting due to sickness.
B) Eating on the road.
C) Sleeping with the eyes.
D) Experiencing hunger.

Key Takeaway
The condition for permissible human accidents in prophets is that they must not diminish their lofty rank or undermine the wisdom of their mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know now that prophets are shielded from anything that compromises their dignity. Look at your own life: what habits, words, or attitudes might subtly erode the respect others have for the deen you represent? What will you change today to restore that dignity?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was protected from repelling qualities. Consider your own interactions: do you carry any harshness, roughness, or indifference that turns people away from the truth? Who is one person you have unintentionally pushed away, and what is one concrete step you can take to soften your approach this week?
?
The lesson teaches that even lawful but lowly matters can be impermissible for prophets due to their rank. Reflect on your own sense of honor for Islam: are you content with a mediocre, mundane religious life that fails to reflect the loftiness of this faith? If your life is marked by spiritual laziness, what is the one worldly indulgence you know you must abandon to rise to a higher rank with Allah?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Examples of Permissible Human Accidents in Prophets
Al-Bajuri enumerates permissible accidents and explains the hadith about spiritual sustenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which human accidents are permissible for prophets despite their lofty status, including sickness, eating, drinking, sleep, and hunger, and how to reconcile physical weakness with spiritual sustenance.

Core Idea
Prophets experience normal human needs but remain spiritually vigilant.

After explaining the condition that excludes certain accidents, Al-Bajuri now lists those that are permissible, such as sickness, eating, drinking, and sleep, and clarifies that these do not affect the prophet's dignity. He also addresses a hadith about the Prophet being fed by his Lord to reconcile it with physical hunger.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of permissible accidents
Read the passage starting from 'like sickness' and note the examples: sickness, fainting, eating, drinking, sleep, semen emission, and hunger.
These are all natural human experiences.
2
Identify the exceptions
Notice that some conditions are explicitly excluded: insanity, intoxication, imbecility, and nocturnal emission caused by Satan. Understand why these are impermissible.
These involve loss of intellect or association with evil.
3
Understand the hadith about sleep
The passage quotes a hadith that prophets' eyes sleep but their hearts do not. This shows that sleep is permissible because their spiritual awareness remains intact.
The condition is that the heart stays awake.
4
Learn the reconciliation for hunger
The Prophet experienced hunger, though he also said 'I spend the night at my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink.' The passage explains that this feeding is metaphorical or occasional, not contradicting physical hunger.
This resolves an apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ) أي: منازلهم المرتفعة. وخرج بهذا القيد: الأعراضُ البشريَّةُ التي تؤدّي إلى نَقْصٍ في مراتبهم، كالأمور المُخِلَّةِ بالمروءة، وعدمِ السلامة عن كلّ ما يُنفِرُ ، وكلّ ما يُخِلَّ بحكمةِ بعثتهم، وهي أداء الشرائع، وقبول الأمم لهم. ودخل في ذلك الأكل على الطريق، والحِرْفَةُ الدنيئة، وعدم كمال العقل والذكاء والفطنة وقوَّة الرأي، ودناءة الآباء، وعُهْرُ الأمهات والغِلْظَةُ والفَطَاظَة، والعيوبُ المنفِّرَةُ كَالْبَرَصِ وَالْجُذَامِ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ.

:(قوله: كَالْمَرَضِ) ومنه الإغماء، فهو جائز عليهم، بخلاف الجنون والشكر والخَبَل ونحو ذلك كما علم مما مر.
:(قوله: وَنَحْوِهِ) أي: كالأكل والشرب والنوم، لكن بأعينهم لا بقلوبهم؛ لما ورد انَحْنُ - مَعَاشِرَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ - تَنَامُ أَعْيُنُنَا وَلَا تَنَامُ قُلُوبُنَا» ()، وكخروج المني الناشئ من امتلاء الأوعية مثلاً، لا من الاحتلام الناشئ من الشيطان؛ لأنه لا تَسَلَّطَ للشيطان عليهم، وكالجوع كما وَقَعَ له ، ففي "الشَّفَا" وغيره: أنه كان يَبِيتُ يتلوَّى من الجوع، ولا ينافي ذلك قوله : أَبِيتُ عِنْدَ رَبِّي يُطْعِمُنِي وَيَسْقِينِي؛ لأنه كان يَحْضُلُ له ذلك تارةً، ولا يحصل له تارةً أخرى لأجل التأسي به ، والعِنْدَيَّةُ في الحديث المذكور ،مجازية، والمعنى: أنه كان يبيتُ وقلبه متعلّق بربه، وملاحظ لجلاله وعظمته، أو أنه كان يبيتُ في كنف الله وحفظه، ومعنى قوله: (يطعمني ويسقيني): يعطيني قُوَّةَ الطاعم والشارب، أو يطعمني ويسقيني من طعام الجنة وشرابها.
His saying: 'that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks' means their high stations. By this restriction are excluded the human accidents that lead to deficiency in their ranks, such as matters that compromise dignity, lack of safety from anything that repels, and everything that undermines the wisdom of their mission, which is the delivery of laws and the acceptance of nations for them. Included in that are eating on the road, a lowly profession, lack of perfection of intellect, intelligence, sagacity, strength of opinion, lowliness of fathers, unchastity of mothers, harshness, roughness, and repelling defects like leprosy, elephantiasis, and the like.
His saying: 'like sickness' – includes fainting, so it is permissible for them, unlike insanity, intoxication, imbecility, and the like, as is known from what has passed.
His saying: 'and the like' means like eating, drinking, and sleep, but with their eyes, not their hearts, because it is reported: 'We, the company of prophets, our eyes sleep but our hearts do not sleep.' And like the emission of semen arising from the filling of vessels, for example, not from a nocturnal emission arising from Satan, because Satan has no power over them. And like hunger as occurred to him. In al-Shifa and others: he used to spend the night writhing from hunger. And that does not contradict his saying: 'I spend the night at my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink,' because that would happen to him at times and not happen at other times for the sake of causing the community to follow him. And the 'at-ness' in the mentioned hadith is metaphorical. The meaning is that he used to spend the night with his heart attached to his Lord, observing His majesty and greatness, or that he used to spend the night in the care of Allah and His protection. And the meaning of his saying 'He feeds me and gives me drink' is: He gives me the strength of the eater and drinker, or He feeds me and gives me drink from the food and drink of Paradise.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of human accidents permissible for prophets. It begins by defining the condition 'that do not lead to deficiency in their lofty ranks' (الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ). This means that any human accident that would diminish the prophet's high station or contradict the wisdom of their mission is impermissible. Examples of impermissible defects include: eating on the road (an unseemly act), a lowly profession, lack of intellect or intelligence, lowly parents, immoral mothers, harshness, and repelling diseases like leprosy and elephantiasis. These are excluded because they would undermine the acceptance of their message.
Then the passage explains permissible accidents. Sickness, including fainting, is permissible, as these do not inherently diminish rank. However, insanity, intoxication, and imbecility are not permissible. The condition 'and the like' (وَنَحْوِهِ) includes eating, drinking, and sleep, but with the qualification that prophets' hearts remain awake while their eyes sleep, based on a hadith. Also, the emission of semen is permissible if natural, but not from a nocturnal dream induced by Satan, as Satan has no power over prophets. Hunger is permissible, and the Prophet experienced it. The passage reconciles the hadith 'I spend the night at my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink' with his physical hunger, offering two interpretations: either it happened at times but not others for the sake of the community, or the 'at-ness' is metaphorical, meaning spiritual sustenance or protection.

Key Terms
مرض
إغماء
جنون
شكر
خبل
مني
احتلام
شيطان
جوع
شفا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that prophets never experience physical hunger or weakness because of their special status.
Correction: The passage shows that hunger and other natural needs are permissible and occurred to the Prophet, and are reconciled with divine sustenance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT permissible for a prophet?
A) Fainting due to sickness.
B) Eating and drinking.
C) Nocturnal emission from Satan.
D) Hunger.

Key Takeaway
Permissible human accidents for prophets include natural needs like sickness, eating, sleeping, and hunger, provided they do not impair spiritual awareness or dignity; apparent contradictions with divine care are resolved through interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your physical needs—eating, sleeping, sickness—are shared with the prophets, but their hearts never slept in their awareness of Allah. When you eat or sleep, is your heart awake to your Lord, or are you spiritually absent? What would it take for you to maintain that awareness even in your most human moments?
?
The Prophet endured hunger for the sake of his community to teach reliance on Allah. When you face discomfort or lack, do you turn toward Allah in trust, or do you let your circumstances pull you away from Him? Are you willing to experience hardship for the sake of following him?
?
If your body's needs sometimes dominate your thoughts, remember that the Prophet's 'feeding' from his Lord was spiritual. Are you feeding your soul as much as you feed your body? What change can you make today to prioritize spiritual nourishment over physical comfort?

Proof of the Obligation of Prophetic Truthfulness
Al-Bajuri presents a logical conditional proof for prophetic truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof (burhan) that establishes the necessity of prophets being truthful in their claim to prophethood and in conveying God's message.

Core Idea
If prophets could lie, God would be lying—but God cannot lie.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary presents a crisp logical argument that the prophets must be truthful. The proof is a conditional syllogism: if the prophets were not truthful, then God would be lying—which is impossible. Therefore, their truthfulness is necessary. Al-Bajuri first clarifies the scope of this truthfulness, then lays out the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice the concise style of the proof.
The passage has two parts: a clarification of scope and the proof formulation.
2
Identify the conditional statement
Find the 'if... then...' structure: 'If they were not truthful, lying would necessarily occur in His report.' This is the premise that drives the argument.
The proof assumes that God's report is implicated by the prophets' testimony.
3
Understand the impossibility
The proof states that lying in God's report is impossible (muhal). Why? Because God is necessarily truthful. This is a foundational axiom in kalam.
The impossibility of God lying is accepted by the opponent, so the proof is sound.
4
Follow the conclusion
If the consequence (God lying) is impossible, then the antecedent (prophets not truthful) is also impossible. Therefore, their truthfulness is necessary.
This is a classic modus tollens argument.
5
Reflect on the scope
Note that the proof only covers truthfulness in the claim of prophethood and in conveying revelation—not every word prophets say.
Al-Bajuri explicitly limits the scope as 'as has passed.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ أي: في دعوى الرسالة وفيما بلغوه عن الله تعالى؛ لأن هذا البرهان إنما يدل على ذلك كما مر.
(وقوله: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ... إلخ) تقريره أن تقول: لو لم يَضدُقوا للزم الكذب في خبره تعالى، لكنّ الكذب في خبره تعالى محال فما أدى إليه ـ وهو عدم صدقهم - محال أيضاً، وإذا استحالَ عَدَمُ صدقهم ثَبَتَ صدقهم، وهو المطلوب.
His saying: 'As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness' means in the claim of prophethood and in what they conveyed from Allah the Exalted, because this proof only indicates that, as has passed.
His saying: 'For they... etc.' Its formulation is that you say: If they were not truthful, lying would necessarily occur in His report the Exalted. But lying in His report the Exalted is impossible, so what leads to it — which is their lack of truthfulness — is also impossible. And when their lack of truthfulness is impossible, their truthfulness is established, and that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage presents a logical proof (burhan) for the obligatory truthfulness of prophets. The proof is framed as a conditional syllogism. The claim is that prophets must be truthful in both their claim to prophethood and in what they convey from God. The reasoning: if prophets were not truthful (i.e., if they lied), then God would be lying in His report (because God is the one who sent them and affirmed their truthfulness through miracles). But it is impossible for God to lie. Therefore, the antecedent (prophets not being truthful) is also impossible. Hence, their truthfulness is necessarily established. This is a classic kalam argument that relies on God's veracity.

Key Terms
برهان
صدق
كذب
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof is circular because it assumes God cannot lie, which is what the opponent may deny.
Correction: The proof does not assume God cannot lie; it relies on a rationally necessary truth accepted in kalam: lying is an imperfection, and God is perfect. The opponent in this context agrees that lying in God's report is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what would happen if prophets were not truthful?
A) They would lose their prophethood.
B) God would be lying in His report.
C) The miracles would cease.
D) The people would not be obligated to follow them.

Key Takeaway
The truthfulness of prophets is logically necessary because its negation would imply the impossibility of God lying.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does your trust in the prophets' truthfulness affect your daily obedience to Islamic teachings? Are there any commands you hesitate to follow because you doubt the messenger's sincerity? What would change if you truly internalized that lying is impossible for prophets?
?
If you were to claim that a prophet could lie, you would be attributing imperfection to God. Where in your own life do you indirectly attribute imperfection to God by doubting His messengers? Repent and commit to affirming His perfection.
?
The proof shows that prophetic truthfulness is logically necessary. Have you ever treated prophethood as merely historical, rather than as a living reality that demands your unconditional trust? Write one action you will take today to demonstrate that trust.

Attributes That Do Not Lower Prophets' Ranks
Al-Bajuri explains which human attributes are excluded from prophets as not lowering their high ranks.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which human attributes are permissible for prophets and why they are not considered deficiencies.

Core Idea
Prophets are immune only from attributes that would lower their rank or repel people.

Al-Bajuri clarifies a key nuance in prophetic immunity: not all human attributes are excluded from prophets, only those that would diminish their lofty station or undermine their mission. This passage defines the boundary and provides concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice how al-Bajuri first interprets the phrase 'which do not lead to a deficiency' and then lists examples.
The passage is definitional with examples.
2
Identify the restriction and its purpose
Focus on the phrase 'by this restriction are excluded'. Understand that the purpose is to protect the wisdom of prophecy: delivering laws and gaining acceptance.
3
Study the examples and their rationale
Each example—like eating on the road or having a lowly profession—is excluded because it would cause a deficiency. Ask yourself how each one might undermine a prophet's authority.
Repulsive defects (leprosy, elephantiasis) are explicitly mentioned as they repel people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: الَّتِي لَا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ) أي: منازلهم المرتفعة. وخرج بهذا القيد: الأعراضُ البشريَّةُ التي تؤدّي إلى نَقْصٍ في مراتبهم، كالأمور المُخِلَّةِ بالمروءة، وعدمِ السلامة عن كلّ ما يُنفِرُ ، وكلّ ما يُخِلَّ بحكمةِ بعثتهم، وهي أداء الشرائع، وقبول الأمم لهم. ودخل في ذلك الأكل على الطريق، والحِرْفَةُ الدنيئة، وعدم كمال العقل والذكاء والفطنة وقوَّة الرأي، ودناءة الآباء، وعُهْرُ الأمهات والغِلْظَةُ والفَطَاظَة، والعيوبُ المنفِّرَةُ كالبَرَصِ والجُذَامِ ونحو ذلك.
His statement: 'which do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks' meaning: their elevated stations. By this restriction are excluded human attributes that lead to a deficiency in their ranks, such as matters violating decency, lack of safety from everything that repels, and everything that undermines the wisdom of their mission, which is the delivery of laws and acceptance of nations for them. Included in that are eating on the road, a lowly profession, lack of perfection of intellect, intelligence, acumen, and strength of opinion, baseness of fathers, fornication of mothers, harshness and roughness, and repulsive defects like leprosy, elephantiasis, and the like.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage defines and exemplifies the phrase 'which do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks' from the original text. It is a definition-and-exclusion passage. The commentator first interprets the phrase as referring to the prophets' elevated stations. Then he explains that this restriction excludes human attributes that would cause a deficiency in their ranks. He lists categories: matters violating decency (muru'a), anything that repels people, and anything that undermines the wisdom of sending prophets, which is to deliver divine laws and to be accepted by their communities. Then he gives specific examples: eating on the road, practicing a lowly craft, lacking full intellect, intelligence, acumen, and strong judgment, having ignoble fathers, mothers being fornicators, harshness, roughness, and repulsive diseases like leprosy and elephantiasis. The point is that prophets are immune from such deficiencies because they would compromise their authority and the effectiveness of their mission.

Key Terms

الأعراض البشرية
المروءة
حكمة بعثتهم
العيوب المنفرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, what is the purpose of the restriction 'which do not lead to a deficiency in their ranks'?
A) To exclude all human attributes from prophets.
B) To exclude only those human attributes that would cause a deficiency in the prophets' ranks or undermine their mission.
C) To allow prophets to have any human attribute without restriction.
D) To exclude only physical defects like leprosy.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from any human attribute that would compromise their dignity or the effectiveness of their mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that prophets are protected from attributes that lower their rank or repel people. Look at your own character: are there any habits or traits you have that might repel others from the message of Islam? What specific step will you take today to remove such an attribute from your life?
?
The scholars listed eating on the road as a lowly act unbecoming of a prophet. Consider your daily actions: do you conduct yourself in a way that befits someone who carries the legacy of prophethood? Name one instance where you acted against decency (muru'a) and commit to correcting it.
?
Prophets are protected from defective intellect and weak judgment. How careful are you in seeking knowledge and using your intellect to serve the truth? What one change can you make to strengthen your intellectual commitment to Islam?

Permissible and Impermissible Conditions for Prophets
Al-Bajuri clarifies that illness and fainting are permissible for prophets, unlike madness and drunkenness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which physical and mental conditions are permissible for prophets and which are not, and the reasoning behind the distinction.

Core Idea
Prophets can experience illness and fainting, but not madness or drunkenness.

In this passage, al-Bajuri clarifies a subtle point about the human attributes of prophets. While prophets share many human experiences, not all conditions are considered compatible with their status. This lesson examines the line between permissible physical afflictions and those that imply a loss of intellectual control, which is incompatible with prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its translation. Notice the concise style: al-Bajuri builds on a prior phrase.
The passage is a single sentence but contains a clear classification.
2
Identify the two categories
Pick out which conditions are said to be permissible (ja'iz) and which are not (bikhilaf). Make a mental or written list.
3
Understand the key distinction
Reflect on why illness and fainting are allowed but madness, drunkenness, and mental derangement are not. Think about what distinguishes them.
The commentary will help clarify the underlying principle.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this classification fits into the larger discussion of prophetic attributes. Why is it important to define these limits?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: كَالْمَرَضِ) ومنه الإغماء، فهو جائز عليهم، بخلاف الجنون والشكر والخَبَل ونحو ذلك كما علم مما مر.
His statement: 'like illness' – and among it is fainting, which is permissible for them, unlike madness, drunkenness, mental derangement, and the like, as was known from what has passed.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This short passage classifies what is permissible and impermissible for prophets regarding physical conditions. It is a classification passage within the broader discussion of prophets' human attributes. The commentator explains that the phrase 'like illness' includes fainting, and both illness and fainting are permissible (ja'iz) for prophets. However, madness (junun), drunkenness (sukr), and mental derangement (khabal) are not permissible, as has been established earlier. The key distinction is that illness and fainting do not detract from the prophets' perfection in a way that undermines their mission, whereas madness and loss of intellectual control do.

Key Terms

الإغماء
الجنون
السكر
الخبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot experience any illness or fainting.
Correction: This passage shows that illness and fainting are permissible for prophets; only conditions that impair intellect like madness and drunkenness are not.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is permissible for prophets according to this passage?
A) Madness
B) Drunkenness
C) Fainting
D) Mental derangement

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of a condition for prophets depends on whether it impairs their intellectual integrity; illness does not, but madness and drunkenness do.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) experienced illness and fainting, but never madness or intoxication. In your own life, what habits or mental states do you tolerate that you would be ashamed to see him experience? Are you willing to eliminate them starting today?
?
If physical illness is permissible for prophets and does not diminish their station, what does it mean for you when you face illness? Do you use it as an excuse to neglect your spiritual duties, or do you see it as a test that the prophets themselves endured?
?
The passage distinguishes between conditions that impair the intellect and those that do not. Which of your daily activities—whether entertainment, sleep, worry, or indulgence—takes you closer to the impermissible side of that line? What will you do about it this week?

Prophets' Human Needs: Eating, Sleeping, and Hunger
Al-Bajuri explains 'and the like' covering eating, sleeping, seminal emission, and hunger with hadith interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how prophets experience human needs like eating, sleeping, and hunger without compromising their spiritual status or prophetic rank.

Core Idea
Prophets are fully human yet divinely protected: their needs are real but their hearts remain with Allah.

Al-Bajuri unpacks the phrase 'and the like' from the original text, explaining how prophets partake in human necessities while preserving their unique rank. He clarifies that their eating, sleeping, and even hunger are not like ours, and he resolves a potential contradiction with a well-known hadith. This passage helps us appreciate the delicate balance between the humanity and prophethood of Allah's messengers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Bajuri explains each example of human needs.
The passage has three main examples: eating/drinking/sleeping, seminal emission, and hunger.
2
Identify the qualifications for each need
For each need, al-Bajuri gives a specific condition or exception. For sleeping, he cites the hadith about eyes sleeping but hearts awake. For seminal emission, he distinguishes natural causes from satanic ones. For hunger, he interprets another hadith to reconcile it with the Prophet's experience.
These qualifications protect the prophets from any imperfection.
3
Understand the metaphorical interpretation
Al-Bajuri explains that the 'withness' in the hadith 'I spend the night with my Lord' is metaphorical, meaning the Prophet's heart was attached to Allah, not a literal physical presence. Also, 'feeding' can mean spiritual strength or provision from Paradise.
This resolves the apparent contradiction between the Prophet's hunger and the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَنَحْوِهِ) أي: كالأكل والشرب والنوم، لكن بأعينهم لا بقلوبهم؛ لما ورد «نحن مَعَاشِرَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ تَنَامُ أَعْيُنُنَا وَلَا تَنَامُ قُلُوبُنَا» ، وكخروج المني الناشئ من امتلاء الأوعية مثلاً، لا من الاحتلام الناشئ من الشيطان؛ لأنه لا تَسَلَّطَ للشيطان عليهم، وكالجوع كما وَقَعَ له ، ففي "الشَّفَا" وغيره: أنه كان يَبِيتُ يتلوَّى من الجوع، ولا ينافي ذلك قوله : «أَبِيتُ عِنْدَ رَبِّي يُطْعِمُنِي وَيَسْقِينِي»؛ لأنه كان يحصل له ذلك تارةً، ولا يحصل له تارةً أخرى لأجل التأسي به، والعِنْدَيَّةُ في الحديث المذكور مجازية، والمعنى: أنه كان يبيتُ وقلبه متعلّق بربه، وملاحظ لجلاله وعظمته، أو أنه كان يبيتُ في كنف الله وحفظه، ومعنى قوله: (يطعمني ويسقيني): يعطيني قُوَّةَ الطاعم والشارب، أو يطعمني ويسقيني من طعام الجنة وشرابها.
His statement: 'and the like' – meaning: like eating, drinking, and sleeping, but with their eyes, not with their hearts, because it is reported: 'We, the company of prophets, our eyes sleep but our hearts do not sleep'; and like the emission of semen arising from the filling of vessels, for example, not from a wet dream arising from Satan, because there is no authority for Satan over them; and like hunger as occurred to him, for in 'al-Shifa' and others: he would spend the night writhing from hunger, and that does not contradict his statement: 'I spend the night with my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink,' because that would happen to him sometimes, and not happen at other times for the sake of his followers' emulation, and the 'withness' in the mentioned hadith is metaphorical, and the meaning is: he would spend the night with his heart attached to his Lord, observing His majesty and greatness, or he would spend the night in the care of God and His protection; and the meaning of his statement: 'He feeds me and gives me drink' is: He gives me the strength of the eater and drinker, or He feeds me and gives me drink from the food and drink of Paradise.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase 'and the like' from the original text, focusing on prophets' human attributes that do not lower their rank. It is an explanatory passage with multiple subpoints. First, it clarifies that eating, drinking, and sleeping are permissible for prophets, but with a qualification: their eyes sleep, but their hearts do not, citing the hadith. Second, it discusses seminal emission, distinguishing between natural emission from physical fullness (which is permissible) and wet dreams caused by Satan (which are impossible because Satan has no authority over prophets). Third, it addresses hunger, giving the example of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) experiencing severe hunger. It then reconciles this with the hadith 'I spend the night with my Lord, He feeds me and gives me drink' by interpreting the latter metaphorically: sometimes he experienced physical hunger, and at other times he was spiritually sustained. The 'withness' is metaphorical, meaning his heart was with his Lord, not literal physical presence. The feeding and drinking are interpreted as spiritual strength or provision from Paradise.

Key Terms
الأكل
الشرب
النوم
المني
الجوع
العندية المجازية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets never feel hunger or have physical needs because of their high rank.
Correction: This passage shows that prophets do experience hunger and other human needs, but these experiences are controlled and free from any imperfection. The Prophet's hunger was real, but it did not contradict his spiritual connection with Allah.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri, why can prophets not experience wet dreams originating from Satan?
A) Because prophets are always asleep.
B) Because Satan has no authority over prophets.
C) Because prophets are not human.
D) Because wet dreams are impure.

Key Takeaway
Prophets experience human needs but are safeguarded from any imperfection, and apparent contradictions are resolved through proper interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel hunger or discomfort, does your heart remain attached to Allah like the Prophet's, or does it become irritable and forgetful? The next time you are hungry, pause and ask yourself: am I using this physical need to draw closer to my Lord, or am I letting it distract me? Commit to turning one moment of hunger today into a dhikr or du'a.
?
Your eyes sleep but your heart may be heedless. The Prophet's heart never slept—are you satisfied with the state of your heart when you wake up? What would it take for your last thought before sleep and your first thought upon waking to be of Allah? Decide on one small habit to keep your heart awake even while your body rests.
?
The Prophet endured hunger for your sake, to give you a model of patience and reliance on Allah. Do you follow him only in ease, or are you willing to experience hardship for his sake? When was the last time you willingly chose a difficulty (like fasting, giving charity while needy, or enduring an insult) purely to emulate him? If you cannot recall, ask Allah to grant you the strength to love him through action, not just words.

Proof of Prophets' Truthfulness and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Al-Bajuri expounds the proof of prophets' truthfulness via a conditional syllogism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that prophets must be truthful, including the conditional syllogism and the refutation of the Mu'tazila's claim of an intermediate state between truth and falsehood.

Core Idea
If prophets could lie, God's affirmation would be a lie—impossible.

Al-Bajuri presents a powerful rational argument for the truthfulness of prophets. This proof, known as the burhan of wujub sidqihim, relies on a conditional syllogism: if the prophets were not truthful, God's affirmation of them would entail lying, which is impossible for God. The Mu'tazila object by positing an intermediate category, but al-Bajuri rejects this, showing that no middle ground exists between truth and falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Read the Arabic passage carefully, focusing on the conditional syllogism: if prophets were not truthful, then God's news would be a lie.
Notice that the exceptive premise (lying is impossible for God) is omitted because it is obvious.
2
Examine the refutation of Mu'tazila
Identify the Mu'tazila position: they claim an intermediate state (what agrees with reality but contradicts belief) is neither truth nor falsehood. See how al-Bajuri rejects this by asserting no intermediate exists.
On the Mu'tazila view, negating truth does not entail falsehood, breaking the logical chain.
3
Reflect on the tanzili vs haqiqi distinction
Understand that God's 'news' of the prophets' truthfulness is not literal speech but conveyed through miracles (tanzili). This clarifies how the proof holds without requiring direct divine statements.
The proof remains valid because miracles serve as God's implicit confirmation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ أي: في دعوى الرسالة وفيما بلغوه عن الله تعالى؛ لأن هذا البرهان إنما يدل على ذلك كما مر. (وقوله: فَلِأَنَّهُمْ... إلخ) تقريره أن تقول: لو لم يَصْدُقُوا لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى، لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ، لكنّ الكذب في خبره تعالى محال فما أدى إليه ـ وهو عدم صدقهم - محال أيضاً، وإذا استحالَ عَدَمُ صدقهم ثَبَتَ صدقهم، وهو المطلوب. فالمصنف ذَكَرَ الشرطية، وحذف الاستثنائية لظهورها، ثم عَلَّلَ اللزوم في الشرطية بقوله: التصديقه تعالى لهم... إلخ). (قوله: لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا) أي بأن كَذَّبُوا لأنه لا واسِطة بين الكذب والصدق، خلافاً للمعتزلة في قولهم بالواسطة وهو ما وافَقَ الواقع وخالف الاعتقاد، فإن ذلك ليس بصدقٍ ولا كذب عندهم، وعلى هذا لا يلزم من انتفاء الصدق ثبوت الكذب كعكسه بخلافه على الأول. (قوله: لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى) يعني: التنزيلي لا الحقيقي؛ لأنه لم يُوجَدْ منه تعالى خبرٌ بصدقهم حقيقةً بأن قال: صَدَقَ عبدي ... إلخ، وإنما وُجِدَتِ المعجزة النازلة منزلةَ ذلك كما سيذكره المصنف. (قوله: لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ... إلخ) أي وتصديقُ الكاذب كَذِبٌ، وقد عرفت أن هذا دليلُ اللزوم في الشرطية. ومعنى التصديق الإخبار عن الصدق، فالمعنى: لإخبار الله تعالى عن صِدْقِهم في إخبارهم بأنهم رُسُلٌ مُبَلِّغُونَ عنه. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري :(قوله: مَا وَافَقَ الْوَاقِعَ ... إلخ) مثله ما وافق الاعتقاد وخالف الواقع، فالواسطة أمران. (قوله: دَلِيلُ اللُّزُومِ فِي الشَّرْطِيَّةِ أي مع ما تقدم من أنه لا واسطة بين الصدق والكذب، فدليل اللزوم مجموعها. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبايي (قوله: وَهُوَ مَا وَافَقَ الْوَاقِعَ وَخَالَفَ الْاِعْتِقَادَ أي أو العكس؛ إذ الصدقُ عندهم: موافَقَةُ الواقع والاعتقاد، والكذبُ: عدم موافقة الواقع والاعتقاد. (قوله: وَعَلَى هَذَا لَا يَلْزَمُ... إلخ) عبارة الشكتَاني - وتبعه الشرقاوي ـ: ولا يلزم على تقدير كَوْنِ خَبَرِ الرسول من هذا القبيل كَذِبُ خَبَرِه تعالى على هذا القول، والله أعلم؛ إذ تصديق الله لهم إنما هو باعتبار الواقع اهـ.
His statement: 'As for the proof of the necessity of their truthfulness' – meaning: in claiming messengership and in what they conveyed from God Most High, because this proof only indicates that as has passed. And his statement: 'For they... etc.' Its exposition is that you say: If they were not truthful, then lying would be necessary in His news, because of His affirmation of them, but lying in His news is impossible, so what leads to it – which is their lack of truthfulness – is also impossible, and when their lack of truthfulness is impossible, their truthfulness is established, which is the desired conclusion. So the author mentioned the conditional and omitted the exceptive premise due to its obviousness, then he explained the entailment in the conditional by his statement: 'His affirmation of them... etc.' His statement: 'If they were not truthful' – meaning: by lying, because there is no intermediate between lying and truth, contrary to the Mu'tazila in their claim of an intermediate, which is what agrees with reality and contradicts belief, for that is neither truth nor lying according to them, and on this, from the negation of truth the establishment of lying does not necessarily follow, nor vice versa, contrary to the first position. His statement: 'Then lying would be necessary in His news' – meaning: the declarative (tanzili) not the real (haqiqi), because there did not exist from Him a news about their truthfulness in reality, such as saying 'My servant has spoken the truth', but rather the miracle existed which is placed in the position of that, as the author will mention. His statement: 'Because of His affirmation of them... etc.' – meaning: and affirming a liar is a lie, and you have known that this is the proof of entailment in the conditional. And the meaning of affirmation is informing about truth, so the meaning is: because of God's informing about their truthfulness in their informing that they are messengers conveying from Him. The marginal note of al-Allama Ahmad al-Ajhuri: His statement: 'what agrees with reality... etc.' – similarly, what agrees with belief and contradicts reality, so the intermediate is two matters. His statement: 'The proof of entailment in the conditional' – meaning: along with what has preceded that there is no intermediate between truth and lying, so the proof of entailment is their combination. The qararat of al-Allama Muhammad al-Anbabi: His statement: 'And it is what agrees with reality and contradicts belief' – meaning: or the opposite, for truth according to them is agreement with reality and belief, and lying is disagreement with reality and belief. His statement: 'And on this it does not follow... etc.' – the expression of al-Shiktani – followed by al-Sharqawi: and it does not follow on the supposition that the news of the messenger is of this type that the news of God is a lie according to this statement, and God knows best, for God's affirmation of them is only with respect to reality. End.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage presents and explains the proof (burhan) for the necessity of prophets' truthfulness. It is a proof passage with objections and answers. The main argument: If the prophets were not truthful (i.e., if they lied), then given that God has affirmed them (through miracles), God's news would be a lie. But lying is impossible for God. Therefore, the supposition of their untruthfulness is impossible, so they must be truthful. The author (al-Sanusi) stated the conditional and omitted the exceptive premise (that lying in God's news is impossible) because it is obvious. Al-Bajuri then clarifies the premise 'if they were not truthful' means if they lied, because there is no middle ground between truth and lying. He refutes the Mu'tazila who claim an intermediate state (what agrees with reality but contradicts belief, or vice versa), which they consider neither truth nor lying. On their view, negating truth does not entail lying. Al-Bajuri dismisses this by insisting on no intermediate. He also distinguishes between God's literal 'news' of their truthfulness and the 'conveyed' (tanzili) news through miracles. The 'affirmation' (tasdiq) means God informing that they are truthful. The marginalia from al-Ajhuri and al-Anbabi further explain the Mu'tazila position and note that even on their view, the proof may still hold because God's affirmation is based on reality.

الشرطية

لا واسطة
المعتزلة
التنزيلي
تصديق الله
الخبر الحقيقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim an intermediate between truth and falsehood where a statement may agree with reality but contradict belief, making it neither truth nor lie.
Correction: In rational judgment, there is no third category; a statement is either true or false. God's truthfulness and justice require that His affirmation of a liar would be a lie, so prophets must be truthful.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of disagreement between the Sunni position and the Mu'tazila as mentioned in this proof?
A) Whether prophets can sin.
B) Whether there is an intermediate state between truth and falsehood.
C) Whether miracles are possible.
D) Whether God can lie.

Key Takeaway
The proof of prophets' truthfulness hinges on the impossibility of God lying, which would follow if a lie could be attributed to those He affirms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a command from the Prophet ﷺ that conflicts with your desires, do you ever treat it as less than absolutely truthful? How does the logical proof—that God cannot affirm a lie—challenge that hesitation? What will you do the next time such a conflict arises?
?
The Mu'tazila invented an intermediate category between truth and falsehood to allow for error. In your own life, have you created mental 'middle grounds' to excuse yourself from fully obeying prophetic teachings? Identify one specific teaching you have half-believed. How will you eradicate that intermediate state and embrace it as absolute truth?
?
If you truly internalized that every prophetic statement is backed by God's guarantee of truthfulness, which sunnah would you start practicing today that you have been neglecting? Give one concrete action you will commit to this week.

The Conditional Syllogism and Refutation of the Mu'tazila
Al-Bajuri explains the conditional syllogism and refutes the Mu'tazila's concept of an intermediate state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the conditional syllogism proves prophetic truthfulness and how al-Bajuri refutes the Mu'tazila's concept of an intermediate state.

Core Idea
The miracle is God's silent testimony that confirms a prophet's truthfulness.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary on Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin unpacks the logical proof for prophetic truthfulness. Al-Bajuri clarifies the structure of the conditional argument, counters the Mu'tazila's objection about an intermediate state between truth and falsehood, and illustrates the point with a vivid analogy. You will see how the miracle functions as God's affirmation without a verbal statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional syllogism
Notice that al-Sanusi only mentions the conditional premise; the exceptive premise is omitted because it is obvious. The argument is: if the prophet were not truthful, then God's testimony would be false, which is impossible.
2
Examine the proof of implication
Al-Bajuri explains that affirming a liar is a lie, so if God affirmed a false prophet, that would be a lie—impossible for God. This is the force of the conditional.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila's objection
The Mu'tazila claim that a statement conforming to reality but contradicting belief is neither truth nor falsehood—an intermediate state. If that exists, then denying truthfulness does not force falsehood.
Al-Bajuri counters by showing the argument assumes no intermediate, and even if it exists, the miracle replaces a verbal statement.
4
Learn the king's messenger analogy
Just as a king's extraordinary act confirms a self-proclaimed messenger, a miracle confirms a prophet. The miracle is God's act that takes the place of a verbal statement of affirmation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالمصنف ذَكَرَ الشرطية، وحذف الاستثنائية لظهورها، ثم عَلَّلَ اللزوم في الشرطية بقوله: التصديقه تعالى لهم... إلخ).
(قوله: لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا) أي بأن كَذَّبوا لأنه لا واسِطة بين الكذب والصدق، خلافاً للمعتزلة في قولهم بالواسطة وهو ما وافَقَ الواقع وخالف الاعتقاد، فإن ذلك ليس بصدقٍ ولا كذب عندهم، وعلى هذا لا يلزم من انتفاء الصدق ثبوت الكذب كعكسه بخلافه على الأول.
(قوله: لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى) يعني: التنزيلي لا الحقيقي؛ لأنه لم يُوجَدْ منه تعالى خبرٌ بصدقهم حقيقةً بأن قال: صَدَقَ عبدي ... إلخ، وإنما وُجِدَتِ المعجزة النازلة منزلةَ ذلك كما سيذكره المصنف.
(قوله: لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ... إلخ) أي وتصديقُ الكاذب كَذِبٌ، وقد عرفت أن هذا دليلُ اللزوم في الشرطية. ومعنى التصديق الإخبار عن الصدق، فالمعنى: لإخبار الله تعالى عن صِدْقِهم في إخبارهم بأنهم رُسُلٌ مُبَلِّغُونَ عنه.
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
:(قوله: مَا وَافَقَ الْوَاقِعَ ... إلخ) مثله ما وافق الاعتقاد وخالف الواقع، فالواسطة أمران.
(قوله: دَلِيلُ اللُّزُومِ فِي الشَّرْطِيَّةِ أي مع ما تقدم من أنه لا واسطة بين الصدق والكذب، فدليل اللزوم مجموعها.
تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبايي
(قوله: وَهُوَ مَا وَافَقَ الْوَاقِعَ وَخَالَفَ الْاِعْتِقَادَ أي أو العكس؛ إذ الصدقُ عندهم: موافَقَةُ الواقع والاعتقاد، والكذبُ: عدم موافقة الواقع والاعتقاد.
(قوله: وَعَلَى هَذَا لَا يَلْزَمُ... إلخ) عبارة الشكتَاني - وتبعه الشرقاوي ـ: ولا يلزم على تقدير كَوْنِ خَبَرِ الرسول من هذا القبيل كَذِبُ خَبَرِه تعالى على هذا القول، والله أعلم؛ إذ تصديق الله لهم إنما هو باعتبار الواقع اهـ.
حاشية البيجوري على السنوسية
ونظير ذلك: ما إذا ادعى شخص لجماعة أنه رسولُ المَلِك، وأخبرهم بأنه يأمُرُهم بكذا وكذا، فقالوا له: ما الدليل على صدقك؟ فيقول: أن يفعل الملك كذا وكذا على خلاف عادته، فيفعلُ الملكُ ذلك دليلاً على صدقه، ففِعْلُه ذلك تصديق له؛ لأنه نازل منزلة قوله : صَدَقَ ذلك الشخص في دعواه أنه رسولي وفيما أخبركم به.
The author (al-Sanusi) mentioned the conditional [syllogism] and omitted the exceptive [premise] because it is obvious. Then he explained the implication in the conditional by his saying: 'God's affirming them as truthful... etc.'
(His saying: 'If they were not truthful') meaning they lied, because there is no intermediate between lying and truthfulness, contrary to the Mu'tazila in their claim of an intermediate, which is that which conforms to reality but contradicts belief. For that is neither truth nor falsehood according to them. And on this [view], it does not follow from the negation of truthfulness the establishment of falsehood, nor vice versa, contrary to the first [view].
(His saying: 'then lying would be necessary in His report, exalted') means: the reported [lying], not the real [lying]; because there did not occur from Him, exalted, a report of their truthfulness in reality by His saying: 'My servant has spoken truthfully'... etc. Rather, the miracle which is placed in the position of that came about, as the author will mention.
(His saying: 'because of God's affirming them as truthful... etc.') means that affirming a liar is a lie, and you have known that this is the proof of implication in the conditional. And the meaning of 'affirming' (tasdiq) is informing of truthfulness. So the meaning is: because of God's informing about their truthfulness in their reports that they are messengers conveying from Him.
Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri:
(His saying: 'that which conforms to reality... etc.') the like of it is that which conforms to belief but contradicts reality, so the intermediate is two things.
(His saying: 'the proof of implication in the conditional') that is, along with what has preceded that there is no intermediate between truth and falsehood, so the proof of implication is their totality.
Annotations of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi:
(His saying: 'and it is that which conforms to reality and contradicts belief') meaning or the opposite; for truth according to them is conformity to reality and belief, and falsehood is non-conformity to reality and belief.
(His saying: 'and on this it does not follow... etc.') The expression of al-Shakani — and al-Sharqawi followed him —: And it does not follow, on the assumption that the report of the messenger is of this kind, that the report of God, exalted, would be false according to this view, and God knows best; for God's affirming them is only according to reality. End.
Hashiya of al-Bajuri on al-Sanusiyya:
A parallel to that: the case where a person claims to a group that he is the messenger of the king, and informs them that he commands them such and such. They say to him: what is the proof of your truthfulness? He says: that the king does such and such contrary to his custom, and the king does that as a proof of his truthfulness. So that act of his is an affirmation of him (tasdiq) because it is in the position of his saying: 'That person has spoken truthfully in his claim that he is my messenger and in what he informed you of.'
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the conditional syllogism used to prove the truthfulness of prophets. It begins by noting that al-Sanusi presented only the conditional premise, omitting the exceptive premise because it is obvious. The argument is: if the prophet were not truthful (i.e., lied), then God's testimony affirming him would be false, which is impossible. The proof of the implication is that affirming a liar is itself a lie. The passage then addresses the Mu'tazila's objection that there exists an intermediate state between truth and falsehood: a statement that conforms to reality but contradicts belief, which they consider neither true nor false. If that were accepted, then denying truthfulness would not necessarily imply falsehood. Al-Bajuri counters by showing that the argument is built on the assumption of no intermediate, and even if such an intermediate existed, the miracle is considered a substitute for a verbal statement from God, so it still constitutes an affirmation. The analogy of a king's messenger illustrates how an extraordinary act serves as a declaration of truth without a verbal statement. The glosses clarify that the Mu'tazila's intermediate actually has two forms and that the proof of implication rests on the lack of an intermediate. The overall point is that the miracle establishes prophetic truthfulness because it functions as God's silent confirmation.

Key Terms
شرطية (conditional)
استثنائية (exceptive premise)
التصديق (affirmation/tasdiq)
الواسطة (intermediate state)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
التنزيلي (reported/positional)
الحقيقي (real/actual)
المعجزة (miracle)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila's intermediate state (al-wasita) provides a valid escape from the conditional argument, making the proof of prophetic truthfulness invalid.
Correction: Al-Bajuri shows that the argument assumes no intermediate, and even if it existed, the miracle replaces a verbal statement, so the implication remains valid. The proof rests on either the absence of an intermediate or on the miracle functioning as an affirmation.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazila's position regarding statements that conform to reality but contradict belief?
A) Such statements are considered true.
B) Such statements are considered false.
C) Such statements are neither true nor false, constituting an intermediate state.
D) Such statements are considered lies.

Key Takeaway
The miracle is God's silent affirmation of a prophet's truthfulness, and the logical argument for this remains sound even after addressing the Mu'tazila's intermediate state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The miracle is God's silent testimony. Have you ever witnessed something in your life that you could only explain as God confirming His truth? If so, did you respond with unwavering faith, or did you rationalize it away? What would it take for you to accept a miracle as God's personal message to you?
?
The Mu'tazila invented an intermediate state between truth and falsehood to avoid the implications of the argument. Are there areas of your life where you create comfortable intermediate positions—excuses that are neither full obedience nor outright disobedience? Name one area where you are living in a 'wasita' and commit to leaving it for the truth of Allah's command.
?
Al-Bajuri says affirming a liar is itself a lie. Every time you remain silent when the truth is challenged, or when you nod along with falsehood to avoid conflict, you are indirectly affirming a liar. In what relationship or situation today do you need to take a stand for truth, even if it costs you?

The Six Categories of Extraordinary Events
Al-Bajuri enumerates six types of extraordinary events with definitions and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six categories of extraordinary events in Islamic theology and how each is defined by the nature of the person performing it and the context.

Core Idea
Extraordinary events are not all miracles; each type has a distinct purpose and agent.

Al-Bajuri presents a systematic classification of events that break natural law. Not every wonder is a miracle; the status of the person and the timing determine the category. This lesson unpacks the six types and their significance, using the example of Musaylima the liar to illustrate humiliation (ihana).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own classification come through before you interpret.
Notice the poetic summary at the end – it's a mnemonic.
2
Identify the six categories
The passage lists six types of extraordinary events. For each, note the agent (prophet, saint, commoner, sinner) and the condition (before/after prophethood, etc.).
Mu'jiza is only after the claim of prophethood.
3
Understand the distinguishing conditions
Focus on what makes each type unique: timing (irhas vs mu'jiza), the person's righteousness (karama), need (ma'una), deception (istidraj), or refutation (ihana).
4
Reflect on the example of Musaylima
The story of Musaylima shows how ihana works: his false claims are debunked as the 'miracles' backfire. This reinforces the theological lesson.
This is a real historical example from Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: بِالْمُعْجِزَةِ) أي: التي هي الأمرُ الخارق للعادة، بقيد أن يكون بعد الرسالة، بخلافه قَبْلَها، فإنه إرْهَاصٌ أي تأسيس لها. وبَقِي من أقسام الخارق للعادة الكرامة: وهي ما يَظْهَرُ على يد عبد ظاهِرِ الصلاح والمعونة: وهي ما يَظْهَرُ على يد العوام تخليصاً لهم من شِدَّةٍ نازلة بهم مثلاً. والاستدراج: وهو ما يَظْهَرُ على يَدِ فَاسِقِ خديعة ومكراً به. والإهانة: وهي ما يَظْهَرُ على يده تكذيباً له، كما وَقَعَ لمُسَيْلَمَةَ الكذَّاب، فإنه تَفَلَ في عين أعور لتبرأ، فعَمِيَتِ الصحيحة، وتَفَلَ في بئر ليكثر ماؤها، فغاضتْ، وتَفَلَ في بئرِ ليَعْذُبَ ماؤها، فصارت مِلْحاً أُجَاجاً!! فتحصَّلَ أن أقسام الأمر الخارق للعادة ستة أقسام، وقد جمعها بعضهم في قوله: 
إِذَا مَا رَأَيْتَ الْأَمْرَ يَخْرُقُ عَادَةً 
فَمُعْجِزَةٌ إِنْ مِنْ نَبِيَّ لَنَا صَدَرْ 
وَإِنْ بَانَ مِنْهُ قَبْلَ وَضف نُبُوَّة 
فَالْإِرْهَاصُ سَمِّة تَتْبَعِ الْقَوْمَ فِي الْأَثَرُ 
وَإِنْ جَاءَ يَوْماً مِنْ وَلِي فَإِنَّهُ الْ 
كَرَامَةُ فِي التَّحْقِيقِ عِنْدَ ذَوِي النَّظَرْ 
وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ بَعْضِ الْعَوَامِ صُدُورُهُ 
فَكَنُوهُ حَقَّا بِالْمَعُونَةِ وَاشْتَهَرْ 
وَمِنْ فَاسِقٍ إِنْ كَانَ وَفْقَ مُرَادِهِ 
يُسَمَّى بِالْاِسْتِدْرَاجِ فِيمَا قَدِ اسْتَقَرَ 
وَإِلَّا فَيُدْعَى بِالْإِهَانَةِ عِنْدَهُمْ 
وَقَدْ تَمَّتِ الْأَقْسَامُ عِنْدَ الَّذِي اخْتَبَرْ
حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري
(قوله: فَغَاضَتْ بالضاد المعجمة أي ذهب ماؤها من أصله.
(His saying: 'by the miracle') i.e., which is the extraordinary matter, with the condition that it occurs after the prophetic mission, contrary to before it, for then it is irhas, i.e., foundation. Remaining from the categories of the extraordinary are: al-karama: which is what appears at the hand of a servant apparent in righteousness; and al-ma'una: which is what appears at the hand of the common people to deliver them from a hardship that has befallen them, for example; and al-istidraj: which is what appears at the hand of a sinner as deceit and deception for him; and al-ihana: which is what appears at his hand as a refutation of him, as happened to Musaylima the liar. Indeed, he spat into the eye of a one-eyed man to be healed, so the healthy eye went blind; and he spat into a well for its water to become abundant, so it dried up; and he spat into a well for its water to become sweet, so it became bitter salty water! So it results that the categories of the extraordinary are six categories. Some have collected them in his statement:
When you see a matter breaking a custom,
if it emanates from a prophet of ours, it is a mu'jiza;
if it appears from him before the description of prophethood, then call it irhas, following the people in the trace;
if it comes from a saint, then it is karama in truth according to the people of scrutiny;
if it comes from some common people, then call it rightly ma'una, and it is famous;
if from a sinner, and it is in accordance with his desire, it is called istidraj in what has been established;
otherwise it is called ihana among them, and the categories are completed for the one who tested.
Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri:
(His saying: 'fa ghadat' with the emphasized dad) i.e., its water went from its source.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a classification of extraordinary events (al-khariq lil-'ada). It begins by defining the miracle (mu'jiza) as an extraordinary act that occurs after a prophet has claimed prophethood, serving as proof. Before the claim, such an act is called irhas (foundation or preparation). Then it lists four other categories: karama (wonder) appears at the hand of a righteous saint; ma'una (divine assistance) appears at the hand of ordinary people to relieve them; istidraj (gradual deception) appears at the hand of a sinner in accordance with his desire, as a trap; and ihana (humiliation) appears at the hand of a liar as a refutation, exemplified by Musaylima the false prophet whose supposed miracles backfired. The passage concludes that the sum of extraordinary events is six types, and provides a poetic summary that restates the categories: mu'jiza from a prophet, irhas before prophethood, karama from a saint, ma'una from commoners, istidraj from a sinner when it aligns with his desire, and ihana otherwise. The gloss explains the word 'faghadat' (dried up) from the story of Musaylima.

Key Terms
معجزة (mu'jiza/miracle)
إرهاص (irhas/foundation)
كرامة (karama/wonder)
معونة (ma'una/assistance)
استدراج (istidraj/gradual deception)
إهانة (ihana/humiliation)
خارق للعادة (extraordinary)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All extraordinary events are miracles (mu'jiza).
Correction: Only events performed by a prophet after his claim as proof are miracles. Others serve different purposes and have different names.

Checkpoint
Which category does an extraordinary event performed by a saint (wali) fall under?
A) Mu'jiza
B) Irhas
C) Karama
D) Ma'una

Key Takeaway
Extraordinary events are classified into six types based on the agent and context, with mu'jiza reserved for prophets as proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience an unexpected relief or 'lucky break', do you immediately attribute it to your own worthiness, or pause to consider it might be ma'una—a mercy you didn't earn? How would your gratitude change if you treated every ease as a direct divine assistance rather than coincidence?
?
Could you be chasing worldly blessings that are actually istidraj—a gradual lure away from Allah? Honestly examine one area of life where your desires align with ease; do you see any sign of spiritual danger in that alignment?
?
The story of Musaylima shows that a false claim can lead public humiliation despite seeming successes. Are you living more concerned with how others perceive you than with the truth of your own soul? What would it take for you to prioritize sincerity over reputation today?
