The Miracle as Informing (Ikhbar) and Its Consequences
Al-Bajuri presents the ikhbar interpretation of miracle and its logical consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ikhbar interpretation of miracle and why it leads to the necessity of God's truthfulness being at stake.

Core Idea
On the ikhbar view, a false prophet would make God a liar.

In this passage, al-Bajuri presents the first of two interpretations of what a miracle indicates. According to one view, a miracle is a divine statement informing that the prophet is truthful. This interpretation has a significant theological implication: if the prophet were false, God's statement would be false, implying that God could lie. This lesson explores that interpretation and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice how al-Bajuri introduces the ikhbar view and the consequence.
2
Identify the key terms
Look for the terms إخبار (informing) and صدق (truthfulness). Understand how they relate.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the ikhbar view makes God's truthfulness contingent on the prophet's truthfulness.
This is a critical point in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: النَّازِلَةُ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي... إلخ) أي: لدلالتها على صدق مَن ظهرت على يديه، فكأن الله قال: صدق عبدي ... إلخ، وهذا كله مبني على القول بأن مدلول المعجزة الإخبارُ عن صِدْقِ الرُّسُل حتى يلزمَ على عدم صدقهم الكذب في خبره تعالى، وأما على القول بأن مدلولها : إنشاء الدلالة على صدقهم. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري.
(قوله: وَالْابْتِلَاءُ) جعله من الخارق غير ظاهر، ولم يذكر الابتلاء من أقسام الخارق في "حاشية الهدهدي" ولا في حاشية الدسوقي على المصنف". (قوله: إِنْشَاءُ الدِّلَالَةِ عَلَى صِدْقِهِمْ المراد بذلك الإنشاء: طلب التبليغ كما هو مصرح به في حاشية الهدهدي" و"حاشية الدسوقي على المصنف. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي.
قال بعض مشايخنا وفيه: أن التصديق النسبة إلى الصدق، وحيث اعتبر في الصدق الاعتقاد على هذا القول؛ كان معنى : صَدَقَ عبدي في كل ما يبلغ عني: وافَقَ خبرُهُ الواقع والاعتقاد في كلّ ما يُبَلِّغُ عني، والفَرَضُ : أنه خالَفَ الاعتقاد، فيلزم كَذِبُ المصدّق، وهو تعالى؛ لأنه لا يُعْتَبَرُ في صدقه اعتقاد لتنزهه عنه، فالاختلاف بين أهل السنة والمعتزلة في تفسير الصدق والكذب إنما هو بالنسبة إلى الحادث، فالملازمة صحيحة على كلّ حالٍ. نعم؛ ينبغي حَمْلُ الكلام على مذهب أهل السنة لكونه المذهب المنصور. تأمل.

(قوله: وَالْابْتِلَاءُ) كأن يَقَعَ له زيادةُ مَرَضِ على خلاف عادته. اهـ مؤلف.
(١) ابن عرفة هو محمد بن محمد الورغمي، أبو عبد الله، إمام تونس وعالمها وخطيبها، مولده ووفاته فيها له: "المختصر الشامل في التوحيد، توفي سنة (٨٠٣هـ).
فلا يلزمُ على عدم صدقهم: الكذبُ في خبره تعالى؛ لأن الصدق والكَذِبَ من أوصاف الخبر لا الإنشاء، وإنما يلزم حينئذٍ وجودُ الدليل بدون المدلول
His saying: 'that which stands in the position of His saying: My servant has spoken truthfully... etc.' meaning: because it indicates the truthfulness of the one upon whose hands it appears, so it is as if God said: My servant has spoken truthfully... etc. All of this is built upon the view that the meaning of the miracle is informing of the truthfulness of the messengers, so that if they were not truthful, lying would be necessary in the news of God. As for the view that its meaning is the institution of indication of their truthfulness. Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri.
(His saying: 'and affliction') making it among the extraordinary is not apparent, and he did not mention affliction among the divisions of the extraordinary in the Hashiyah of al-Hadadi nor in the Hashiyah of al-Dasuqi on the work. (His saying: 'the institution of indication of their truthfulness') what is meant by that institution is requesting the delivery, as is explicitly stated in the Hashiyah of al-Hadadi and the Hashiyah of al-Dasuqi on the work. Decisions of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi.
Some of our teachers said: there is something in it: verification is attribution to truthfulness, and since belief is considered in truthfulness according to this view, the meaning of 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me' is: his news agreed with reality and belief in everything he conveys from Me. The assumption is that he opposed belief, so lying of the verifier, i.e., God, would be necessary, because belief is not considered in His truthfulness due to His transcendence. The difference between Ahl al-Sunnah and the Mu'tazila in interpreting truthfulness and lying is only with respect to the created being. So the implication is correct in every case. Yes, it is appropriate to interpret the speech according to the school of Ahl al-Sunnah because it is the supported school. Reflect.
(His saying: 'But sorcery was added to it') meaning: based on it being extraordinary, as is the doctrine of Ibn 'Arafa and the author of al-Maqasid, contrary to al-Qarafi who says it is habitual, and its strangeness is only due to ignorance of its causes. So whoever knows its causes and practices it, it is possible. And according to this view, the author proceeded in al-Kubra when he said: 'And among the habitual are sorcery and the like.'
(His saying: 'and affliction') such that an increase of illness occurs to him contrary to his habit. End of the author.
(1) Ibn 'Arafa is Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Warghami, Abu 'Abd Allah, the Imam of Tunis and its scholar and preacher, born and died there. He authored 'al-Mukhtasar al-Shamil fi al-Tawhid', died in 803 AH.
So it is not necessary, upon their lack of truthfulness, that there be lying in the news of God, because truthfulness and lying are attributes of information, not of institution. Rather, what would be necessary in that case is the existence of the indication without the indicated.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of miracle and its indication. It begins by explaining a phrase from the matn, stating that the miracle stands in the position of God saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' This is based on one opinion: the miracle informs (ikhbar) of the messengers' truthfulness, so if they were false, God would be lying. The author then presents the alternative opinion: the miracle is an institution (insha') of the indication, not an informative statement. A gloss by al-Ajhuri notes that making affliction (ibtila') a category of the extraordinary is not apparent, and it was not mentioned in other commentaries. Another note clarifies that 'institution of indication' means requesting the delivery of the message. The discussion then turns to the concept of tasdiq (verification) and the difference between Ahl al-Sunnah and Mu'tazila regarding the definition of truth and falsehood in relation to God and humans. The passage concludes with an addition: sorcery (sihr) and affliction (ibtila') are added as types of extraordinary events, with a note on the disagreement between Ibn 'Arafa and al-Qarafi over whether sorcery is habitual or extraordinary. The final sentence on page 178 explains that on the institution view, the falsehood of prophets does not entail God lying, but only that the indication exists without the indicated.

Key Terms
معجزة
إخبار
صدق
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the miracle itself proves prophecy without any divine speech.
Correction: The ikhbar view holds that the miracle is a divine statement about the prophet's truthfulness.

Checkpoint
According to the ikhbar view, what would happen if a prophet were not truthful?
A) The miracle would cease to exist.
B) God would be lying.
C) The prophet would be punished.
D) The miracle would become habitual.

Key Takeaway
The ikhbar view interprets the miracle as a divine informative statement, implying that a false prophet would entail a false statement from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the miracles of the Prophet are like God saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully,' do you still find yourself hesitating to obey his commands? What does that hesitation reveal about your trust in God's testimony?
?
The lesson shows that a false prophet would make God a liar. Are there areas in your life where you are acting as if the prophetic message is not fully true—perhaps in your priorities, choices, or hidden habits? How will you realign with the truth today?

The Miracle as Institution (Insha') and the Analysis of Tasdiq
Al-Bajuri explains the insha' interpretation and analyzes the concept of tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the insha' interpretation of miracle and how it avoids the problem of God's truthfulness, along with the related discussion on tasdiq.

Core Idea
On the insha' view, the miracle is not a report but an instituted sign, so no divine lying ensues.

This lesson delves into the second interpretation of miracle, where it is seen as an institution (insha') of indication rather than a statement. The passage explores the meaning of 'institution' and then engages in a detailed analysis of tasdiq (verification), explaining how truthfulness and lying are understood differently for God and humans.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the text starting from the definition of insha' to the reflection on Ahl al-Sunnah.
2
Understand the concept of institution
Note that 'institution' here means requesting the delivery of the message, not informing.
3
Follow the tasdiq analysis
Carefully follow the argument about how truthfulness applies to God and creatures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: النَّازِلَةُ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي... إلخ) أي: لدلالتها على صدق مَن ظهرت على يديه، فكأن الله قال: صدق عبدي ... إلخ، وهذا كله مبني على القول بأن مدلول المعجزة الإخبارُ عن صِدْقِ الرُّسُل حتى يلزمَ على عدم صدقهم الكذب في خبره تعالى، وأما على القول بأن مدلولها : إنشاء الدلالة على صدقهم. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري.
(قوله: وَالْابْتِلَاءُ) جعله من الخارق غير ظاهر، ولم يذكر الابتلاء من أقسام الخارق في "حاشية الهدهدي" ولا في حاشية الدسوقي على المصنف". (قوله: إِنْشَاءُ الدِّلَالَةِ عَلَى صِدْقِهِمْ المراد بذلك الإنشاء: طلب التبليغ كما هو مصرح به في حاشية الهدهدي" و"حاشية الدسوقي على المصنف. تقريرات العلامة محمد الأنبابي.
قال بعض مشايخنا وفيه: أن التصديق النسبة إلى الصدق، وحيث اعتبر في الصدق الاعتقاد على هذا القول؛ كان معنى : صَدَقَ عبدي في كل ما يبلغ عني: وافَقَ خبرُهُ الواقع والاعتقاد في كلّ ما يُبَلِّغُ عني، والفَرَضُ : أنه خالَفَ الاعتقاد، فيلزم كَذِبُ المصدّق، وهو تعالى؛ لأنه لا يُعْتَبَرُ في صدقه اعتقاد لتنزهه عنه، فالاختلاف بين أهل السنة والمعتزلة في تفسير الصدق والكذب إنما هو بالنسبة إلى الحادث، فالملازمة صحيحة على كلّ حالٍ. نعم؛ ينبغي حَمْلُ الكلام على مذهب أهل السنة لكونه المذهب المنصور. تأمل.
(قوله: لَكِنْ زِيدَ عَلَيْهِ السِّحْرُ) أي: بناءً على أنه خارق للعادة كما هو مذهب ابن عَرَفَةً (١) وصاحب "المقاصد"، خلافاً للقَرَافِي القائل: إنه معتاد، وغرابته إنما هي للجهل بأسبابه، فكل عَرَفَ أسبابَهُ وتعاطاه؛ أجابَ معه، وعلى هذا القول جرى المصنف في من "الكبرى" حيث قال: ومن المعتاد السحرُ ونحوه.
(قوله: وَالْابْتِلَاءُ) كأن يَقَعَ له زيادةُ مَرَضِ على خلاف عادته. اهـ مؤلف.
(١) ابن عرفة هو محمد بن محمد الورغمي، أبو عبد الله، إمام تونس وعالمها وخطيبها، مولده ووفاته فيها له: "المختصر الشامل في التوحيد، توفي سنة (٨٠٣هـ).
فلا يلزمُ على عدم صدقهم: الكذبُ في خبره تعالى؛ لأن الصدق والكَذِبَ من أوصاف الخبر لا الإنشاء، وإنما يلزم حينئذٍ وجودُ الدليل بدون المدلول
His saying: 'that which stands in the position of His saying: My servant has spoken truthfully... etc.' meaning: because it indicates the truthfulness of the one upon whose hands it appears, so it is as if God said: My servant has spoken truthfully... etc. All of this is built upon the view that the meaning of the miracle is informing of the truthfulness of the messengers, so that if they were not truthful, lying would be necessary in the news of God. As for the view that its meaning is the institution of indication of their truthfulness. Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri.
(His saying: 'and affliction') making it among the extraordinary is not apparent, and he did not mention affliction among the divisions of the extraordinary in the Hashiyah of al-Hadadi nor in the Hashiyah of al-Dasuqi on the work. (His saying: 'the institution of indication of their truthfulness') what is meant by that institution is requesting the delivery, as is explicitly stated in the Hashiyah of al-Hadadi and the Hashiyah of al-Dasuqi on the work. Decisions of the scholar Muhammad al-Anbabi.
Some of our teachers said: there is something in it: verification is attribution to truthfulness, and since belief is considered in truthfulness according to this view, the meaning of 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me' is: his news agreed with reality and belief in everything he conveys from Me. The assumption is that he opposed belief, so lying of the verifier, i.e., God, would be necessary, because belief is not considered in His truthfulness due to His transcendence. The difference between Ahl al-Sunnah and the Mu'tazila in interpreting truthfulness and lying is only with respect to the created being. So the implication is correct in every case. Yes, it is appropriate to interpret the speech according to the school of Ahl al-Sunnah because it is the supported school. Reflect.
(His saying: 'But sorcery was added to it') meaning: based on it being extraordinary, as is the doctrine of Ibn 'Arafa and the author of al-Maqasid, contrary to al-Qarafi who says it is habitual, and its strangeness is only due to ignorance of its causes. So whoever knows its causes and practices it, it is possible. And according to this view, the author proceeded in al-Kubra when he said: 'And among the habitual are sorcery and the like.'
(His saying: 'and affliction') such that an increase of illness occurs to him contrary to his habit. End of the author.
(1) Ibn 'Arafa is Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Warghami, Abu 'Abd Allah, the Imam of Tunis and its scholar and preacher, born and died there. He authored 'al-Mukhtasar al-Shamil fi al-Tawhid', died in 803 AH.
So it is not necessary, upon their lack of truthfulness, that there be lying in the news of God, because truthfulness and lying are attributes of information, not of institution. Rather, what would be necessary in that case is the existence of the indication without the indicated.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of miracle and its indication. It begins by explaining a phrase from the matn, stating that the miracle stands in the position of God saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' This is based on one opinion: the miracle informs (ikhbar) of the messengers' truthfulness, so if they were false, God would be lying. The author then presents the alternative opinion: the miracle is an institution (insha') of the indication, not an informative statement. A gloss by al-Ajhuri notes that making affliction (ibtila') a category of the extraordinary is not apparent, and it was not mentioned in other commentaries. Another note clarifies that 'institution of indication' means requesting the delivery of the message. The discussion then turns to the concept of tasdiq (verification) and the difference between Ahl al-Sunnah and Mu'tazila regarding the definition of truth and falsehood in relation to God and humans. The passage concludes with an addition: sorcery (sihr) and affliction (ibtila') are added as types of extraordinary events, with a note on the disagreement between Ibn 'Arafa and al-Qarafi over whether sorcery is habitual or extraordinary. The final sentence on page 178 explains that on the institution view, the falsehood of prophets does not entail God lying, but only that the indication exists without the indicated.

Key Terms
إنشاء
تصديق
صدق
كذب
اعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the insha' view still makes God's truthfulness depend on the prophet.
Correction: The passage explains that for God, truthfulness does not involve belief, so no lying arises.

Checkpoint
According to the insha' view, what is the meaning of 'institution' in the context of miracle?
A) Informing of truthfulness
B) Requesting the delivery of the message
C) Creating the miracle physically
D) Affirming the prophet's honesty

Key Takeaway
The insha' view interprets the miracle as an instituted sign, not a divine statement, thus avoiding any question of God's truthfulness being compromised by a false prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may have never thought that the way we define 'truth' could differ between God and yourself. When you read that belief is not attributed to God, does it unsettle you that your own standard of truth is not God’s? How will you adjust your understanding of God’s truthfulness in moments when circumstances seem to contradict His promises?
?
This lesson shows that even the most subtle theological arguments have real consequences — they protect God from being reduced to human categories. In what areas of your life have you unknowingly imagined God’s actions as if He were a human, and what will you do to correct that image starting today?
?
Al-Bajuri’s analysis reveals that the Mu'tazilite definition of truth would actually cause a problem if applied to God. Have you ever held a belief about God that, if truly thought through, would lead to an impossibility or contradiction? Will you commit to testing your current understanding of God’s attributes against rigorous scholarship?

Addition of Sorcery and Affliction as Extraordinary Events
Al-Bajuri discusses the addition of sihr and ibtila' as extraordinary events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sorcery (sihr) and affliction (ibtila') are added as types of extraordinary events and the scholarly disagreements surrounding them.

Core Idea
Sorcery is considered extraordinary by some, affliction an unusual hardship.

The passage extends the discussion of extraordinary events beyond miracles to include sorcery and affliction. There is a disagreement on whether sorcery is truly extraordinary or merely habitual due to ignorance. Affliction is defined as an unusual increase in illness. This lesson examines these additions and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the text covering the addition of sihr and ibtila', including the footnote on Ibn 'Arafa.
2
Understand the disagreement on sihr
Note the two positions: Ibn 'Arafa and al-Qarafi on whether sorcery is extraordinary or habitual.
3
Define affliction
See how affliction is defined as an extraordinary event contrary to habit.
4
Reflect on the final line
The final line reinforces the consequence of the insha' view.
It connects back to the earlier lesson.

The Proof of Trustworthiness: A Conditional Argument
Al-Bajuri presents the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness of prophets using a conditional argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that prophets must be trustworthy, based on the command to follow them.

Core Idea
If prophets could sin, following them would turn sin into obedience—impossible, so they are sinless.

In this lesson, Al-Bajuri presents a crisp rational argument for the obligation of trustworthiness (amanah) of prophets. He uses a conditional statement and a reductio ad absurdum to show that prophets are infallible. This argument is foundational for the sam'iyyat section.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the argument.
Focus on the conditional structure.
2
Identify the conditional statement
The argument begins with a conditional: 'If they betrayed... then the forbidden would become obedience.' Find this in the text.
The antecedent is the betrayal, the consequent is the transformation.
3
Understand the implication (luzum)
The author justifies the implication by stating that God commanded us to follow the prophets. So if they did something, we must follow it, making it obedience. Understand this reasoning.
This is the key step.
4
Recognize the impossibility
It is impossible for a forbidden act to be obedience. Therefore, the consequent is false, so the antecedent must be false. That means prophets do not betray.
This is the reductio.
5
Conclude the obligation of trustworthiness
Since betrayal is impossible, prophets are trustworthy. This is the desired conclusion (matlub).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فَلِأَنَّهُمْ... إلخ) تقريرُهُ أن تقول: لو خانوا بفِعْل مُحَرَّم أو مكروه لا نقلب المحرَّمُ أو المكروه طاعةً في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام، لكن التالي باطل، وإذا بَطَلَ التالي بَطَلَ المقدَّمُ، فثبت نقيضُه، وهو المطلوب. فالمصنف ذَكَرَ الشرطية، وحَذَفَ الاستثنائية لظهورها، ثم بَيَّنَ وجه اللزوم في الشرطية بقوله: (لأن الله تعالى أمرنا بالاقتداء بهم... إلخ). ومُحَصَّلُه أن جميع ما صَدَرَ عنهم لا يكون إلا مأموراً به من الله تعالى وكلّ ما أَمَرَ به لا يكون إلا طاعة؛ لأنه لا يأمر بالفحشاء. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري.
(وقوله: وجُودُ الدَّليل) أي: الدال على ذلك الإنشاء الذي هو المعجزة. (وقوله: بِدُونِ الْمَدْلُولِ) المراد به متعلق المدلول لا نفس المدلول؛ لأن المدلول وهو طلب التبليغ حاصل بالمعجزة قطعاً على هذا القول؛ لأنها على هذا القول إنشاء والإنشاء ما حصل مدلوله به فالمتخلف هنا تبليغ ما أمروا بتبليغه الذي هو متعلق الطلب؛ لأنهم إن لم يصدقوا فقد بلغوا غير ما أمروا بتبليغه. ويرد على هذا القول أن المعجزة متأخرة عن التبليغ، فلا يظهر كونها دالة على طلبه، وإنما يظهر ذلك لو كانت سابقة عليه. تقريرات العلامة محمد الألبابي
(قوله: وَمُحَصَّلُهُ : أَنَّ جَمِيعَ مَا صَدَرَ عَنْهُمْ... إلخ) غاية ما يُسْتَفَادُ من قول المصنف: لأن الله أمرنا بالاقتداء بهم... إلخ): أنه لو وقع منهم الزنا مثلاً، لانقلب المحرَّمُ طاعةً لكوننا مأمورين باتباعهم فيه، ولا يأمرُ الله عبده إلا بطاعة، فيكون الزنا في حق المأمورين - وهم أتباع النبي - طاعةً، فقد انْقَلَبَتِ المعصية في حق المأمورين طاعةً في حقهم أيضاً، و انقلاب المعصية طاعةً ،محال، فما أدى إليه محال، فثبت المطلوب، ولم يُسْتَقَد من هذا: انقلاب المحرم مثلاً طاعة في حق الرسل، بل في حق المأمورين، فقول المصنف: (في حقهم غير ظاهر
(His saying: 'As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, may peace and blessings be upon them, it is because they... etc.') Its elaboration is that you say: If they betrayed by doing something forbidden or disliked, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience with respect to them, may peace and blessings be upon them. But the consequent is false, and when the consequent is false, the antecedent is false, so its opposite is established, which is the desired conclusion. So the author mentioned the conditional and omitted the exceptive because it is obvious, then he explained the aspect of the implication in the conditional by his saying: 'Because God Almighty commanded us to follow them... etc.' And its conclusion is that all that issues from them is not but commanded by God Almighty, and everything He commands is not but obedience, because He does not command indecency. Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri.
(And his saying: 'the existence of the indication') i.e., the indicator of that institution which is the miracle. (And his saying: 'without the indicated') what is meant by it is the related of the indicated, not the indicated itself; because the indicated, which is the request for delivery, is necessarily obtained by the miracle according to this view, because the miracle according to this view is an institution, and the institution is something by which its indicated is obtained. So what is here is the delivery of what they are commanded to deliver, which is the object of the request. For if they are not truthful, they have delivered other than what they were commanded to deliver. And an objection to this view is that the miracle occurs after the delivery, so it is not apparent that it indicates the request, and that would only be apparent if it preceded it. Decisions of the scholar Muhammad al-Albabi.
(His saying: 'And its conclusion is that all that issues from them... etc.') The utmost that can be derived from the author's saying 'because God commanded us to follow them... etc.' is that if, for example, fornication occurred from them, the forbidden would turn into obedience because we are commanded to follow them in it. And God does not command His servant except to obedience. So fornication would be obedience with respect to the commanded—i.e., the followers of the Prophet—so disobedience would have turned into obedience with respect to them as well. And the transformation of disobedience into obedience is impossible. Therefore, what leads to it is impossible, so the desired is established. And from this it is not derived that the forbidden, for example, turns into obedience with respect to the messengers, but rather with respect to the commanded. So the author's saying 'with respect to them' is not apparent.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage explains the proof (burhan) for the obligation of trustworthiness (wujub al-amanah) of the prophets. It is a conditional argument: if prophets were to commit a forbidden or disliked act (like treason or sin), then that act would become an act of obedience (ta'a) for them because God commands us to follow them in everything. But it is impossible for a forbidden act to be obedience, so the antecedent is false. Therefore, prophets are infallible and trustworthy. The commentary then discusses a nuance: the transformation of disobedience into obedience would occur in the followers, not in the prophets themselves. It also addresses an objection related to the institution view of miracles: if the miracle is an institution, it might be said that the indication exists without the indicated, but the response is that the miracle's function is to indicate the request for delivery, and the request is fulfilled by the miracle itself. However, an objection notes that the miracle occurs after the delivery, so it cannot indicate the request. The passage ends with a clarification that the proof shows that the sin would become obedience for the followers, not for the prophets, so the author's wording 'with respect to them' may need interpretation.

Misconception: The proof assumes prophets are sinless without reasoning.
Correction: It actually proves sinlessness by showing that sin would lead to contradiction, so sin is impossible.

Nuances of the Proof: Who Transforms? and the Timing of Miracles
Al-Bajuri explains that the transformation applies to followers and discusses an objection about miracles indicating the request.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the transformation of sin into obedience would apply to the followers, not the prophets themselves, and an objection regarding the timing of miracles.

Core Idea
The proof shows that sin would become obedience for followers; miracles must indicate the request before the act.

In this lesson, we examine two subtle points from the commentators. First, a clarification that the transformation of a forbidden act into obedience would occur for the followers, not the prophets. Second, an objection to the view that miracles are institutions: they occur after the delivery, so how can they indicate the request? Let's explore.

Guided Path
1
Read the passages
Read the two sections: the first about 'existence of indication without the indicated' and the second about 'the conclusion that all that issues from them...'
Focus on the nuance about who the obedience applies to.
2
Understand the first nuance
The commentator clarifies that the proof does not imply that the forbidden becomes obedience for the prophets, but for the followers who are commanded to follow them. The author's wording 'with respect to them' may be problematic.
This avoids a potential misinterpretation.
3
Analyze the objection about miracles
The second part discusses an objection: if the miracle is an institution, it indicates the request for delivery, but the miracle occurs after the delivery, so it cannot indicate the request. This challenges the view.
Consider the implications.
4
Evaluate the response
The text mentions a possible response but then gives a counter-objection. Understand the debate.
This shows the depth of kalam arguments.

(His saying: 'As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, may peace and blessings be upon them, it is because they... etc.') Its elaboration is that you say: If they betrayed by doing something forbidden or disliked, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience with respect to them, may peace and blessings be upon them. But the consequent is false, and when the consequent is false, the antecedent is false, so its opposite is established, which is the desired conclusion. So the author mentioned the conditional and omitted the exceptive because it is obvious, then he explained the aspect of the implication in the conditional by his saying: 'Because God Almighty commanded us to follow them... etc.' And its conclusion is that all that issues from them is not but commanded by God Almighty, and everything He commands is not but obedience, because He does not command indecency. Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ajhuri.
(And his saying: 'the existence of the indication') i.e., the indicator of that institution which is the miracle. (And his saying: 'without the indicated') what is meant by it is the related of the indicated, not the indicated itself; because the indicated, which is the request for delivery, is necessarily obtained by the miracle according to this view, because the miracle according to this view is an institution, and the institution is something by which its indicated is obtained. So what is here is the delivery of what they are commanded to deliver, which is the object of the request. For if they are not truthful, they have delivered other than what they were commanded to deliver. And an objection to this view is that the miracle occurs after the delivery, so it is not apparent that it indicates the request, and that would only be apparent if it preceded it. Decisions of the scholar Muhammad al-Albabi.
(His saying: 'And its conclusion is that all that issues from them... etc.') The utmost that can be derived from the author's saying 'because God commanded us to follow them... etc.' is that if, for example, fornication occurred from them, the forbidden would turn into obedience because we are commanded to follow them in it. And God does not command His servant except to obedience. So fornication would be obedience with respect to the commanded—i.e., the followers of the Prophet—so disobedience would have turned into obedience with respect to them as well. And the transformation of disobedience into obedience is impossible. Therefore, what leads to it is impossible, so the desired is established. And from this it is not derived that the forbidden, for example, turns into obedience with respect to the messengers, but rather with respect to the commanded. So the author's saying 'with respect to them' is not apparent.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage explains the proof (burhan) for the obligation of trustworthiness (wujub al-amanah) of the prophets. It is a conditional argument: if prophets were to commit a forbidden or disliked act (like treason or sin), then that act would become an act of obedience (ta'a) for them because God commands us to follow them in everything. But it is impossible for a forbidden act to be obedience, so the antecedent is false. Therefore, prophets are infallible and trustworthy. The commentary then discusses a nuance: the transformation of disobedience into obedience would occur in the followers, not in the prophets themselves. It also addresses an objection related to the institution view of miracles: if the miracle is an institution, it might be said that the indication exists without the indicated, but the response is that the miracle's function is to indicate the request for delivery, and the request is fulfilled by the miracle itself. However, an objection notes that the miracle occurs after the delivery, so it cannot indicate the request. The passage ends with a clarification that the proof shows that the sin would become obedience for the followers, not for the prophets, so the author's wording 'with respect to them' may need interpretation.

Correction: The transformation actually occurs for the followers, not the prophets themselves, as clarified by the text.

The Conditional Proof for Prophets' Trustworthiness
Bajuri expounds the conditional proof for the necessity of trustworthiness in prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the kalam proof that prophets must be trustworthy, including the conditional premise, the implication, and the clarification of its scope.

Core Idea
If prophets could betray, forbidden acts would become obedience—an impossibility.

This lesson unpacks a classic kalam argument for the necessity of prophets' trustworthiness. The proof uses a conditional (if-then) structure to show that any betrayal would lead to a logical contradiction. We will follow the author's reasoning step by step, from the initial conditional to the final clarification that the transformation applies to the followers, not the prophets themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how compact the proof is.
2
Identify the conditional premise
Find the 'if' part (the antecedent) and the 'then' part (the consequent) in the proof. The antecedent is 'if they betrayed' and the consequent is 'then a forbidden/disliked act would become obedience.'
The author mentions the conditional and omits the exceptive form for brevity.
3
Understand the implication (luzūm)
Focus on why the consequent follows from the antecedent: because Allah commanded us to follow them, so all their actions are commanded, and Allah only commands obedience. Thus any act from them must be obedience.
This is the key link in the argument.
4
See why the consequent is false
Recognize that it is impossible for a forbidden act to become obedience—that would be a contradiction. Therefore the consequent is false, so the antecedent is false, and its opposite (trustworthiness) is true.
This is the core logical move.
5
Note the clarification about the followers
The commentator clarifies that the transformation into obedience would apply only to the followers, not to the prophets themselves. This prevents a misunderstanding that the proof implies prophets could turn forbidden into obedience for themselves.
This subtlety is important for precise theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فَلِأَنَّهُمْ... إلخ) تقريرُهُ أن تقول: لو خانوا بفِعْل مُحَرَّم أو مكروه لانقلب المحرَّمُ أو المكروه طاعةً في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام، لكن التالي باطل، وإذا بَطَلَ التالي بَطَلَ المقدَّمُ، فثبت نقيضُه، وهو المطلوب. فالمصنف ذَكَرَ الشرطية، وحَذَفَ الاستثنائية لظهورها، ثم بَيَّنَ وجه اللزوم في الشرطية بقوله: (لأن الله تعالى أمرنا بالاقتداء بهم... إلخ). ومُحَصَّلُه أن جميع ما صَدَرَ عنهم لا يكون إلا مأموراً به من الله تعالى وكلّ ما أَمَرَ به لا يكون إلا طاعة؛ لأنه لا يأمر بالفحشاء. (قوله: وَمُحَصَّلُهُ : أَنَّ جَمِيعَ مَا صَدَرَ عَنْهُمْ... إلخ) غاية ما يُسْتَفَادُ من قول المصنف: لأن الله أمرنا بالاقتداء بهم... إلخ): أنه لو وقع منهم الزنا مثلاً، لانقلب المحرَّمُ طاعةً لكوننا مأمورين باتباعهم فيه، ولا يأمرُ الله عبده إلا بطاعة، فيكون الزنا في حق المأمورين - وهم أتباع النبي - طاعةً، فقد انْقَلَبَتِ المعصية في حق المأمورين طاعةً في حقهم أيضاً، وانقلاب المعصية طاعةً محال، فما أدى إليه محال، فثبت المطلوب، ولم يُسْتَقَد من هذا: انقلاب المحرم مثلاً طاعة في حق الرسل، بل في حق المأمورين، فقول المصنف: (في حقهم غير ظاهر
His saying: 'As for the proof of the necessity of trustworthiness for them, may blessings and peace be upon them, it is because they... etc.' Its exposition is that you say: If they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked act, that forbidden or disliked act would become obedience in their case, may blessings and peace be upon them. But the consequent is false. And if the consequent is false, the antecedent is false. So its opposite is established, and that is what is sought. The author mentioned the conditional, and omitted the exceptional [form] due to its obviousness. Then he explained the aspect of implication in the conditional by his saying: 'Because Allah, exalted be He, commanded us to follow them... etc.' And its conclusion is that everything that proceeds from them is only commanded by Allah, and everything He commands is only obedience, because He does not command indecency. (His saying: 'And its conclusion: that everything that proceeds from them... etc.') The utmost gained from the author's saying 'because Allah commanded us to follow them...' is that if adultery occurred from them, for example, the forbidden would become obedience because we are commanded to follow them in it, and Allah does not command His servant except to obedience. So adultery would be obedience for the commanded ones—who are the followers of the Prophet. Thus disobedience would be transformed into obedience for them as well. But the transformation of disobedience into obedience is impossible. So what leads to it is impossible, so what is sought is established. And from this it is not derived that the forbidden, for example, becomes obedience in the case of the messengers, but rather in the case of the followers. So the author's saying 'in their case' is not apparent.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents the proof (burhān) for the necessity of prophets being trustworthy (amāna). It is a conditional argument. The proof is structured as follows: If the prophets were to betray by committing a forbidden (ḥarām) or disliked (makrūh) act, then that act would become obedience (ṭā‘a) in their case, because Allah has commanded us to follow them, and whatever Allah commands is obedience. However, it is impossible for a forbidden or disliked act to become obedience, as that would entail a contradiction. Therefore, the premise that they could betray is false, and its opposite—that they are trustworthy—is established. The commentator clarifies that the author only stated the conditional premise and omitted the exceptive form for brevity. He then explains the connection (luzūm) in the conditional: Allah's command to follow the prophets implies that all their actions are commanded by Him, and since Allah never commands indecency (faḥshā'), their actions cannot be indecent. A further clarification is given: the transformation of the act into obedience applies to the followers, not to the prophets themselves. That is, if a prophet committed an act that is normally forbidden, the followers' imitation of it would make it obedience for them, but this does not imply it becomes obedience for the prophet. The objection that the author's phrase 'in their case' is unclear is noted.

أمانة
برهان
شرطية
طاعة
معصية
لزوم
اقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof shows that forbidden acts become obedience for the prophets themselves.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that the transformation applies only to the followers, not the prophets. If a prophet committed a forbidden act, it would be obedience for the followers who imitate him, but it does not become obedience for the prophet.

Checkpoint
What is the consequent (tālī) in the conditional proof for the prophets' trustworthiness?
A) The prophets are trustworthy.
B) A forbidden act becomes obedience in their case.
C) Allah commands indecency.
D) The prophets never betray.

Key Takeaway
The trustworthiness of prophets is proven by the impossibility of their betraying, as that would entail a logical contradiction in divine commands.

The Pronoun Reference in the Command to Follow Prophets
Al-Bajuri clarifies the pronoun reference in the command to follow prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how grammatical analysis of a single pronoun can have significant theological implications, specifically in interpreting the command to follow prophets and the role of previous scriptures.

Core Idea
Pronoun reference can determine whether a command is universal or specific.

This lesson examines a key passage from al-Bajuri's commentary where he clarifies the pronoun 'us' in the verse 'Allah commanded us to follow them.' At first glance, one might think it refers only to Muslims. But al-Bajuri argues it refers to all nations, with an important exception from the Maliki school. This finer point reveals how grammatical analysis intersects with theology and legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, noting the pronouns and their references. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the implicit and explicit pronouns.
2
Identify the main claim
Al-Bajuri states that the pronoun 'us' refers to all nations, not just the Islamic ummah. Find the reasoning he provides.
3
Understand the exception
The passage mentions an exception based on the Maliki view of 'shar' man qablana'. Consider why this matters and why the Shafi'is consider it weak.
This shows how different schools of thought affect interpretation.
4
Reflect on the distributive interpretation
Al-Bajuri concludes that the command is distributive: each nation follows its own prophet. How does this resolve the issue?
This avoids the problem of one nation being commanded to follow another's prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: لأنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَمَرَنَا بِالْاِقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ... إلخ) من المعلوم أن الضمير المستتر عائد الله تعالى والبارز عائد لجميع الأمم، لا لهذه الأمة فقط، وإلا لم يَصِحْ قوله: (بالاقتداء بهم... إلخ)؛ لأن هذه الأمة لا يَلْزَمُها الاقتداء بغيره كعيسى وموسى، إلا أن يقال: إنه مبني على أن شَرْعَ من قبلنا شَرْع لنا فيما لم يَرِدْ نبينا فيه شيء كما هو مذهبُ السادَةِ المالكية الذين منهم المصنف، وهو قول ضعيف عند الشافعية، وعلى الأول؛ فكلُّ أمةٍ مأمورة بالاقتداء برسولها، فهو على سبيل التوزيع.
(His saying: 'Because Allah, exalted be He, commanded us to follow them... etc.') It is known that the implicit pronoun refers to Allah, exalted be He, and the explicit pronoun refers to all nations, not only this ummah. Otherwise, his saying 'to follow them' would not be correct, because this ummah is not obliged to follow others like Jesus and Moses, unless it is said that it is based on the view that the law of those before us is law for us in matters where our prophet has not brought anything—as is the school of the Malikis, among whom is the author—and that is a weak opinion among the Shafi'is. On the first interpretation, every nation is commanded to follow its own messenger, so it is on a distributive basis.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and theological clarification of the phrase 'Allah commanded us to follow them.' The commentator explains that the pronoun 'us' (nā) in the Arabic refers to all nations collectively ('all nations'), not exclusively to the Islamic ummah. If it were only for this ummah, then the command to follow prophets like Jesus and Moses would not apply, since this ummah is not obligated to follow previous prophets directly. However, he notes an exception: according to the Maliki school (to which the author al-Sanusi belongs), the laws of previous prophets are binding on us if our Prophet has not legislated on the matter—but this is considered a weak position by the Shafi'is. The more apparent interpretation is distributive: each nation is commanded to follow its own prophet.

ضمير
أمة
اقتداء
شرع من قبلنا
توزيع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The pronoun 'us' in the command to follow prophets refers exclusively to the Islamic ummah.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that it refers to all nations, with a distributive meaning: each nation follows its own prophet.

Checkpoint

A) Only the Islamic ummah.
B) All nations.
C) The Companions of the Prophet.
D) The scholars.

Key Takeaway
The pronoun 'us' in the command to follow prophets refers to all nations, not just Muslims, and is interpreted distributively unless one adopts the Maliki view on the binding nature of previous scriptures.

Following the Prophet: Scope and Specificities
Bajuri defines the scope of following prophets and excludes their unique characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that believers must follow the Prophet in all words, deeds, and tacit approvals, except for matters proven to be specific to him (khuṣūṣiyyāt).

Core Idea
Follow the Prophet in everything unless a specificity is proven.

Bajuri explains the comprehensive scope of following the Prophet. It includes not just explicit statements and actions but also his tacit approvals. The default is to follow, unless a matter is clearly established as unique to the Prophet. This principle is rooted in the Quranic command of obedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice how Bajuri defines the scope of following.
The passage concludes with a Quranic proof.
2
Identify the categories of following
The passage mentions words (aqwal), deeds (af‘al), and tacit approvals (taqrirat). Understand that silence on an action counts as approval because prophets are protected from error.
Taqrirat are often overlooked.
3
Understand the exception of specificities
Specificities (khuṣūṣiyyāt) are matters unique to the Prophet, like marrying more than four wives. These are not binding on the community. The default is to follow unless specificity is proven.
This prevents unnecessary hesitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ أي وتقريراتهم وسكوتهم على الفعل؛ إذ لا يُقَرُّون على خطأ، ويُستثنى من ذلك ما ثَبَتَتْ خصوصيته بهم، كنكاح ما زَادَ على الأربع، ويُعْلَمُ من ذلك أنه ليس للمكلف منا أن يتوقف في فعل شيءٍ مما ثَبَتَ عنه لاحتمال الخصوصية، بل يَتْبَعُهُ في جميع أقواله وأفعاله إلا ما ثَبَتَ أنه من خصوصياته؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: ﴿ قُل إن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي )
(His saying: 'in their words and deeds' means their tacit approvals and their silence regarding an action, for they are not confirmed upon error. And from that is excepted whatever is established as specific to them, such as marrying more than four. And from this it is known that the responsible person among us should not hesitate in doing anything that is established from him due to the possibility of specificity; rather, he follows him in all his words and deeds except what is established as being among his specificities, due to the generality of Allah's saying: 'Say: If you love Allah, then follow me.')
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage explains the extent to which believers must follow the prophet. It covers not only explicit statements (aqwāl) and actions (af‘āl) but also tacit approvals (taqrīrāt) and silence (sukūt) regarding an action, because prophets are not confirmed in error. However, there are exceptions: matters proven to be specific to the prophet (khuṣūṣiyyāt), such as marrying more than four wives, are not binding on the community. The principle derived is that a believer should not refrain from following an established action of the prophet out of suspicion that it might be a specificity; rather, one should follow unless a specificity is clearly proven. This is supported by the general command in the Quran: 'Say: If you love Allah, then follow me.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any unusual action of the Prophet must be specific to him and not binding.
Correction: The default is to follow; specificity must be explicitly established before exemption.

Checkpoint
What is the general rule regarding following the prophet's actions according to this passage?
A) Follow only his words, not his deeds.
B) Follow everything except what is proven to be a specificity.
C) Follow nothing unless explicitly commanded.
D) Follow only actions that are obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The default in following the Prophet is comprehensive, covering all his words, deeds, and tacit approvals, unless a specificity is proven.

Objection on the Proof and the Revised Formulation
Al-Shaktani and al-Dasuqi raise an objection of circularity and propose a clearer formulation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection of circularity raised against the proof for trustworthiness and the revised formulation that avoids it by appealing to the impossibility of a single act being both obedience and disobedience.

Core Idea
A proof must not presuppose what it tries to prove, and a revised formulation avoids circularity by focusing on logical contradiction.

In theological arguments, objections often reveal hidden assumptions. The proof for prophetic trustworthiness faced a challenge: it seemed to assume the very infallibility it aimed to establish. This objection, raised by al-Shaktani and al-Dasuqi, led to a refined formulation that rests on the impossibility of a single act being both obedience and disobedience.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial proof and the circularity objection
First, recall the proof that prophets are trustworthy because they are commanded to be followed, making their actions obedience. The objection says this assumes their infallibility (ʿiṣma) to conclude that their actions are obedience, creating a circular argument (dawr).
Circularity occurs when the conclusion is used as a premise.
2
Grasp the second objection about transformation
The second objection argues that even if a forbidden act becomes obedience, that transformation is not harmful. What is truly impossible is the transformation of the essential nature of an act (e.g., obligatory becoming permissible). This objection refines the issue.
The commentator suggests focusing on the impossibility of two opposites coexisting.
3
See the revised formulation using contradiction
The revised formulation states: if prophets betrayed by a forbidden act, that single act would be both obedience (because commanded) and not obedience (because it is betrayal). This combination of two opposites (naqīḍān) is impossible, so the proof holds without circularity.
This avoids the assumption of infallibility at the outset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال: إن أَمْرَنا بالاقتداء بهم في أفعالهم مثلاً يقتضي بحسب العادة: أن المقتدى فيه مرغوب فيه ومحبوب للأمر بالنسبة للمقتدي والمقتدى به، فيكون طاعةً في حق كلّ منهما، فصح قول المصنف: (في حقهم، إلا أنه ليس بقيد، وفي الشكتاني: أنه لا يلزم ما ذُكِرَ من انقلاب المحرَّم أو المكروه طاعةً في حقهم إلا بعد ثبوت عصمتهم التي الكلام فيها حتى تكون أفعالهم طاعةً دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب، وهذا موجب للدَّوْرِ، فلا يصح قوله: في حقهم .اهـ. وتبعه الدسوقي ويَرِدُ على هذا الدليل أيضاً: أن انقلاب المحرَّم أو المكروه طاعةً لا يَضُرُّ؛ إذ المُضِرُّ إنما هو انقلاب حقيقة الواجب إلى الجائز أو المستحيل أو كلّ منهما إلى الواجب أو الجائز، مستحيلاً أو بالعكس كما تقدم للمحشِي، فكان الأظهرُ أن يقول: لو خانوا بفعل محرم أو مكروه لاجتمع النقيضان أي كونُ الشيء طاعةً وغير طاعةً؛ لأن الله تعالى... إلخ
And it may be said: Our being commanded to follow them in their actions, for example, implies customarily that the thing followed is desired and loved due to the command, both for the follower and the one followed. So it is obedience in the case of each. Thus the author's saying 'in their case' is correct, except that it is not a restriction. And in al-Shaktani: What was mentioned of the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience in their case does not follow except after establishing their infallibility, which is what is under discussion, such that their actions are obedience ranging between obligatory and recommended. This leads to circularity, so his saying 'in their case' is not valid. End quote. Al-Dasuqi followed him. And an objection is also raised against this proof: that the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience is not harmful; rather, what is harmful is the transformation of the reality of the obligatory into the permissible or impossible, or each of them into the obligatory or permissible, being impossible or vice versa, as the commentator previously mentioned. So the more apparent is to say: If they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked act, then two opposites would combine, i.e., the thing being obedience and not obedience, because Allah... etc.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents objections raised by later commentators (al-Shaktani and al-Dasuqi) against the proof for trustworthiness. The first objection is that the argument presupposes the prophets' infallibility ('iṣma) to conclude that their actions are obedience, making the proof circular (dawr). The second objection, attributed to al-Shaktani and al-Dasuqi, argues that the transformation of a forbidden act into obedience is not intrinsically harmful; what is truly impossible is the transformation of the essential nature of an act (e.g., the obligatory becoming permissible or impossible). The commentator suggests that to avoid this, the proof should be reformulated as a contradiction of two opposites: if the prophets betrayed, a single act would be both obedience and not obedience, which is impossible. This revised formulation is more robust because it does not rely on the transformation of categories but on the logical impossibility of two contradictory properties co-existing in one action.

Key Terms
عصمة
دور
انقلاب
نقيضان
طاعة
معصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the objection refutes the proof entirely.
Correction: The objection does not refute the proof; it refines it to avoid circularity and clarifies the logical impossibility involved. The revised formulation shows that the proof still holds when correctly expressed.

Checkpoint
What is the core of the revised formulation proposed in this passage?
A) The prophets never commit any act.
B) If prophets betrayed, a single act would be both obedience and disobedience.
C) The forbidden can become recommended.
D) The proof is invalid and should be discarded.

Key Takeaway
The proof for trustworthiness is refined to avoid circularity by showing that betrayal would lead to a logical contradiction (obedience and disobedience simultaneously), which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about Allah or His prophets that you accepted simply because 'that's what I was taught'—without examining whether your reasoning is circular? Will you now seek clear, non-circular proofs from the Qur'an and Sunnah?
?
If logical contradiction is impossible for Allah’s prophets, what about the consistency of your own actions? Are there areas where you claim to follow the Prophet but your deeds contradict that claim? How will you resolve that today?
?
When you face doubts about the reliability of prophetic teachings, do you run from logical scrutiny or embrace it? Will you commit to testing your faith with the same rigor the scholars used, trusting that truth can withstand examination?

The Objection of Transforming Forbidden Acts into Obedience
Sanusi presents and refutes the transformation objection with circularity and attribute distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection that following prophets would transform forbidden acts into obedience leads to circular reasoning and how the attribute vs essence distinction resolves it.

Core Idea
Following prophets adds an attribute of obedience without altering an act's essential ruling.

A common objection to the necessity of following prophets is that if we are commanded to follow them in all actions, even their forbidden acts would become acts of obedience, which is absurd. In this lesson, we examine this objection and the scholarly responses, including the problem of circularity and the distinction between essential and accidental attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial response
Read the passage from the beginning through al-Shakani's criticism. Notice how the objection assumes that following requires the act to be desirable, and how al-Shakani points out the circularity of needing sinlessness.
The objection is based on customary reasoning about command and desirability.
2
Understand the circularity problem
Al-Shakani argues that the objection only works if the prophet's sinlessness is already established, but that is precisely what is being debated. This creates a vicious circle (دور).
3
See the attribute vs essence clarification
The passage clarifies that when Sanusi says 'forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience', he means it acquires an additional attribute of obedience, not that its original ruling changes. This resolves the objection without logical contradiction.
The transformation is not a change in essence but an addition of a new attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال: إن أَمْرَنا بالاقتداء بهم في أفعالهم مثلاً يقتضي بحسب العادة: أن المقتدى فيه مرغوب فيه ومحبوب للأمر بالنسبة للمقتدي والمقتدى به، فيكون طاعةً في حق كلّ منهما، فصح قول المصنف: (في حقهم، إلا أنه ليس بقيد، وفي الشكتاني: أنه لا يلزم ما ذُكِرَ من انقلاب المحرَّم أو المكروه طاعةً في حقهم إلا بعد ثبوت عصمتهم التي الكلام فيها حتى تكون أفعالهم طاعةً دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب، وهذا موجب للدَّوْرِ، فلا يصح قوله: في حقهم .اهـ. وتبعه الدسوقي ويَرِدُ على هذا الدليل أيضاً: أن انقلاب المحرَّم أو المكروه طاعةً لا يَضُرُّ؛ إذ المُضِرُّ إنما هو انقلاب حقيقة الواجب إلى الجائز أو المستحيل أو كلّ منهما إلى الواجب أو الجائز، مستحيلاً أو بالعكس كما تقدم للمحشِي، فكان الأظهرُ أن يقول: لو خانوا بفعل محرم أو مكروه لاجتمع النقيضان أي كونُ الشيء طاعةً وغير طاعةً؛ لأن الله تعالى... إلخ، إلا أن يقال: إن مراده بقوله: (لانقلب المحرم أو المكروه طاعة): أنه يتَّصِفُ بكونه طاعةً زيادة على ما اتصف به من الحرمة أو الكراهة، فيُرْجِعُ لما قلنا. ويَرِدُ على هذا الدليل أيضاً: أنهم إذا خانوا بفعل مُحَرَّم أو مكروه؛ فلا يخلو الحال؛ إما أن يكون ذلك بعد تبليغهم حُكْمَ هذا الفعل أو لا، فإن كان بعد تبليغهم لحكمه؛ لم يَلْزَمِ المكلف حينئذ اتباعُهم فيه، كيف وقد أخبروا بالنهي عنه إن لم يحتمل النسخ؟ وإن احتمل النسخ، لَزِمَهُ اتباعُهم، وكان نسخاً للحكم السابق، فلم يلزم المحذور، وإن كان قبل تبليغهم بأن كتموا الحكم عن الخلق كان إبطال الكتمان كافياً عن إبطال الخيانة. ويجاب باختيار الأول. ودُفعَ ما وَرَدَ عليه بأنا مأمورون باتباعهم في جميع الأقوال والأفعال عموماً كما دل عليه الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، ما عدا ما ثَبَتَ اختصاصهم به، وما عدا الأمور الجبلية كالقيام والقعود والمشي، فإنا لم نُؤْمَرُ بالاتباع فيها، ومن الآيات الدالة على الإتباع قوله تعالى في حق نبينا قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللهُ ) (١) وَاتَّبِعُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَهْتَدُونَ ) () (وَرَحْمَتِي وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ الزَّكَوةَ وَالَّذِينَ هُم بِايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِي الأمن . وأورد على هذا الدليل غير ذلك.
And it may be said: Indeed, our command to follow them in their actions, for example, necessitates according to custom that the followed thing is desirable and beloved because of the command for the follower and the followed, so it becomes an act of obedience in respect of each of them. So the author's saying: (in their respect) is correct, except that it is not a restriction. And in al-Shakani: that what was mentioned of the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience in their respect is not necessary except after establishing their sinlessness, which is under discussion, until their actions become obedience that circles between obligatory and recommended. And this leads to a vicious circle, so his saying: 'in their respect' is not valid. End quote. And al-Dasuqi followed him. And it is also objected to this proof: that the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience does no harm; for the harmful is only the transformation of the essence of the obligatory into the permissible or impossible, or each of them into the obligatory or permissible, impossible or vice versa, as the commentator mentioned. So it would be more apparent for him to say: if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked action, the two contradictories would gather, i.e., a thing being obedience and not obedience; because Allah Almighty... etc. Except that it may be said: that his intention by his saying: (so the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience) is that it becomes characterized as obedience in addition to what it was characterized by of prohibition or dislike, so it returns to what we said. And it is also objected to this proof: that if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked action, then the situation is not free; either that was after they conveyed the ruling of this action or not. If it was after they conveyed its ruling, then the obligated one is not then obliged to follow them in it, how can he when they have informed of the prohibition of it if it does not allow abrogation? And if it allows abrogation, then following them is necessary, and it would be an abrogation of the previous ruling, so the problematic does not follow. And if it was before they conveyed it, by their hiding the ruling from the creation, then nullifying the hiding is sufficient for nullifying the betrayal. And it is answered by choosing the first. And what was objected to it is refuted by that we are commanded to follow them in all words and actions generally as the Book, Sunnah, and consensus indicate, except what is established to be specific to them, and except natural matters like standing, sitting, and walking, for we are not commanded to follow in them. And among the verses indicating following are His saying regarding our prophet: {Say: if you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you} (1) and {Follow him that you may be guided} () and {My mercy encompasses all things, so I will prescribe it for those who fear and give zakah and those who believe in our verses, those who follow the messenger, the unlettered prophet}... and other things were objected to this proof.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and refutations regarding the proof that prophets are followed in all actions. It begins with an objection: if we are commanded to follow them, their actions become desirable and thus acts of obedience for both the prophet and follower. Al-Shakani points out this reasoning is circular because it assumes the prophet's sinlessness, which is exactly what is being debated. Al-Dasuqi follows. Another objection says that transforming a forbidden act into obedience is not harmful; only transforming the essence of an obligation into something else is harmful. The author (Sanusi) apparently intended to say that if prophets were to betray, it would lead to a contradiction (a thing being both obedience and not obedience). Then a clarification: the intended meaning is that the act acquires an additional attribute of obedience, not that it loses its original ruling. A further objection considers the timing: if prophets committed a forbidden act after conveying its prohibition, following them is not required; if before, they hid the ruling. The answer chooses the first scenario (after conveying). Then a defense: the general command to follow them is based on Book, Sunnah, and consensus, except for specifics and natural actions. Verses are cited as evidence. Then it notes that other objections were raised to this proof.

Key Terms
انقلاب
عصمة
دور
نقيضان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the objection about turning forbidden acts into obedience is fatal and shows following prophets is impossible.
Correction: The refutation shows it only adds an attribute of obedience, not a change in essence, so no contradiction arises.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main problem with the objection that following a prophet would make his forbidden act an obedience?
A) It requires the prophet to be sinless, causing circularity
B) It assumes transformation of essence is impossible
C) It contradicts the Quran
D) It leads to infinite regress

Key Takeaway
The transformation objection fails because it confuses adding an attribute of obedience with changing the essence of the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you follow the Prophet (peace be upon him) in an action that you might otherwise consider worldly or even disliked, do you ever feel that you are merely performing an external act? This lesson teaches that obedience adds a quality to the action. Are you conscious of that added quality when you follow the Sunnah? Will you strive from now on to intend that quality?
?
This passage discusses the necessity of sinlessness for prophets. How does your belief in the sinlessness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) affect your trust in his guidance? Do you follow his commands with the certainty that they are always right, or do you sometimes doubt? Ask yourself: Is there an area of your life where you haven't fully submitted to the prophetic model because of personal preference? What step will you take to align with it?

The Timing Objection and the Command to Follow Prophets
Sanusi addresses the timing objection and defends the general command to follow prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection about prophets betraying after or before conveying rulings and the refutation based on the general command to follow them.

Core Idea
The general command to follow prophets covers all actions except specifics and natural acts.

Another objection to following prophets is that if they commit a forbidden act after conveying its prohibition, following them would be contradictory. Alternatively, if they did so before conveying, they would have hidden the ruling. This lesson examines both scenarios and the answer given by scholars, which affirms the general command to follow them.

Guided Path
1
Read the timing objection scenarios
Read the passage from 'يَرِدُ على هذا الدليل أيضاً' through the two scenarios (after or before conveying). Notice how each scenario leads to a potential problem.
The objection assumes that betrayal by a prophet is possible.
2
Understand the answer choosing the first scenario
The answer selects the first scenario (betrayal after conveying). In that case, if abrogation is possible, following is allowed; if not, following is not required. But the defense then shows that we are commanded to follow generally.
The passage says 'ويجاب باختيار الأول' – the first scenario is chosen.
3
See the general command defense
The refutation states that we are commanded to follow prophets in all words and actions according to Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, except what is specific to them or natural actions like standing and sitting. This provides a positive basis for following.
Verses from the Quran are cited as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال: إن أَمْرَنا بالاقتداء بهم في أفعالهم مثلاً يقتضي بحسب العادة: أن المقتدى فيه مرغوب فيه ومحبوب للأمر بالنسبة للمقتدي والمقتدى به، فيكون طاعةً في حق كلّ منهما، فصح قول المصنف: (في حقهم، إلا أنه ليس بقيد، وفي الشكتاني: أنه لا يلزم ما ذُكِرَ من انقلاب المحرَّم أو المكروه طاعةً في حقهم إلا بعد ثبوت عصمتهم التي الكلام فيها حتى تكون أفعالهم طاعةً دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب، وهذا موجب للدَّوْرِ، فلا يصح قوله: في حقهم .اهـ. وتبعه الدسوقي ويَرِدُ على هذا الدليل أيضاً: أن انقلاب المحرَّم أو المكروه طاعةً لا يَضُرُّ؛ إذ المُضِرُّ إنما هو انقلاب حقيقة الواجب إلى الجائز أو المستحيل أو كلّ منهما إلى الواجب أو الجائز، مستحيلاً أو بالعكس كما تقدم للمحشِي، فكان الأظهرُ أن يقول: لو خانوا بفعل محرم أو مكروه لاجتمع النقيضان أي كونُ الشيء طاعةً وغير طاعةً؛ لأن الله تعالى... إلخ، إلا أن يقال: إن مراده بقوله: (لانقلب المحرم أو المكروه طاعة): أنه يتَّصِفُ بكونه طاعةً زيادة على ما اتصف به من الحرمة أو الكراهة، فيُرْجِعُ لما قلنا. ويَرِدُ على هذا الدليل أيضاً: أنهم إذا خانوا بفعل مُحَرَّم أو مكروه؛ فلا يخلو الحال؛ إما أن يكون ذلك بعد تبليغهم حُكْمَ هذا الفعل أو لا، فإن كان بعد تبليغهم لحكمه؛ لم يَلْزَمِ المكلف حينئذ اتباعُهم فيه، كيف وقد أخبروا بالنهي عنه إن لم يحتمل النسخ؟ وإن احتمل النسخ، لَزِمَهُ اتباعُهم، وكان نسخاً للحكم السابق، فلم يلزم المحذور، وإن كان قبل تبليغهم بأن كتموا الحكم عن الخلق كان إبطال الكتمان كافياً عن إبطال الخيانة. ويجاب باختيار الأول. ودُفعَ ما وَرَدَ عليه بأنا مأمورون باتباعهم في جميع الأقوال والأفعال عموماً كما دل عليه الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، ما عدا ما ثَبَتَ اختصاصهم به، وما عدا الأمور الجبلية كالقيام والقعود والمشي، فإنا لم نُؤْمَرُ بالاتباع فيها، ومن الآيات الدالة على الإتباع قوله تعالى في حق نبينا قُلْ إِن كُنتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللهُ ) (١) وَاتَّبِعُوهُ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَهْتَدُونَ ) () (وَرَحْمَتِي وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ الزَّكَوةَ وَالَّذِينَ هُم بِايَتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِي الأمن . وأورد على هذا الدليل غير ذلك.
And it may be said: Indeed, our command to follow them in their actions, for example, necessitates according to custom that the followed thing is desirable and beloved because of the command for the follower and the followed, so it becomes an act of obedience in respect of each of them. So the author's saying: (in their respect) is correct, except that it is not a restriction. And in al-Shakani: that what was mentioned of the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience in their respect is not necessary except after establishing their sinlessness, which is under discussion, until their actions become obedience that circles between obligatory and recommended. And this leads to a vicious circle, so his saying: 'in their respect' is not valid. End quote. And al-Dasuqi followed him. And it is also objected to this proof: that the transformation of the forbidden or disliked into obedience does no harm; for the harmful is only the transformation of the essence of the obligatory into the permissible or impossible, or each of them into the obligatory or permissible, impossible or vice versa, as the commentator mentioned. So it would be more apparent for him to say: if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked action, the two contradictories would gather, i.e., a thing being obedience and not obedience; because Allah Almighty... etc. Except that it may be said: that his intention by his saying: (so the forbidden or disliked would turn into obedience) is that it becomes characterized as obedience in addition to what it was characterized by of prohibition or dislike, so it returns to what we said. And it is also objected to this proof: that if they betrayed by a forbidden or disliked action, then the situation is not free; either that was after they conveyed the ruling of this action or not. If it was after they conveyed its ruling, then the obligated one is not then obliged to follow them in it, how can he when they have informed of the prohibition of it if it does not allow abrogation? And if it allows abrogation, then following them is necessary, and it would be an abrogation of the previous ruling, so the problematic does not follow. And if it was before they conveyed it, by their hiding the ruling from the creation, then nullifying the hiding is sufficient for nullifying the betrayal. And it is answered by choosing the first. And what was objected to it is refuted by that we are commanded to follow them in all words and actions generally as the Book, Sunnah, and consensus indicate, except what is established to be specific to them, and except natural matters like standing, sitting, and walking, for we are not commanded to follow in them. And among the verses indicating following are His saying regarding our prophet: {Say: if you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you} (1) and {Follow him that you may be guided} () and {My mercy encompasses all things, so I will prescribe it for those who fear and give zakah and those who believe in our verses, those who follow the messenger, the unlettered prophet}... and other things were objected to this proof.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and refutations regarding the proof that prophets are followed in all actions. It begins with an objection: if we are commanded to follow them, their actions become desirable and thus acts of obedience for both the prophet and follower. Al-Shakani points out this reasoning is circular because it assumes the prophet's sinlessness, which is exactly what is being debated. Al-Dasuqi follows. Another objection says that transforming a forbidden act into obedience is not harmful; only transforming the essence of an obligation into something else is harmful. The author (Sanusi) apparently intended to say that if prophets were to betray, it would lead to a contradiction (a thing being both obedience and not obedience). Then a clarification: the intended meaning is that the act acquires an additional attribute of obedience, not that it loses its original ruling. A further objection considers the timing: if prophets committed a forbidden act after conveying its prohibition, following them is not required; if before, they hid the ruling. The answer chooses the first scenario (after conveying). Then a defense: the general command to follow them is based on Book, Sunnah, and consensus, except for specifics and natural actions. Verses are cited as evidence. Then it notes that other objections were raised to this proof.

نسخ
تبليغ
اتباع

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the refutation of the timing objection?
A) The prophets are sinless
B) The general command to follow prophets from Quran, Sunnah, and consensus
C) The impossibility of abrogation
D) The prohibition of following in natural actions

Key Takeaway
The command to follow prophets is general, covering all actions except those specific to them or natural acts like standing and sitting.

Alternative Proof of Prophetic Truthfulness
Sanusi proposes an alternative proof for prophetic truthfulness using God's truthful reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand an alternative proof for prophetic truthfulness that is grounded in God's own truthfulness and avoids circular reasoning.

Core Idea
Prophetic truthfulness is proven because God's report about them must be true.

Sanusi presents a refined proof for why prophets must be truthful. Instead of relying solely on miracles, this proof starts from the certainty that God's own reports are true. Since God has informed us that prophets are truthful conveyors, any failure on their part would imply a deficiency in God, which is impossible. This passage shows how the miracle then serves as evidence for the necessary attributes of prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Note that this is a proposed reformulation of the standard proof.
2
Understand the logical structure
Identify the conditional chain: if prophets were not truthful, then God's report would be a lie; but lying is impossible for God; therefore, prophets must be truthful.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Identify the three required attributes
The passage concludes that truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance are necessary for prophets. The miracle (mu'jiza) is evidence for these three.
4
Reflect on why this proof is considered an improvement
Consider why starting from God's truthfulness makes the proof more direct and avoids reliance on external evidence.
This proof is more foundational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة فلو غَيْرَ المصنف هذه العبارة وقال: أما برهان وجوب الصدق؛ فهو أنهم لو لم يصدقوا للزم الكذبُ في خبره تعالى التنزيلي، والكَذِبُ نَقص، والنقص عليه تعالى محال، ويلزم من ذلك ثبوتُ الأمانة والتبليغ وذلك أنهم أخبروا أنهم مبلغون معصومون، فلو كانوا كاتمين أو خائنين؛ لما صَدَقَ ،خبرهم ولو لم يَصْدُقُ خبرهم؛ للزم الكَذِبُ في خبر الله تعالى التنزيلي، وكَذِبُه ،محال، فما أدى إليه من عدم صدق خبرهم محال، فما أدى إليه من الكتمان أو الخيانة محال ، لأجادَ ووفى بالمراد، وحينئذ تكون المعجزة دليل الأمور الثالثة الواجبة في حق الرسل.
And in sum, if the author changed this expression and said: As for the proof of the necessity of truthfulness, it is that if they did not speak truth, then lying would be necessary in God's revealed report, and lying is a deficiency, and deficiency upon Him is impossible, and from that follows the establishment of trustworthiness and conveyance. And that is because they reported that they are conveyors and sinless, so if they were concealers or betrayers, their report would not be true; and if their report were not true, then lying would be necessary in God's revealed report, and His lying is impossible. So what leads to their report not being true is impossible, so what leads to it of concealment or betrayal is impossible. So he would have done well and fulfilled the intent, and then the miracle would be evidence of the three necessary matters in respect of the messengers.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a proposed reformulation of the proof of prophetic truthfulness. The commentator suggests that the author should rephrase the argument as follows: The proof of the necessity of truthfulness (sidq) for prophets is that if they were not truthful, it would imply lying in God's report about them, because God reports that they are conveyors and sinless. Lying is a deficiency, impossible for God. Therefore, their concealment or betrayal is impossible. This proof links truthfulness to God's own truthfulness. The miracle (mu'jiza) then serves as evidence for the three necessary matters (truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance) regarding prophets.

Key Terms
