The Wisdom of Drawing Attention to the World's Lowliness
Sanusi explains that showing afflictions alerts others to the world's worthlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how afflictions serve as divine signals that expose the world's real worthlessness, encouraging detachment and redirecting hearts toward the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Afflictions are divine signals that expose the world's real worthlessness.

Sanusi now presents the fourth wisdom behind afflictions: they are not merely punishments or tests, but powerful reminders. When believers see the righteous turn away from worldly enjoyment as one would avoid a carcass, they recognize the world's true insignificance before Allah. This lesson unpacks that lesson through Quranic and prophetic citations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's words set the stage before diving into analysis.
2
Understand 'tanbih' as a wisdom
Identify how Sanusi defines 'tanbih' (drawing attention) and its role as a fourth purpose of afflictions. Note that it targets observers, not the afflicted.
This is a key distinction: the wisdom benefits those who witness the afflictions.
3
Examine the three scriptural proofs
List the three proofs: the world as a foul carcass, the gnat's wing tradition, and the 'stranger/passerby' instruction. Reflect on how each reinforces the lowliness of the world.
Pay special attention to the contrast between a 'stranger' and a 'passerby' in the commentary.
4
Reflect on the commentary's elaboration
The commentator describes the stranger's longing for home and the passerby's urgency. Consider how this imagery deepens the lesson of detachment.
The marginal note links this wisdom to the previous one about consolation.
5
Internalize the applied lesson
Ask yourself: How can seeing others' detachment from worldly goods shift your own priorities? This wisdom is meant to transform hearts.
This connects the theoretical to personal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: أَوِ لِلتَّنْبِيهِ لِخِسَةِ قَدْرِهَا عِنْدَ اللهِ تَعَالَى :أي: تنبيه غيرهم لحقارة قدرها عنده تعالى، وذلك لأنه إذا رآهم مُغرضين عنها إعراضَ العاقل عن الجيفة؛ تنبه وتيقظ لحقارة قدرها عند الله تعالى، ولذلك قال الله: «الدُّنْيَا جيفَةٌ قَذِرَةٌ). وقال : «لَوْ كَانَتِ الدُّنْيَا تَزِنُ عِنْدَ اللهِ جَنَاحَ بَعُوضَةٍ مَا سَقَى الْكَافِرَ مِنْهَا جَرْعَةَ مَاءٍ ). وقال الله خطاباً لابن عمر - والمراد ما يعمه وغيره -: «كُنْ فِي الدُّنْيَا كَأَنَّكَ غَرِيبٌ أَوْ عَابِرُ سَبِيلِ» (۳)، زاد الترمذي: «وَعْدَّ نَفْسَكَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُبُورِ»، والغريبُ: هو الذي قَدِمَ بلداً لا مَسْكَنَ له فيها ولا أهل فقاسى الذل والمسكنة في غربته، وتعلَّقَ قلبه بالرجوع إلى وطنه ولما كان الغريب قد يقيم في بلاد الغربة أضرب عنه بقوله: أو عابر سبيل أي بل كُنْ مثل المارّ في الطريق لأجل أن يصل إلى وطنه وبينه وبينه مفاوِزُ ومهالك، فهل له أن يُقيم لحظة؟ حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري (قوله: أَوْ لِلتَّنْبِيهِ) هو والتسلي عن الدنيا مرتبان على قلة المال ونحوها من الأمور الشاقة.
(His saying: 'or for drawing attention to the lowliness of its worth with Allah Most High') i.e., drawing the attention of others to the contemptibility of its worth with Him Most High. That is because when they see them turning away from it like the turn of a sensible person from a carcass, they become attentive and alert to the contemptibility of its worth with Allah Most High. Therefore Allah said: 'The world is a foul carcass.' And He said: 'If the world weighed with Allah the wing of a gnat, He would not give a disbeliever from it a sip of water.' And Allah said, addressing Ibn Umar – and what is meant is that which encompasses him and others – : 'Be in this world as if you are a stranger or a passerby.' Al-Tirmidhi added: 'And count yourself among the inhabitants of the graves.' The stranger (gharib) is one who comes to a land where he has no home nor family, so he endures humiliation and misery in his alienation, and his heart is attached to returning to his homeland. And since the stranger may stay in the land of alienation, He turned away from that by His saying: 'or a passerby' – i.e., rather be like the traveller on the road, in order to reach his homeland, and between him and it are deserts and dangers, so can he stay for a moment? Gloss of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri: (His saying: 'or for drawing attention') this and the consolation from the world are both based on lack of wealth and similar burdensome matters.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage expounds the fourth wisdom: drawing attention to the lowliness of the world (al-tanbih li-khisat qadriha). It explains that when people see the elect of Allah turning away from worldly goods as a sensible person turns away from a filthy carcass, they become alert to the world's worthlessness before Allah. Three scriptural proofs are cited: (1) 'The world is a foul carcass' (a hadith), (2) 'If the world weighed a gnat's wing with Allah, He would not give a disbeliever a sip of water' (a hadith), and (3) the instruction to be in the world as a stranger or a passerby, with the added warning to count oneself among the dead. The commentator elaborates on the parable of a stranger longing for home, and highlights the intensity of detachment required: a passerby crosses through hardship without lingering. The marginal gloss summarizes that tanbih and tasalli are both consequences of seeing the righteous face lack of wealth and difficulties, reinforcing the lesson of detachment.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Islam condemns all material enjoyment, teaching hatred of the world.
Correction: This passage teaches awareness of the world's low value compared to the eternal life, not hatred of creation itself.

Key Takeaway
Afflictions serve as powerful reminders of the world's true worthlessness, turning hearts toward the eternal.

Implications of 'Muhammad Rasul Allah'
Bajuri explains the second shahada's implications and a linguistic note.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the phrase 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' entails belief in all prophets and the obligation of their truthfulness, and why the word 'sa'ir' is used to encompass all prophets.

Core Idea
Belief in Muhammad ﷺ implies belief in all prophets and their truthfulness.

This passage from Bajuri's commentary carefully unpacks the second half of the shahada. While the first half establishes tawhid, the second half establishes prophethood. Bajuri explains that this phrase necessarily includes belief in all prophets, not just Muhammad (peace be upon him), and from it we derive the obligation that all messengers are truthful. He also clarifies a linguistic point about the word 'sa'ir' to ensure that no prophet is excluded.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the structure: it begins by contrasting with the first shahada, then states the implication, then focuses on the derived obligation, and ends with a linguistic clarification.
2
Identify the two main implications
The passage shows that 'Muhammad Rasul Allah' implies (a) belief in all prophets (b) and the obligation of their truthfulness. Find the phrases that convey each.
The phrase 'wa yu'khadhu minhu wujub sidq al-rusul' is key.
3
Understand the linguistic nuance of 'sa'ir'
Bajuri explains that 'sa'ir' can mean either 'all' or 'remaining'. Reflect on why this linguistic flexibility is important for the doctrine: it ensures belief covers every prophet, no matter how they are categorized.
The two derivations: from 'sūr' (wall) giving 'all', and from 'su'r' (leftover) giving 'remaining'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ... إلخ) هذا مقابل لمحذوف، والتقدير: أما قولنا: لا إله إلا الله فيدخل فيه ما تقدم، وأما قولنا: محمد رسول الله فيدخل فيه... إلخ. (قوله: فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ) أي: في معناه؛ لأن الدخول ليس في مجرَّدِ القول، بل في معناه. (وقوله: الْإِيمَانُ... إلخ) أي: التصديق بذلك، ولا يخفى أن ذلك زائد على المقصود من بيانِ اندراج العقائد المذكورة فيما تقدم تحت ذلك، فالمقصود في الحقيقة قوله : ويؤخذ منه وجوب صدق الرسل... إلخ). (قوله: بِسَائِرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ أي بجميعهم أو بباقيهم؛ لأن سائِرَ إِن أُخِذَ من السُّورِ؛ كان بمعنى جميع لما فيه من معنى الإحاطة، وإن أخذ من السُّورِ كان بمعنى: باق؛ لأن معنى السؤر البقيَّةُ.
His saying: 'And as for our saying “Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah”... etc.' This is in contrast to an omitted [part], and the estimation is: As for our saying “There is no god but Allah”, it includes what preceded, and as for our saying “Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah”, it includes... etc. His saying: 'so it enters into it' means into its meaning, because the entering is not in the mere saying, but in its meaning. And his saying: 'faith... etc.' means the affirmation (tasdiq) of that, and it is not hidden that this is additional to the intended purpose of explaining the inclusion of the mentioned beliefs under that in what preceded. So the real intended purpose is his saying: 'and from it is taken the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers... etc.' His saying: 'in all the prophets (bi-sā'ir al-anbiyā')' meaning in all of them or the rest of them, because 'sā'ir' if taken from 'sūr' (wall) means 'all' because of the meaning of encompassment, and if taken from 'su'r' (leftover) means 'remaining' because the meaning of 'su'r' is leftover, and from that is 'the leftover drink of the believer is a cure.'
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage explains the second part of the shahada, 'Muhammad Rasul Allah', and what it implies. It begins by contrasting it with the first part: while 'La ilaha illa Allah' includes the attributes of God, 'Muhammad Rasul Allah' includes belief in the prophets. The entry (al-dukhul) is in the meaning, not the mere wording. It then clarifies that the mention of 'faith' (iman) in the text is additional to the main point, which is that from this shahada we derive the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers (wujub sidq al-rusul). Finally, it provides a linguistic note on the word 'sa'ir' used in 'bi-sā'ir al-anbiyā''. 'Sa'ir' can mean either 'all' (if derived from suur, meaning a wall, connoting encompassment) or 'the rest' (if derived from su'r, meaning leftover). Both meanings are valid, indicating that belief must encompass all prophets, both those before and after.

صدق الرسل
سائر
أنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'sa'ir' only means 'remaining', limiting belief to later prophets.
Correction: The word can also mean 'all' (from 'sūr'), so it encompasses every prophet, past and future.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The second shahada obligates belief in all prophets and their truthfulness, and the word 'sa'ir' linguistically ensures this includes every prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The linguistic precision of 'sa'ir' ensures no prophet is excluded. Examine your heart: do you harbour any prejudice or doubt about the message of any prophet? Ask Allah to purify your faith and grant you complete submission to all His messengers.

The Correct View on the Number of Prophets
Al-Bajuri discusses the total number of prophets and the duty to know twenty-five.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper Islamic position on the total number of prophets and why it is obligatory to know twenty-five by name while refraining from specifying the exact total.

Core Idea
Believe in all prophets generally, but know twenty-five individually.

In this passage, Al-Bajuri addresses a question that often arises: How many prophets are there? He reviews several transmitted numbers but then explains why fixing a total number can be problematic. Instead, he clarifies what is truly obligatory upon believers—to believe in all prophets sent by Allah in a general sense, while specifically knowing the twenty-five prophets mentioned in the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the different numbers mentioned and the conclusion.
The passage includes a poetic summary at the end.
2
Identify the correct view
Look for the phrase 'al-sahih: al-imsak 'an hasrihim fi 'adad'. This is the key statement: it is correct to refrain from confining them to a number.
Think about why this is the prudent position.
3
Understand the exception for twenty-five
The passage then says it is obligatory to know twenty-five prophets in detail. Find the names mentioned in the poem and verify they are the well-known ones.
This shows that detailed knowledge is required for a subset, while general belief suffices for the rest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد تقدَّمَ أنه اختلفت الروايات في عددهم، ففي رواية : أنهم مائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً، وفي رواية وخمسة وعشرون ألفاً، وفي رواية: أنهم ألف ألف ومائتا ألف، وفي رواية وأربعمائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً، والصحيح: الإمساك عن حَصْرِهم في عددٍ؛ لأنه ربما أدَّى إلى إثبات النبوَّة لمن ليس كذلك، أو إلى نَفْيها عمن هو كذلك، فيجب الإيمانُ: بأن الله أنبياء على الإجمال، إلا خمسة وعشرين، فيجب معرفتهم على التفصيل كما أشار لذلك بعضهم بقوله:
ختم عَلَى كُلِّ ذِي التَّكْلِيفِ مَعْرِفَةٌ بِأَنْبِيَاءَ عَلَى التَّفْصِيل قَدْ عُلِمُوا في تِلْكَ حُجَّتُنَا مِنْهُمْ ثَمَانِيَةٌ مِنْ بَعْدِ عَشْرٍ، وَيَبْقَى سَبْعَةٌ وَهُمُو إِدْرِيسُ هُودٌ شُعَيْبٌ صَالِحٌ وَكَذَا ذُو الْكِفْلِ آدَمُ بِالْمُخْتَارِ قَدْ خُتِمُوا
And it has preceded that the reports differ concerning their number. In one report: they are one hundred and twenty-four thousand. In another report: and twenty-five thousand. In another report: they are one million two hundred thousand. In another report: four hundred and twenty-four thousand. And the correct [view] is to refrain from confining them to a number, because perhaps it leads to affirming prophethood for those who are not prophets, or to denying it from those who are. So it is obligatory to believe that there are prophets of Allah in general (ijmal), except for twenty-five, for whom it is obligatory to know them in detail (tafsil), as some alluded to by his saying: 
'Sealed upon every accountable person is knowledge of prophets in detail. They are known. In that our argument: from them are eight after ten, and seven remain, and they are: Idris, Hud, Shu'ayb, Salih, and likewise Dhul-Kifl, Adam, and [the Chosen One] they have concluded.'
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage addresses the number of prophets. It begins by recounting various transmitted reports about the total number: 124,000; 125,000; 1,200,000; or 424,000. Al-Bajuri states that the correct position is to refrain from fixing a number because doing so might wrongly include non-prophets as prophets or exclude true prophets. What is obligatory is to believe in the prophets as a whole in general terms, except for twenty-five specific prophets who must be known individually. This is illustrated by a poetic summary: eight prophets follow the first ten, plus seven others (Idris, Hud, Shu'ayb, Salih, Dhul-Kifl, Adam, and the Chosen One—meaning Muhammad), totaling twenty-five. The passage thus defines the proper approach to belief in prophets: general belief in all, detailed knowledge of twenty-five.

Key Terms
الأنبياء
النبوَّة
الإجمال
التفصيل
الحصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think it is necessary to know the exact total number of prophets.
Correction: The correct view is to refrain from specifying a total number, as the reports vary and fixing a number could be problematic.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe in all prophets in general, but to know twenty-five specific prophets in detail, while refraining from fixating on the total number.

?
The lesson warns against confining Allah's messengers to a number. In your own life, are there ways you confine Allah's mercy or guidance to a narrow set of people or experiences? What would it look like to expand your heart to accept His limitless grace?

The Number of Prophets and Obligation to Believe in Them
Al-Bajuri explains the varying reports on the number of prophets and the correct stance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic stance on the total number of prophets, the obligation to believe in them generally, and the necessity of knowing twenty-five specific prophets in detail.

Core Idea
Believing in all prophets is obligatory, but their exact number is unknown; only twenty-five must be known by name.

Al-Bajuri addresses a common question: how many prophets did God send? While various numbers are reported, the authentic position is to refrain from specifying a count. This lesson clarifies what is required of believers: general belief in all prophets, with the exception of twenty-five whose names are revealed and must be known in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Pay attention to the variant numbers listed.
2
Identify the variant narrations
The passage lists four different numbers reported about the total prophets. Find each one and note that they vary widely.
3
Understand the correct stance
The author states the correct opinion: to refrain from specifying a number. Ask yourself why this is the safest position.
Consider the risk of false confirmation or false denial of prophethood.
4
Distinguish general vs. detailed belief
The passage divides the obligation: general belief in all prophets, and detailed knowledge of twenty-five specific ones. Reflect on why these twenty-five are singled out.
The poetic summary gives a partial list.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد تقدَّمَ أنه اختلفت الروايات في عددهم، ففي رواية : أنهم مائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً، وفي رواية وخمسة وعشرون ألفاً، وفي رواية: أنهم ألف ألف ومائتا ألف، وفي رواية وأربعمائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفاً، والصحيح: الإمساك عن حَصْرِهم في عددٍ؛ لأنه ربما أدَّى إلى إثبات النبوَّة لمن ليس كذلك، أو إلى نَفْيها عمن هو كذلك، فيجب الإيمانُ: بأن الله أنبياء على الإجمال، إلا خمسة وعشرين، فيجب معرفتهم على التفصيل كما أشار لذلك بعضهم بقوله:
ختم عَلَى كُلِّ ذِي التَّكْلِيفِ مَعْرِفَةٌ بِأَنْبِيَاءَ عَلَى التَّفْصِيل قَدْ عُلِمُوا في تِلْكَ حُجَّتُنَا مِنْهُمْ ثَمَانِيَةٌ مِنْ بَعْدِ عَشْرٍ، وَيَبْقَى سَبْعَةٌ وَهُمُو إِدْرِيسُ هُودٌ شُعَيْبٌ صَالِحٌ وَكَذَا ذُو الْكِفْلِ آدَمُ بِالْمُخْتَارِ قَدْ خُتِمُوا
And it has preceded that the narrations differ regarding their number. In one narration: they are one hundred twenty-four thousand. In another narration: and twenty-five thousand. In another narration: they are one thousand thousand and two hundred thousand. In another narration: and four hundred thousand and twenty-four thousand. And the correct opinion is to refrain from limiting them to a number; because perhaps that would lead to confirming prophethood for one who is not so, or to denying it from one who is so. So it is obligatory to believe generally in the prophets of Allah, except for twenty-five, for whom detailed knowledge is obligatory, as some alluded to by his saying: 'It is obligatory upon every legally responsible person to have knowledge of the prophets in detail, those who are known. Among them are eight from our proof after ten, and seven remain: Idris, Hud, Shuʿayb, Salih, and likewise Dhul-Kifl, Adam, and the Chosen One (Muhammad), by whom the prophets are sealed.'
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage first states that there are multiple narrations about the total number of prophets, giving four variant counts. Then it declares that the correct position is to refrain from specifying a number, because doing so could lead to error: either falsely attributing prophethood to someone not a prophet, or denying prophethood to a true prophet. Therefore, the required belief is general: one must believe that God sent prophets, without needing to know the exact count. However, there are twenty-five prophets whose names are known from revelation, and it is obligatory to have detailed knowledge of them. The author then cites a poetic summary listing the eight from the proof (possibly referring to a known list) and the seven others, ending with Adam and Muhammad, the seal.

Key Terms

نبوة
إيمان
تفصيل
إجمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is obligatory to know all prophets by name.
Correction: The passage clarifies that general belief suffices except for the twenty-five known from revelation.

Checkpoint

A) They are exactly 124,000.
B) They are exactly 25,000.
C) One should refrain from specifying a number.
D) They are exactly 1,200,000.

Key Takeaway
The number of prophets is not fixed by revelation, but we must believe in all generally and know twenty-five specifically.

The Resurrection and the Great Intercession
Sanusi describes the Resurrection scene and the Prophet's exclusive Great Intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the events of the Resurrection leading to the Prophet Muhammad's exclusive Great Intercession and its significance in Muslim theology.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Great Intercession is the key that unlocks all other intercessions on the Day of Judgment.

This passage from Sanusi's work paints a vivid picture of the Day of Gathering, from the oppressive heat to the desperate search for an intercessor. It culminates in the unique role of Prophet Muhammad, who alone accepts to intercede for the commencement of judgment. Through this narrative, we learn not only the sequence of events but also the supreme status of the Prophet and the mercy he brings to his community.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the sequence of events from the gathering to the intercession.
Pay attention to the emotional crescendo: fear, hope, and relief.
2
Visualize the scene
Imagine the crowd, the angels, the sun at a distance of a kohl stick's mile, and the mounting terror that makes people wish for the Fire.
This helps internalize the gravity of the situation.
3
Observe the prophets' responses
Note how each prophet declines intercession by citing their own sin and saying 'myself, myself'. This highlights their humility and fear.
Contrast with the Prophet Muhammad's response.
4
Focus on the Prophet's role
The Prophet Muhammad accepts the intercession, prostrates, and is granted permission to intercede for the decisive judgment. This is the Great Intercession.
He is called 'the greatest chief' and 'the most perfect master'.
5
Understand exclusivity and derivation
Sanusi states this intercession is exclusive to the Prophet, and all other intercessions (by other prophets, scholars, etc.) are enabled only through his intercession.
This corrects the misconception that others can intercede independently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عند وصولهم إلى المحشر يقفون فيه، وتصطف الملائكة محدقين حولهم، وتدنو الشمس من رؤوسهم حتى ما يكون بينها وبينهم إلا قدر ميل - أي: ميل المكحلة لا الميل المعروف ، فحينئذ يشتد الخوف والهول، ويعظم الكرب، فيتمنون الانصراف ولو إلى النار، ثم بعد طول الموقف عليهم يلهمون أن الأنبياء هم الواسطة بين الله وبين خلقه، فيذهبون إليهم يستشفعون بهم واحداً بعد واحد، فيتنصل - أي: يعتذر - كل منهم بما وقع له من صورة الخطيئة، ويقول: لست لها، لست لها، نفسي نفسي. فإذا انتهى الأمر للرئيس الأعظم والسيد الأكمل الأفخم قال: أنا لها، أمتي أمتي، ثم يخر ساجداً تحت العرش كسجود الصلاة، فيقال: يا محمد، ارفع رأسك، وسل تعط، واشفع تشفع، فيرفع رأسه، ويشفع في فصل القضاء. وهذه هي الشفاعة العظمى، وهي مختصة به، وله شفاعات أخر، بل ولغيره من باقي الأنبياء والعلماء والصالحين؛ لأنهم يتجاسرون على ذلك بسبب شفاعته، فهو الذي يفتح لهم باب الشفاعة.
Then when they arrive at the gathering place, they stand in it, and the angels line up surrounding them, and the sun draws near to their heads until there is only a mile between them and it – meaning the mile of the kohl stick, not the well-known mile. At that moment, fear and terror intensify, and distress becomes great, so they wish to depart even to the Fire. Then, after a long stand, they are inspired that the prophets are the intermediaries between God and His creation, so they go to them seeking their intercession one after another. But each prophet declines – i.e., apologizes – due to what occurred from him in the form of a sin, and says: 'Not for me, not for me, myself, myself.' When the matter reaches the greatest chief, the most perfect and most glorious master, he says: 'I am for it, my community, my community.' Then he falls prostrating under the Throne like the prostration of prayer, and it is said: 'O Muhammad, raise your head, ask and you shall be given, intercede and your intercession shall be accepted.' So he raises his head and intercedes for the decisive judgment. This is the Great Intercession, and it is exclusive to him. He has other intercessions, and even other prophets, scholars, and righteous people have intercession, but they dare to do so because of his intercession; he opens the door of intercession for them.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a narrative description by Sanusi of the events of the Resurrection, culminating in the exclusive Great Intercession of the Prophet Muhammad.  It follows the order of events: the gathering, the intense heat, the terror, the search for intercessors among the prophets, each declining due to their own perceived shortcomings, and finally the Prophet Muhammad accepting to intercede for the commencement of the Judgment.  Sanusi emphasizes that this specific intercession (for the Judgment to begin) is unique to the Prophet.  He notes that other intercessions exist for him and others, but all are dependent on his initial intercession, as he opens the door.  The passage is doctrinal, affirming the role of the Prophet as the highest intercessor and the means of relief for the community.

Key Terms
المحشر
الملائكة
ميل المكحلة
الشفاعة العظمى
الرئيس الأعظم
فصل القضاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the intercession of other prophets is independent of the Prophet Muhammad.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that all other intercessions occur only through the Prophet's intercession; he opens the door for them.

Checkpoint
Why do the other prophets decline to intercede when approached?
A) Because they are not allowed to intercede
B) Because they are too weak
C) Because they recall a sin they committed
D) Because they are angry with the people

Key Takeaway
The Great Intercession for the decisive judgment is exclusive to Prophet Muhammad, and he opens the door for all other intercessions on the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The other prophets said 'نفسي نفسي' (myself, myself), but the Prophet said 'أمتي أمتي' (my community, my community). What one step can you take today to align your heart more with the Prophet's compassion?
?

On what basis do you hope to be included in his 'أمتي'? If you were to die today, what evidence would there be that you genuinely belonged to his community?
?
The Prophet prostrated under the Throne and was told 'اشفع تشفع' (intercede, your intercession shall be accepted). The Seventy Thousand and the Prophet's Request for More
Sanusi relates the hadith of seventy thousand and subsequent increases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about seventy thousand entering Paradise without reckoning and how the Prophet's intercession multiplied that number.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession multiplies God's mercy beyond measure.

This lesson presents a famous hadith about the immense mercy of Allah and the high station of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The hadith describes a large group entering Paradise without prior accounting, and then the Prophet's request for even more. Through this, we see the generosity of Allah and the intercessory role of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the progression: first seventy thousand, then each with seventy thousand, then three handfuls.
The phrase 'or as he said' is a narratorial caution about exact wording.
2
Understand the first exemption
The hadith begins by stating that after the general accounting, some people are exempted. The Prophet mentions seventy thousand who enter without reckoning. Reflect on the significance of 'without reckoning'.
3
Follow the requests for increase
The companions ask the Prophet to ask for more. He does, and each time Allah grants a larger number. Notice how the increments are described: first 70,000 per person, then three handfuls.
The three handfuls are interpreted as three more large groups.
4
Connect to the Prophet's intercession
This hadith illustrates the Prophet's power of intercession and the boundless mercy of Allah. It also shows the Prophet's care for his community.
The lesson reinforces the importance of hadith in eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد ذلك يحاسبون، إلا من ورد الحديث باستثنائه، فإنه ورد أنه قال: يدخل الجنة من أمتي سبعون ألفاً بغير حساب، فقيل له: هلا استزدت ربك؟ فقال: استردته فزادني مع كل واحد سبعين ألفاً، فقيل له: هلا استزدت ربك؟ فقال: استزدته فزادني ثلاث حثيات بيده، أو كما قال.
Then after that they will be called to account, except those whom the hadith exempts. For it is reported that he said: 'Seventy thousand of my community will enter Paradise without reckoning.' It was said to him: 'Will you not ask your Lord for more?' He said: 'I asked Him, and He gave me with each one seventy thousand.' It was said to him: 'Will you not ask your Lord for more?' He said: 'I asked Him, and He gave me three handfuls with His hand' – or as he said.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a hadith report from Sanusi concerning the promise of Paradise without prior judgment for a substantial number of the Prophet's community.  It begins by stating that people will be held accountable after the intercession, except those specifically exempted by hadith.  The Prophet is reported to have said that seventy thousand will enter without account.  When asked if he could ask for more, he did so, and each of those seventy thousand was given another seventy thousand.  When asked again, he asked for more and received three handfuls (or three additional groups).  The phrase 'or as he said' is a standard narratorial caveat indicating precision in wording is not guaranteed.  The passage demonstrates the Prophet's intercessory power and God's boundless mercy, as well as the importance of the hadith as a source of eschatological knowledge.

Key Terms

بغير حساب
استردته
ثلاث حثيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this hadith contradicts the idea that everyone will be judged.
Correction: The exemption is specific to this group; others are still judged, but with mercy.

The Comprehensive Content of Belief in the Prophet
Al-Bajuri explains the comprehensive scope of faith in the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that believing in Muhammad as the Messenger of Allah necessarily entails believing in all the divine, prophetic, and revealed matters he brought.

Core Idea
Belief in the Prophet includes belief in everything he brought.

This lesson explores the far-reaching implications of affirming Muhammad's prophethood. The commentary shows that our testimony is not just a verbal statement but a comprehensive acceptance of three categories of doctrine: matters pertaining to God, matters pertaining to prophets, and matters known through revelation. Understanding this helps us appreciate the holistic nature of Islamic faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from the commentary about 'because he came with verification of all that'. Notice how the commentator explains the entailment.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the three categories mentioned: ilahiyyat (divine matters), nubuwwiyyat (prophetic matters), and sam'iyyat (revealed matters). Note the examples given for sam'iyyat.
3
Understand the emphasis
The phrase 'all of it' (kullihi) is an emphasis. Understand why the commentator stresses comprehensiveness.
This emphasizes that nothing is left out.
4
Reflect on personal faith
Ask yourself: does your faith in the Prophet include acceptance of all these categories? This lesson shows that true faith is all-encompassing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: لأَنه جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيع ذَلِكَ أي: ويلزم من التصديق برسالته ما جاء به، فعند التحقيق يدخل في قولنا: محمد رسول الله، الإيمان الإلهيات - أي: ما يتعلق بالإله - وجميعُ النبويات - أي: ما يتعلق بالأنبياء - وجميع السَّمْعِيّات من سؤال القبر وعذابه والجنة والنار وغير ذلك. (قوله: كُلّهِ) تأكيد للعموم المستفاد من (جميع). (قوله: وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: وُجُوبُ صِدْقُ الرُّسُلِ... إلخ) أي: لأنه جاء بذلك، ويلزم من التصديق برسالته التصديق ما جاء به. وقد صَرَّحَ المصنف هنا بجميع الصدق واستحالة الكذب، وأشار إلى استحالة الخيانة والكتمان بقوله: بوجوب واستحالة فعل المنهيات كلها) ويلزمُ من استحالة الخيانة: وجوب الأمانة، ومن استحالة الكتمان وجوبُ التبليغ فعُلِمَ من ذلك الواجب في حق الرسل، وكذا المستحيلُ، وسيذكر الجائز. فتدبر. (قوله: وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِم من عطف اللازم على الملزوم؛ لأنه يلزم من وجوب الصدق استحالة الكذب كما لا يخفى. (قوله: وَإِلَّا لَمْ يُكُونُوا... إلخ) أي: وإلا يجب الصدق لهم، ويستحيل الكذب عليهم؛ لم يكونوا... إلخ. ووجه ذلك: أن الله تعالى قد أخبر بصدقهم بخلق المعجزة على أيديهم، ويجب أن يكون خَبَرُهُ تعالى على وَفْقِ علمه، وهو عالم بكلّ شيء، فيلزم من ذلك وجوب الصدق لهم، واستحالة الكذب عليهم. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري . (قوله: جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ... إلخ) يحتمل أن المعنى: جاء مصدّقاً بجميع ذلك، وأن المعنى: جاء آمراً لنا بأن نصدق بجميع ذلك، والأقرب الثاني، وعلى هذا يكون قوله: (بتصديق على تقدير مضاف، أي: بوجوب تصديق جميع ذلك.
(His saying: 'because he came with the verification of all that' means: and it follows from verifying his messengership [the verification of] what he brought. So upon careful consideration, our saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' includes belief in the divine matters – that is, what pertains to the Divine – and all the prophetic matters – that is, what pertains to the prophets – and all the sam'iyyat (things known by hearing) such as the questioning of the grave and its punishment, Paradise, Hellfire, and other than that. (His saying: 'all of it') is an emphasis of the generality understood from 'all'. (His saying: 'and from it is taken: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers... etc.') means: because he came with that, and from verifying his messengership follows verifying what he brought. And the author stated explicitly here [the obligation of] all truthfulness and the impossibility of lying, and he alluded to the impossibility of treachery and concealment by his saying: 'with the obligation and impossibility of doing all the forbidden things' and from the impossibility of treachery follows the obligation of trustworthiness, and from the impossibility of concealment follows the obligation of conveying. So from that is known the obligatory [attributes] with respect to the messengers, and likewise the impossible, and he will mention the possible. So reflect. (His saying: 'and the impossibility of lying against them' is from the conjunction of the necessary to the necessitated; because from the obligation of truthfulness follows the impossibility of lying, as is not hidden. (His saying: 'and otherwise they would not be... etc.') means: and if it were not obligatory for them to be truthful, and lying impossible for them, they would not be... etc. And the explanation of that is that Allah the Exalted has informed of their truthfulness by creating the miracle at their hands, and it is necessary that His report, Exalted be He, be in accordance with His knowledge, and He is knowledgeable of everything, so from that follows the obligation of truthfulness for them and the impossibility of lying against them. Commentary of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri. (His saying: 'came with verification... etc.) could mean: he came verifying all that, or that he came commanding us to verify all that. The second is closer, and on this his saying 'with verification' is upon an implicit genitive, i.e., with the obligation of verifying all that.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'because he came with the verification of all that' from the matn. It explains that believing in Muhammad as a messenger necessarily implies believing in everything he brought, which includes three categories: ilahiyyat (matters pertaining to God), nubuwwiyyat (matters pertaining to prophets), and sam'iyyat (matters heard through revelation, such as the grave's questioning, punishment, Paradise, Hell, etc.). The commentary then deduces the necessary attributes of prophets from the text: the obligation of truthfulness (wajib al-sidq) and the impossibility of lying (mustahil al-kidhb). It further infers the obligation of trustworthiness (amana) from the impossibility of treachery, and the obligation of conveying (tabligh) from the impossibility of concealment. The proof for these attributes is given: Allah confirmed the truthfulness of the prophets by creating miracles at their hands, and Allah's report (khabar) must accord with His knowledge, which is all-encompassing. Thus, truthfulness is obligatory and lying impossible. Finally, the text considers two possible interpretations of 'came with verification': either he came verifying all that himself, or he came commanding us to verify all that. The commentary favors the latter, explaining that the phrase implies an obligation on us to affirm all those matters.

Key Terms
تصديق
رسالة
إلهيات
نبويات
سمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that believing in the Prophet is separate from believing in the specific doctrines he brought.
Correction: The commentary shows that the two are inseparable; authentic faith in the Prophet necessarily requires accepting all the ilahiyyat, nubuwwiyyat, and sam'iyyat he conveyed.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the phrase 'all of it' emphasize?
A) The comprehensiveness of the categories
B) The number of prophets
C) The miracles
D) The obligation of truthfulness

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's message is incomplete unless it encompasses all the divine, prophetic, and revealed matters he brought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Your faith in the Prophet is not complete until you embrace all he brought. Will you commit today to seeking knowledge of any neglected aspect of his message—whether about Allah, other prophets, or the afterlife—and to accept it wholeheartedly?

The Necessary Attributes of Prophets and Their Proof
Al-Bajuri deduces necessary prophetic attributes and gives a proof from miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical deduction of prophetic attributes (truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveying) from the obligation of truthfulness and the rational proof from miracles.

Core Idea
Prophetic truthfulness is proven by miracles, which are from Allah.

Building on the previous lesson, the commentary now extracts the essential moral attributes of prophets from the very fact that they brought divine truth. It then grounds these attributes in a rational proof involving miracles. This lesson helps us see how Islamic theology logically justifies the integrity of prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on deduction of attributes
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'and from it is taken: the obligation of truthfulness...'. Note the list of attributes derived.
2
Trace the logical deduction
Follow the deduction: truthfulness (sidq) implies impossibility of lying, impossibility of treachery implies trustworthiness, impossibility of concealment implies conveying. Understand each step.
This is a chain of logical entailments.
3
Examine the proof from miracles
Read the explanation of why truthfulness is obligatory: Allah creates miracles through prophets, confirming their truth. Since Allah's report must match His knowledge, the prophets are necessarily truthful.
This is a key theological argument.
4
Consider the linguistic interpretation
The passage ends with a note on the meaning of 'came with verification'. Reflect on the nuance between 'he came verifying' and 'he came commanding us to verify'.
The author prefers the latter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: لأَنه جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيع ذَلِكَ أي: ويلزم من التصديق برسالته ما جاء به، فعند التحقيق يدخل في قولنا: محمد رسول الله، الإيمان الإلهيات - أي: ما يتعلق بالإله - وجميعُ النبويات - أي: ما يتعلق بالأنبياء - وجميع السَّمْعِيّات من سؤال القبر وعذابه والجنة والنار وغير ذلك. (قوله: كُلّهِ) تأكيد للعموم المستفاد من (جميع). (قوله: وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: وُجُوبُ صِدْقُ الرُّسُلِ... إلخ) أي: لأنه جاء بذلك، ويلزم من التصديق برسالته التصديق ما جاء به. وقد صَرَّحَ المصنف هنا بجميع الصدق واستحالة الكذب، وأشار إلى استحالة الخيانة والكتمان بقوله: بوجوب واستحالة فعل المنهيات كلها) ويلزمُ من استحالة الخيانة: وجوب الأمانة، ومن استحالة الكتمان وجوبُ التبليغ فعُلِمَ من ذلك الواجب في حق الرسل، وكذا المستحيلُ، وسيذكر الجائز. فتدبر. (قوله: وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِم من عطف اللازم على الملزوم؛ لأنه يلزم من وجوب الصدق استحالة الكذب كما لا يخفى. (قوله: وَإِلَّا لَمْ يُكُونُوا... إلخ) أي: وإلا يجب الصدق لهم، ويستحيل الكذب عليهم؛ لم يكونوا... إلخ. ووجه ذلك: أن الله تعالى قد أخبر بصدقهم بخلق المعجزة على أيديهم، ويجب أن يكون خَبَرُهُ تعالى على وَفْقِ علمه، وهو عالم بكلّ شيء، فيلزم من ذلك وجوب الصدق لهم، واستحالة الكذب عليهم. حاشية العلامة أحمد الأجهوري . (قوله: جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ... إلخ) يحتمل أن المعنى: جاء مصدّقاً بجميع ذلك، وأن المعنى: جاء آمراً لنا بأن نصدق بجميع ذلك، والأقرب الثاني، وعلى هذا يكون قوله: (بتصديق على تقدير مضاف، أي: بوجوب تصديق جميع ذلك.
(His saying: 'because he came with the verification of all that' means: and it follows from verifying his messengership [the verification of] what he brought. So upon careful consideration, our saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' includes belief in the divine matters – that is, what pertains to the Divine – and all the prophetic matters – that is, what pertains to the prophets – and all the sam'iyyat (things known by hearing) such as the questioning of the grave and its punishment, Paradise, Hellfire, and other than that. (His saying: 'all of it') is an emphasis of the generality understood from 'all'. (His saying: 'and from it is taken: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers... etc.') means: because he came with that, and from verifying his messengership follows verifying what he brought. And the author stated explicitly here [the obligation of] all truthfulness and the impossibility of lying, and he alluded to the impossibility of treachery and concealment by his saying: 'with the obligation and impossibility of doing all the forbidden things' and from the impossibility of treachery follows the obligation of trustworthiness, and from the impossibility of concealment follows the obligation of conveying. So from that is known the obligatory [attributes] with respect to the messengers, and likewise the impossible, and he will mention the possible. So reflect. (His saying: 'and the impossibility of lying against them' is from the conjunction of the necessary to the necessitated; because from the obligation of truthfulness follows the impossibility of lying, as is not hidden. (His saying: 'and otherwise they would not be... etc.') means: and if it were not obligatory for them to be truthful, and lying impossible for them, they would not be... etc. And the explanation of that is that Allah the Exalted has informed of their truthfulness by creating the miracle at their hands, and it is necessary that His report, Exalted be He, be in accordance with His knowledge, and He is knowledgeable of everything, so from that follows the obligation of truthfulness for them and the impossibility of lying against them. Commentary of the scholar Ahmad al-Ujhuri. (His saying: 'came with verification... etc.) could mean: he came verifying all that, or that he came commanding us to verify all that. The second is closer, and on this his saying 'with verification' is upon an implicit genitive, i.e., with the obligation of verifying all that.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'because he came with the verification of all that' from the matn. It explains that believing in Muhammad as a messenger necessarily implies believing in everything he brought, which includes three categories: ilahiyyat (matters pertaining to God), nubuwwiyyat (matters pertaining to prophets), and sam'iyyat (matters heard through revelation, such as the grave's questioning, punishment, Paradise, Hell, etc.). The commentary then deduces the necessary attributes of prophets from the text: the obligation of truthfulness (wajib al-sidq) and the impossibility of lying (mustahil al-kidhb). It further infers the obligation of trustworthiness (amana) from the impossibility of treachery, and the obligation of conveying (tabligh) from the impossibility of concealment. The proof for these attributes is given: Allah confirmed the truthfulness of the prophets by creating miracles at their hands, and Allah's report (khabar) must accord with His knowledge, which is all-encompassing. Thus, truthfulness is obligatory and lying impossible. Finally, the text considers two possible interpretations of 'came with verification': either he came verifying all that himself, or he came commanding us to verify all that. The commentary favors the latter, explaining that the phrase implies an obligation on us to affirm all those matters.

استحالة الكذب
وجوب الأمانة
وجوب التبليغ
معجزة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof for prophetic truthfulness is circular or subjective.
Correction: The commentary clarifies that the proof is based on Allah's objective action (creating miracles) and His omniscience, making it a rational and objective argument.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what attribute of prophets follows from the impossibility of treachery (خيانة)?
A) Truthfulness (صدق)
B) Trustworthiness (أمانة)
C) Conveying (تبليغ)
D) Infallibility (عصمة)

Key Takeaway
The obligation of truthfulness and trustworthiness in prophets is rationally proven by the miracles Allah performs through them.

?

The Rational Proof for Prophetic Truthfulness
Al-Bajuri proves prophetic truthfulness via miracles and God's knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that establishes the obligation of truthfulness and impossibility of lying for prophets, derived from the occurrence of miracles and God's perfect knowledge.

Core Idea
Miracles prove prophets are truthful because God cannot confirm a liar.

We now explore a key argument in prophetic theology: how do we know that prophets must be truthful and can never lie? Al-Bajuri shows that this is not merely a moral expectation but a rational necessity based on the very nature of miracles and God's knowledge. The passage unpacks the logical chain that binds divine confirmation to prophetic integrity.

Guided Path
1
Read the core argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author moves from the fact that God creates miracles at the hands of prophets to a necessary conclusion about their truthfulness.
Pay attention to the term 'الملازمة' (necessary connection).
2
Trace the logical chain
Identify the key premises: (1) God creates miracles to confirm a prophet; (2) God's report must correspond to His knowledge; (3) God knows all things, including hidden matters. Then see how these lead to the conclusion: prophets must be truthful and cannot lie.
3
Understand the derived attributes
The passage also derives trustworthiness and delivery from the impossibility of betrayal and concealment. Note how each negation yields a positive obligation.
This shows the method of 'عطف اللازم على الملزوم' (annexation of necessary to necessitated).
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that prophetic truthfulness is based on personal character. The passage shows it is a theological necessity grounded in divine action and omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: وُجُوبُ صِدْقُ الرُّسُلِ... إلخ أي: لأنه جاء بذلك، ويلزم من التصديق برسالته التصديق ما جاء به. وقد صَرَّحَ المصنف هنا بجميع الصدق واستحالة الكذب، وأشار إلى استحالة الخيانة والكتمان بقوله: بوجوب واستحالة فعل المنهيات كلها) ويلزمُ من استحالة الخيانة: وجوب الأمانة، ومن استحالة الكتمان وجوبُ التبليغ فعُلِمَ من ذلك الواجب في حق الرسل، وكذا المستحيلُ، وسيذكر الجائز. فتدبر. قوله: وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِم من عطف اللازم على الملزوم؛ لأنه يلزم من وجوب الصدق استحالة الكذب كما لا يخفى. قوله: وَإِلَّا لَمْ يُكُونُوا... إلخ أي: وإلا يجب الصدق لهم، ويستحيل الكذب عليهم؛ لم يكونوا... إلخ. ووجه ذلك: أن الله تعالى قد أخبر بصدقهم بخلق المعجزة على أيديهم، ويجب أن يكون خَبَرُهُ تعالى على وَفْقِ علمه، وهو عالم بكلّ شيء، فيلزم من ذلك وجوب الصدق لهم، واستحالة الكذب عليهم. قوله: الْعَالِمِ بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ إشارة إلى بيان وجه الملازمة في قوله: (وإلا لم يكونوا... إلخ) كما تقدم. والخفيَّاتُ: غَوَامِضُ الأمور ومشكلاتها، ولا يخفى أنه إذا كان عالماً بالخفيات؛ كان عالماً بالجليات الظاهرات من باب أولى وتقسيم الأمور إلى خفيَّاتٍ وجلِيَّاتٍ إنما هو بالنسبة إلينا، وأما بالنسبة إليه تعالى؛ فكل الأمور جليات على حد سواء.
His statement: 'And from it is derived the obligation of the truthfulness of the messengers... etc.' means: because he came with that, and from affirming his messengership follows affirming what he brought. The author has explicitly stated here the obligation of truthfulness and the impossibility of lying, and alluded to the impossibility of betrayal and concealment by his saying: 'with the obligation and impossibility of committing all the prohibitions.' And from the impossibility of betrayal follows the obligation of trustworthiness, and from the impossibility of concealment follows the obligation of delivery. So from that is known what is obligatory regarding the messengers, and likewise what is impossible, and he will mention what is possible. So ponder. His statement: 'and the impossibility of lying upon them' is an annexation of the necessary to the necessitated, because from the obligation of truthfulness follows the impossibility of lying, as is not hidden. His statement: 'and if not, they would not be... etc.' means: if it were not obligatory for them [to be truthful] and impossible for them [to lie], they would not be... etc. The explanation of that is that Allah the Exalted has informed of their truthfulness by creating miracles at their hands, and it is necessary that His report be in accordance with His knowledge, and He is Knower of all things, so from that follows the obligation of truthfulness for them and the impossibility of lying upon them. His statement: 'the Knower of hidden things' is an indication to explain the connection in his statement: 'and if not, they would not be... etc.' as previously mentioned. And the hidden things are the obscure and problematic matters. And it is not hidden that if He is Knower of the hidden things, He is Knower of the apparent things a fortiori. And the division of things into hidden and apparent is only relative to us; but as for Him, all things are apparent equally.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a rigorous rational proof for the necessary truthfulness and impossibility of lying for prophets. The author begins by noting that from belief in the messenger, we derive the obligation of his truthfulness. The author explicitly states the obligation of truthfulness and impossibility of lying, and alludes to the impossibility of betrayal and concealment. The logical structure is outlined: from the impossibility of betrayal comes the obligation of trustworthiness, and from the impossibility of concealment comes the obligation of delivery. Then the author explains the reasoning behind the impossibility of lying: God creates miracles at the hands of prophets to confirm their truthfulness. Since God's report must correspond to His knowledge, and He knows all things, it follows necessarily that the prophets are truthful and cannot lie. The author also comments on the phrase 'Knower of hidden things,' explaining that this attribute reinforces the argument: God knows even hidden matters, so He certainly knows apparent ones. The division into hidden and apparent is only from our perspective; for God everything is equally evident. This argument grounds the obligatory prophetic attributes in divine action and omniscience.

استحالة الكذب
المعجزة
العالم بالخفيات
الملازمة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophetic truthfulness is based on their inherent moral character.
Correction: The passage shows it is a logical necessity based on divine confirmation via miracles and God's omniscience.

D) The rational impossibility of a prophet lying

Key Takeaway
Prophets are necessarily truthful and incapable of lying because God confirms them with miracles, and His confirmation must accord with His perfect knowledge.

Impossibility of Betrayal and Concealment: Deriving Trustworthiness and Delivery
Al-Bajuri explains the concise method of indicating two impossible and two obligatory prophetic attributes through one phrase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a single phrase in Sanusi's creed concisely implies both impossible and obligatory prophetic attributes, and the reasoning behind this concise formulation.

Core Idea
One short phrase can imply two impossible and two obligatory prophetic attributes through logical entailment.

In this passage, Al-Bajuri explains the elegant conciseness of Sanusi's wording when stating the attributes of prophets. Instead of listing each attribute separately, Sanusi uses a single phrase that covers two impossible attributes and, by logical implication, their obligatory opposites. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows how it reflects the pedagogical style of kalam works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical connectors like 'ويلزم من'.
2
Identify the two impossible attributes
The passage explicitly names betrayal (الخيانة) and concealment (الكتمان) as covered by 'all prohibitions'. Circle them in the text.
3
Derive the obligatory opposites
From the impossibility of betrayal, the obligation of trustworthiness (الأمانة) follows. From the impossibility of concealment, the obligation of delivery (التبليغ) follows. Trace this logical entailment.
This is a key principle in kalam: impossibilities imply their obligatory opposites.
4
Understand the author's rationale
Al-Bajuri notes that Sanusi explicitly mentioned truthfulness and lying earlier because the core mission of prophets is reporting from Allah. The other attributes are derived concisely.
This shows the focus on conveying divine messages.
5
Appreciate conciseness
Compare stating all four attributes separately versus using one phrase. Al-Bajuri highlights that the single phrase is more concise (أخصر).
This reflects the kalam tradition's value of brevity without losing meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْل الْمَنْهِيَّات كُلَّهَا أي: الشاملة للخيانة والكتمان، ويلزم من استحالة الخيانة: وجوب الأمانة، ومن استحالة الكتمان: وجوب التبليغ، وقد صَرَّحَ قبلُ بوجوب الصدق واستحالة الكذب عليهم، ولعل المصنف إنما فَعَلَ ذلك؛ لأن مدار الرسالة على الإخبار عن الله تعالى، فاحتاج إلى ذِكْرِ ما يتعلق بالخبر، وهو الصدق والكذبُ بالمطابقة بخلاف غيرهما، وأيضاً اللفظ الذي ذكره يَدُلُّ على مستحيلين، وهما الخيانة والكتمان، وعلى واجبين، وهما الأمانة والتبليغ، فكان أخصر من ذِكْرِ الواجبين ثم المستحيلين.
His statement: 'and the impossibility of committing all the prohibitions' i.e., which includes betrayal and concealment. And from the impossibility of betrayal follows the obligation of trustworthiness, and from the impossibility of concealment follows the obligation of delivery. And he explicitly mentioned before the obligation of truthfulness and the impossibility of lying upon them. Perhaps the author only did that because the basis of the message is reporting about Allah the Exalted, so he needed to mention what pertains to the report, which is truthfulness and lying by correspondence, unlike other than them. And also, the wording he mentioned indicates two impossibilities, namely betrayal and concealment, and two obligations, namely trustworthiness and delivery. Thus it was more concise than mentioning the two obligations then the two impossibilities.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage justifies the author's (Sanusi's) concise method in stating the attributes of prophets. Rather than listing separately the obligatory attributes of trustworthiness and delivery and the impossible attributes of betrayal and concealment, he simply says 'impossibility of committing all prohibitions'. This covers both impossible attributes (betrayal and concealment) and by implication their obligatory opposites (trustworthiness and delivery). The author of the commentary (Al-Bajuri) explains that the primary focus of prophethood is conveying reports from God, hence the explicit mention of truthfulness and lying since they directly relate to reporting. The other attributes are derived from the same phrase, making the text more concise. This demonstrates a pedagogical efficiency in kalam works.

Key Terms
الخيانة
الكتمان
الأمانة
التبليغ
المنهيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Trustworthiness and delivery are not explicitly stated and therefore less important or not obligatory.
Correction: The passage shows they are logically entailed from the impossibility of betrayal and concealment, thus equally obligatory.

Checkpoint

B) Betrayal and concealment
C) Error and forgetfulness
D) Sin and disobedience

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'impossibility of committing all prohibitions' succinctly implies both betrayal and concealment (impossible) and their opposites trustworthiness and delivery (obligatory).

The author prioritized truthfulness because the message is about reporting Allah. How seriously do you take reporting truthfully about Allah's religion? Impossibility of Betrayal and Concealment for Prophets
Al-Bajuri glosses Sanusi's phrase on impossibility of forbidden acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the impossibility of betrayal and concealment logically entails the obligations of trustworthiness and delivery for prophets, and why Sanusi used concise wording.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot betray or conceal; thus they must be trustworthy and deliver the message.

Al-Bajuri unpacks a dense phrase from Sanusi's creed. He shows that the impossibility of certain acts directly implies opposite obligations. This passage reveals a logical economy in theological exposition: one statement carries multiple doctrinal conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms khiyāna (betrayal) and kitmān (concealment).
2
Identify the two pairs
Find the two impossible acts (betrayal, concealment) and the two obligatory acts (trustworthiness, delivery). Note how each impossibility implies an obligation.
The passage states: 'from the impossibility of betrayal follows the obligation of trustworthiness' and similarly for concealment.
3
Understand the author's reasoning
Al-Bajuri explains why Sanusi focused on truthfulness and lying earlier, and now only mentions these two pairs. The reason is that prophethood is about conveying news from God.
He says 'the basis of the message is informing about God'.
4
Reflect on conciseness
Notice that Sanusi's wording implies both impossibilities and obligations simultaneously, making the text more concise than listing each separately.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْل الْمَنْهِيَّات كُلَّهَا أي: الشاملة للخيانة والكتمان، ويلزم من استحالة الخيانة: وجوب الأمانة، ومن استحالة الكتمان: وجوب التبليغ، وقد صَرَّحَ قبلُ بوجوب الصدق واستحالة الكذب عليهم، ولعل المصنف إنما فَعَلَ ذلك؛ لأن مدار الرسالة على الإخبار عن الله تعالى، فاحتاج إلى ذِكْرِ ما يتعلق بالخبر، وهو الصدق والكذبُ بالمطابقة بخلاف غيرهما، وأيضاً اللفظ الذي ذكره يَدُلُّ على مستحيلين، وهما الخيانة والكتمان، وعلى واجبين، وهما الأمانة والتبليغ، فكان أخصر من ذِكْرِ الواجبين ثم المستحيلين.
His saying: "And the impossibility of committing all forbidden acts" means: including betrayal and concealment. And from the impossibility of betrayal follows the obligation of trustworthiness, and from the impossibility of concealment follows the obligation of delivery. And he has previously stated the obligation of truthfulness and the impossibility of lying upon them. Perhaps the author only did this because the basis of the message (al-risāla) is informing about God, so he needed to mention what pertains to the report (al-khabar), namely truthfulness and lying by direct correspondence, unlike others. Also, the wording he mentioned indicates two impossible things, namely betrayal and concealment, and two obligatory things, namely trustworthiness and delivery, and this was more concise than mentioning the two obligations then the two impossibilities.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a gloss on Sanusi's statement "and the impossibility of committing all forbidden acts". Al-Bajuri first specifies that "all forbidden acts" includes betrayal (khiyāna) and concealment (kitmān). He then notes the logical implications: from the impossibility of betrayal comes the obligation of trustworthiness (amāna), and from the impossibility of concealment comes the obligation of delivery (tablīgh). He reminds that Sanusi has already separately stated the obligation of truthfulness and impossibility of lying. Al-Bajuri offers a reason why Sanusi structured it this way: since the core of prophethood is conveying news about God, he focused on matters directly related to the report (al-khabar), i.e., truthfulness and lying by direct correspondence (bi-l-mutābaqa). Additionally, the wording concisely implies both impossibilities and obligations simultaneously.

Key Terms
الخيانة (al-khiyāna)
الكتمان (al-kitmān)
الأمانة (al-amāna)
التبليغ (al-tablīgh)
الصدق (al-ṣidq)
الكذب (al-kadhib)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Sanusi forgot to mention other necessary attributes of prophets.
Correction: Al-Bajuri explains that Sanusi's wording is deliberately concise and covers both the impossibilities and obligations, focusing on those most relevant to prophethood as communication of divine news.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between the impossibility of betrayal and trustworthiness according to this passage?
A) They are unrelated.
B) Trustworthiness is impossible.
C) From the impossibility of betrayal follows the obligation of trustworthiness.
D) Betrayal is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of an act like betrayal logically necessitates the obligation of its opposite (trustworthiness), and Sanusi's concise wording efficiently conveys multiple doctrinal points.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe prophets were absolutely trustworthy. But what about you? Where in your life are you betraying a trust—from God, from others, or even from yourself? Will you repent and become trustworthy today?
?
The prophets delivered the message without concealing any part. Are you delivering the truth you know, or are you hiding it out of fear or convenience? What truth have you been silent about that you need to speak?
?
If impossibility of betrayal entails obligation of trustworthiness for prophets, what does your own betrayal of small trusts say about your obligation before God? When will you stop rationalizing and start being fully trustworthy?

Prophets' Words, Actions, and Silence as Proofs
Al-Bajuri explains how prophets' words, actions, and silence serve as proofs, with conditions for silence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophet's words, actions, and silence serve as proofs in Islamic theology, including the conditions under which silence indicates approval.

Core Idea
The Prophet's silence is a proof—but only when there is no clear opposition or abrogation.

This passage from Al-Bajuri's commentary explains the three types of prophetic evidence: words, deeds, and silence. Al-Bajuri provides concrete examples and clarifies an important exception: silence does not always mean approval, especially if the speaker is a disbeliever. This lesson unpacks these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Al-Bajuri gives specific examples from the Prophet's life.
2
Identify the three proofs
The passage presents three proofs: words, actions, and silence. Find each one and see how they are exemplified.
3
Understand the silence condition
Al-Bajuri explains that silence is a proof only when certain conditions are met. Identify the exception he mentions.
The exception involves a disbeliever and the impossibility of abrogation.
4
Reflect on the priority note
The passage ends with a note on 'min bab awla' (by priority). Consider what this means for our understanding of God's perspective.
This reminds us that priority is based on human reasoning, not divine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: بِأَقْوَالِهِمْ) أي: كقوله: «إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ». (وقوله: وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ) أي: كتوضُته وغُسْلِه. (وقوله: وَسُكُوتِهِمْ) أي: كسكوته عن ابن عمر لما قال بحضرته: أُحِلَّتْ لنا مَيْتان ودَمَان: السمك والجرادُ والكَبِدُ والطُّحَالُ، فأقرَّهُ، وهو لا يُقِرُّ على خطأ؛ وإن صَدَرَ من غيرِ مُكلَّف؛ لأن السكوت عليه ـ وإن لم يَأْتُمْ به يُوهِمُ من جَهِلَ حُكْمَ ذلك جوازَهُ. نعم؛ إن كان من صَدَرَ عنه ذلك كافراً عُلِمَتْ معاندته له، والحالُ لا يحتمل النسخ؛ لم يدلُّ سكوته على جوازه. (قوله: مِنْ بَاب أَوْلَى أي بحسب عقولنا، وإلا؛ فالأمور مستوية عنده تعالى كما يعلم من آخر كلامه.
His saying: "By their words" i.e., like his statement: "Actions are but by intentions." And his saying: "and by their actions" i.e., like his ablution and his washing. And his saying: "and by their silence" i.e., like his silence towards Ibn Umar when he said in his presence: "Permitted for us are two dead animals and two bloods: fish and locusts, and liver and spleen." So he approved it, and he does not approve of error. And if it comes from someone not legally responsible (ghayr mukallaf), because remaining silent about it—even if he does not sin [from it]—gives the impression to one who is ignorant of its ruling that it is permissible. Yes, if the one from whom that emanated is a disbeliever, then his opposition is known, and the situation does not admit abrogation, his silence does not indicate its permissibility. His saying: "By priority" (min bab awla) i.e., according to our intellects; otherwise, things are equal in His sight, as is known from the end of his speech.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory gloss on Sanusi's statement that the actions of prophets (words, deeds, silence) are proofs. Al-Bajuri provides examples: the Prophet's words like the hadith on intentions, his actions like ablution, and his silence approving Ibn Umar's statement about the permissibility of certain animals. He clarifies that the Prophet does not approve of error, but silence itself may be taken as approval unless there is context. He adds a condition: if the statement comes from a non-mukallaf (someone not legally responsible), silence might mislead. However, if the person is a known disbeliever, silence does not imply approval because his opposition is clear. Finally, the note on "min bab awla" reminds that priority is according to our reasoning; in God's sight, all matters are equal.

Key Terms
السكوت (al-sukūt)
الإقرار (al-iqrār)
المكلف (al-mukallaf)
باب أولى (bāb awlā)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Prophet's silence always indicates approval of whatever was said or done.
Correction: Al-Bajuri clarifies that silence does not indicate approval if the speaker is a disbeliever and the situation does not admit abrogation, because his opposition to the truth is known.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when does the Prophet's silence not indicate permissibility?
A) When the speaker is a Muslim.
B) When the speaker is a disbeliever and the situation does not allow abrogation.
C) When the silence is long.
D) When the action is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's silence is a proof, but its indication of permissibility is conditional on the absence of known opposition and the possibility of abrogation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a moment when you remained silent while witnessing something wrong. In light of this lesson, does your silence reflect approval, indifference, or fear? How will you change your silence to align with the Prophet's example?
?
The Prophet's silence was a proof because he never approved of error. Now consider your own silence: when you stay quiet about a truth you know, are you approving of error? What truth are you avoiding speaking today?
?
This lesson shows that even the Prophet's silence had conditions. What conditions must your silence meet to be a proof of your faith rather than a proof of your negligence? Commit to one situation this week where you will break your silence.

Proof of Prophetic Infallibility from God's Command
Al-Bajuri presents a reductio proof for prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational necessity why prophets must be free from anything that contradicts God's command.

Core Idea
Sending a prophet who disobeys would make God command disobedience.

Al-Bajuri unpacks a profound argument for the infallibility of prophets. The reasoning is simple yet powerful: if a prophet contradicted God's command, God would be commanding us to follow that contradiction. Since God only commands obedience, this cannot happen. Let's walk through the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its structure. Notice the conditional 'if... then...' and the concluding 'otherwise' clause.
The passage is a gloss on Sanusi's original text.
2
Understand the premise
Identify the hidden premise: God only commands obedience. This is the bedrock of the argument.
3
Trace the reductio ad absurdum
Follow the logical chain: if a prophet opposed God's command, and God sent him anyway, then God would be commanding people to imitate that opposition. That contradicts God's nature.
This is a classical kalam proof by contradiction.
4
Check your understanding
Take the checkpoint quiz to confirm you grasp the core premise and conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ... إلخ) أي: لأنه لو عَلِمَ الله تعالى أن يكون فيها مخالَفَةٌ لأمره تعالى لما أرسلهم ليُعْلِمُوا الخلق بأقوالهم وأفعالهم وسكوتهم، وإلا؛ لكان الله تعالى آمِراً بالاقتداء بهم في تلك المخالفة، وهو باطل؛ لأنه تعالى لا يأمرُ إلا بالطاعة.
His saying: "Then it necessarily follows that they would not be..." etc., i.e., because if God knew that there would be in them opposition to His command, He would not have sent them to inform the creation by their words, actions, and silence. Otherwise, God would be commanding imitation of them in that opposition, and this is false because He commands only obedience.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a gloss on Sanusi's argument that prophets must be free from all that contradicts their message. Al-Bajuri explains the logical implication: if God knew that a prophet would act contrary to His command, He would not send him as a model to be followed through words, actions, and silence. Because if God sent him despite knowing he would oppose His command, then God would be implicitly commanding people to imitate the prophet in that opposition, which is impossible because God only commands obedience. This is a rational proof for the infallibility of prophets in conveying and acting.

Key Terms
المخالفة (al-mukhālafa)
الاقتداء (al-iqtidā')
الطاعة (al-ṭā'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof assumes prophets are sinless by nature, not by divine choice.
Correction: The proof does not rely on nature; it is a logical necessity based on God's purpose in sending prophets.

Checkpoint
What is the premise of the proof that prophets cannot oppose God's command?
A) God only commands obedience.
B) Prophets are infallible by nature.
C) Silence indicates approval.
D) The Prophet never sinned.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be free from opposing God's command because otherwise God would be commanding disobedience, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you honestly point to an area in your life where you follow a cultural practice that you know, deep down, contradicts what God has commanded? This lesson shows that God never commands disobedience—so what is your excuse for not aligning that practice with the prophetic example?
?
If you were to stand before God today and He asked you, 'Why did you imitate so-and-so in an act that clearly opposed My command?' would you have any defense? This argument strips away every justification except ignorance or arrogance. Which will you choose to address?
?
The prophets are infallible, but you are not. Yet this lesson forces you to see that every act of yours that contradicts God's command is a silent endorsement of opposition to Him. What specific habit will you commit to changing this week to align your actions with the obedience God alone commands?
