Why Bodily Ailments Are Permissible for Prophets
Al-Bajuri derives that bodily ailments are permissible for prophets as they do not detract from their message.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational criterion for what is permissible or impossible for prophets, and why bodily ailments do not conflict with their prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophets are only immune from things that harm their message, not from ordinary human ailments.

In this passage, al-Bajuri derives an important principle from Sanusi's earlier statement: not everything that seems undignified is forbidden for prophets. Only those things that detract from the rank of prophethood are impossible. This helps us understand the boundaries of prophetic immunity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the key terms: جواز الأعراض (jawāz al-a‘rāḍ) and القدح (al-qudḥ).
2
Identify the inference
Al-Bajuri says 'it is taken from it' (يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ) that ailments are permissible. Identify the source of this inference from the previous context.
The inference is based on the fact that prophets are established for prophethood, not divinity or kingship.
3
Understand the criterion
The passage states that nothing is impossible for prophets except what detracts from the rank of prophethood (مرتبة الرسالة). This is the key principle.
Ask yourself: why does this principle allow bodily ailments?
4
Reflect on the implication
Bodily ailments do not detract from the message, so they are permissible (جائز). Reflect on other examples of permissible human imperfections in prophets.
This guards against the misconception that prophets must be free from all human weaknesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قوله: وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: جَوَازُ الْأَعْرَاضِ... إلخ) أي: لأنه إنما أُثْبِتَ له الرسالة لا الألوهية ولا الملكية، وكذلك إخوانه المرسلون، وحينئذ فلا يمتنع في حقهم إلا ما يَقْدَحُ في مرتبة الرسالة، وتلك الأعراضُ لا تَقْدَحُ فيها كما أشار لذلك بقوله: (إذ ذاك لا يقدح في رسالتهم)، أي: وكلُّ ما لا يقدح فيها فهو جائز.
His saying: "And it is taken from it: the permissibility of ailments (al-a‘rāḍ)..." etc., i.e., because he was established for prophethood (al-risāla), not divinity (al-ulūhiyya) nor kingship (al-mulkiyya), and likewise his brothers the messengers. And so nothing is impossible for them except what detracts from the rank of prophethood, and those ailments do not detract from it, as he indicated by his saying: "For that does not detract from their message." That is, everything that does not detract from it is permissible.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage explains the inference from the previous context that bodily ailments (a‘rāḍ, such as sickness) are permissible for prophets. The reasoning: prophets are sent for the rank of prophethood, not divinity or kingship. Therefore, only things that conflict with the rank of prophethood are impossible for them. Bodily ailments like illness, poverty, etc., do not conflict with conveying the message, so they are permissible. This is based on Sanusi's statement "for that does not detract from their message".

Key Terms
جواز الأعراض (jawāz al-a‘rāḍ)
الرسالة (al-risāla)
القدح (al-qudḥ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets must be free from all human imperfections, including bodily ailments.
Correction: Prophets are only protected from things that detract from their message; bodily ailments do not detract, so they are permissible.

Checkpoint
What is the criterion for something being impossible for prophets according to al-Bajuri?
A) Anything that contradicts divine attributes.
B) Anything that detracts from the rank of prophethood.
C) All human ailments.
D) Anything that causes pain.

Key Takeaway
Bodily ailments are permissible for prophets because they do not detract from their essential role of conveying the message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a chronic illness or hardship, do you ever feel that your worth in Allah's sight diminishes? Reflect on this lesson: if bodily ailments did not lower the rank of prophets, how can you trust that your own trials do not reflect a loss of divine favor? What would it mean for you to truly internalize that worth is tied to your message, not your physical state?
?
Do you sometimes look at a righteous person suffering affliction and secretly doubt their piety or Allah's love for them? This lesson teaches that physical trials are not signs of displeasure. How can you actively combat this assumption in your heart the next time you see a believer in hardship? What specific thought from this lesson will you recall?

Deriving the Permissibility of Human Attributes for Prophets
Al-Bajuri explains derivation of permissibility of human attributes for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human attributes like marriage and sickness are permissible for prophets and how they can actually increase their rank.

Core Idea
Only what detracts from prophethood is prohibited; human attributes do not.

Al-Bajuri explains a key principle: prophets are not divine beings but messengers. This means only things that compromise their message are forbidden. Hunger, sickness, marriage are not flaws; they can even be opportunities for greater reward or legislation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation to get the flow of Al-Bajuri's commentary.
Notice the ellipses and parentheses—these are characteristic of glosses.
2
Identify the main argument
Find the core reasoning: prophets are established as having the message, not divinity, so only what detracts from messengership is prohibited. Human attributes do not detract, so they are permissible.
3
Understand 'does not detract'
Al-Bajuri clarifies that 'does not detract' means it does not disparage or decrease their rank. This reinforces that such attributes are not flaws.
Check the alternative reading in some copies: 'because that does not detract'.
4
Explore the increase in rank and reward dispute
Read how with proper intention (legislation, strengthening worship, patience), these attributes can increase rank. Then consider the disagreement on whether reward is for the calamity itself or for patience.
This part is an additional nuance showing that not only are these attributes permissible, but they can be spiritually beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ: جَوَازُ الْأَعْرَاضِ... إلخ) أَي: لأَنَّهُ إِنَّمَا أُثْبِتَ لَهُ الرِّسَالَةُ لَا الْأُلُوهِيَّةُ وَلَا الْمَلَكِيَّةُ، وَكَذَلِكَ إِخْوَانُهُ الْمُرْسَلُونَ، وَحِينَئِذٍ فَلَا يَمْتَنِعُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ إِلَّا مَا يَقْدَحُ فِي مَرْتَبَةِ الرِّسَالَةِ، وَتِلْكَ الْأَعْرَاضُ لَا تَقْدَحُ فِيهَا كمَا أَشَارَ لِذَلِكَ بِقَوْلِهِ: (إِذْ ذَاكَ لَا يَقْدَحُ فِي رِسَالَتِهِمْ)، أَيْ: وَكُلُّ مَا لَا يَقْدَحُ فِيهَا فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ.
(قوله: إِذْ ذَاكَ لَا يَقْدَحُ... إلخ) تَعْلِيلٌ لِجَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ، وَفِي بَعْضِ النُّسَخِ: (لأَنَّ ذَلِكَ لَا يَقْدَحُ، وَمَعْنَى: لَا يَقْدَحُ لَا يَطْعَنُ وَلَا يُنْقِصُ.)
(قوله: بَلْ ذَاكَ مِمَّا يَزِيدُ... إلخ) أَيْ: لأَنَّهُ إِمَّا أَنْ يُقَارِنَهُ قَصْدُ التَّشْرِيعِ كَمَا فِي النِّكَاحِ، أَوْ قَصْدُ التَّقَوِّي عَلَى الْعِبَادَةِ كَمَا فِي الْأَصْلِ، أَوْ طَاعَةُ الصَّبْرِ كَمَا فِي الْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ. وَاخْتُلِفَ هَلِ الثَّوَابُ عَلَى الْمَصَائِبِ أَوْ عَلَى الصَّبْرِ عَلَيْهَا؟ فَذَهَبَ الْعِزُّ بْنُ عَبْدِ السَّلَامِ فِي طَائِفَةٍ إِلَى الثَّانِي؛ لأَنَّ الثَّوَابَ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ عَلَى صُنْعِ الْعَبْدِ، وَالْمَصَائِبُ لَا صُنْعَ لَهُ فِيهَا. وَذَهَبَ الْجُمْهُورُ إِلَى الْأَوَّلِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: {ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُمْ لَا يُصِيبُهُمْ ظَمَأٌ وَلَا نَصَبٌ وَلَا مَخْمَصَةٌ إِلَى أَنْ قَالَ: إِلَّا كُتِبَ لَهُمْ بِهِ عَمَلٌ صَالِحٌ} وَلِخَبَرِ مُسْلِمٍ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ مَرْفُوعًا: «مَا مِنْ مُسْلِمٍ يُشَاكُ بِشَوْكَةٍ فَمَا فَوْقَهَا إِلَّا كُتِبَ لَهُ بِهَا دَرَجَةٌ، وَمُحِيَتْ عَنْهُ بِهَا خَطِيئَةٌ».
And it is taken from this: the permissibility of (human) attributes… etc., i.e., because he is established as having the message, not divinity nor sovereignty, and likewise his brother messengers. And then nothing is prevented in their right except what detracts from the station of messengership, and those attributes do not detract from it, as he pointed to that by his saying: 'Then that does not detract from their messengership,' i.e., everything that does not detract from it is permissible. (His saying: 'Then that does not detract… etc.') is an explanation for the permissibility of human attributes, and in some copies: 'Because that does not detract, and the meaning of does not detract is it does not disparage nor decrease.' (His saying: 'Rather that is from that which increases… etc.') i.e., because it is either accompanied by the intention of legislation as in marriage, or the intention of strengthening for worship as in the original, or the obedience of patience as in sickness and the like. And there is disagreement: is the reward for the calamities or for patience over them? Al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam and a group went to the second, because reward is only for the action of the servant, and the calamities have no action of his in them. And the majority went to the first due to His saying: 'That is because they are not afflicted with thirst nor fatigue nor hunger… until His saying: except that it is written for them thereby a righteous deed' and due to the hadith of Muslim from Aisha raised: 'No Muslim is pricked by a thorn or more than that except that a degree is written for him thereby and a sin is erased from him thereby.'
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a set of glosses explaining the derivation of the permissibility of human attributes (like hunger, sickness, marriage) for prophets. The first part argues that from the fact that prophets are established as having the message (risāla) and not divinity or sovereignty, it follows that only things that detract from messengership are prohibited. Human attributes do not detract, so they are permissible. The second part clarifies that 'does not detract' means it does not disparage or decrease their rank. The third part explains that rather than detracting, such attributes can actually increase the prophets' rank, depending on the accompanying intention: for legislation (e.g., marriage to teach rulings), for strengthening worship (e.g., eating for energy), or for practicing patience (e.g., illness). The passage then notes a scholarly dispute: is the reward for the calamity itself or for patience over it? Al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam holds the latter because reward is for the servant's action, but calamities are not his action. The majority holds the former, citing the Quranic verse that hardship is recorded as a righteous deed and the hadith that a thorn prick erases sins and raises degrees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That permissibility of human attributes implies prophets are imperfect or flawed.
Correction: Rather, it emphasizes their humanity and such attributes can increase their rank when accompanied by proper intention.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why are human attributes like marriage or sickness permissible for prophets?
A) Because prophets are not required to be free of all human attributes.
B) Because such attributes do not detract from the station of messengership.
C) Because prophets are human and thus all human attributes are obligatory.
D) Because such attributes increase their rank by default.

Key Takeaway
Human attributes like marriage and sickness are permissible for prophets because they do not detract from their message and can even increase their rank when accompanied by proper intention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson shows that human attributes like illness can increase a prophet's rank when accompanied by patience. When you face a trial, do you view it as an opportunity to rise in Allah's sight, or as a mere obstacle? What would need to change in your heart for you to welcome difficulties as a means of drawing closer to Him?
?
The prophets' human attributes are permissible because they do not detract from their message. Consider your own daily habits—eating, sleeping, socializing. Do these activities enhance your role as a believer, or do they sometimes distract you from your purpose? How can you transform them into acts of worship with a simple shift in intention?
?
If the permissibility of human attributes for prophets is based on their not detracting from their special rank, what does that mean for you? Your actions as a Muslim—even permissible ones—can either elevate or diminish your spiritual station. Are you mindful of how your everyday choices affect your relationship with Allah? What is one change you can make today to ensure your common activities are aligned with your faith?
